成为技术领导者的评论

Reviews of Becoming a Technical Leader

“……对于身为领导者、想成为领导者或认为只有头衔中带有‘领导者’或‘经理’的人才是领导者的人来说，这是一本极好的书。” ——Elisabeth Hendrickson，Quality Tree Consulting

“… an excellent book for anyone who is a leader, who wants to be a leader, or who thinks only people with ‘leader’ or ‘manager’ in their title are leaders.” —Elisabeth Hendrickson, Quality Tree Consulting

“……开发个人领导潜能的指南，但远不止于此。. . 它充满了关于作为专业人士的个人成长的有用见解。” —系统管理杂志

“… a guide to developing personal leadership potential, but it is much more than that . . . it is filled with useful insights into personal growth as a professional.” —Journal of Systems Management

“……总是很迷人。. . 将我们的注意力集中在如何让有思想的技术人员团队有效地合作。” —IEEE计算机

“… always fascinating . . . focuses our attention on what it takes to make teams of thinking technical people work effectively together.” —IEEE Computer

“关于从技术明星到解决问题领导者的转变的 24 个理由充分、发人深省的章节。. . 非常实用和脚踏实地。. . ” -因果

“twenty-four well-reasoned, thought-provoking chapters on making the change from technical star to problem-solving leader . . . extremely practical and down-to-earth. . . .” —CAUSE/Effect

“这本书比任何其他关于这个主题的书都更能引起我的共鸣。Weinberg 迫使你参与探索如何创建技术领导者，他提供了如何实现这一目标的真实步骤。——Lisa Simone

“This book resonates in me more than any other book on the subject. Weinberg forces you to participate in the exploration of how a technical leader is created, and he provides real steps on how to get there.—Lisa Simone

“一本改变人生的书。我所知道的关于成为经理或主管的最好的人。……有关权力和领导力的重要资源；解决问题和创新；愿景和激励他人；领导风格；等等。”——一位亚马逊客户

“A life-changing book. The best one I know about becoming a manager or supervisor. …A great resource on power and leadership; problem solving and innovation; vision and motivating others; leadership styles; and much more.”—an Amazon Customer

“我从这本书中得到的比我读过的任何其他书都多。它非常适合认为自己可能对领导力感兴趣的当前软件开发人员。”— Philip R. Heath

“I have gotten more out of this book than any other that I have read. It is ideal for current software developers who think they might be interested in leadership.”— Philip R. Heath

“无论您的头衔中是否有领导者，这本书都将帮助您成为问题解决者以及其他人寻求建议和领导力的人。- Mark Plesko，Logan's Rings

“Whether or not you have Leader in your title this book will help you become a problem solver and someone that others look to for advice and leadership.— Mark Plesko, Logan’s Rings

前言

Preface

当 Banzan 穿过一个市场时，他无意中听到了一位屠夫和他的顾客之间的谈话。“给我最好的一块肉，”顾客说。

When Banzan was walking through a market he overheard a conversation between a butcher and his customer. “Give me the best piece of meat you have,” said the customer.

“我店里的东西都是最好的，”屠夫回答道。“你在这里找不到任何不是最好的肉。”

“Everything in my shop is the best,” replied the butcher. “You cannot find here any piece of meat that is not the best.”

听到这些话，班赞开悟了。

At these words Banzan became enlightened.

——Paul Reps，“一切都是最好的”，来自Zen Flesh、Zen Bones

—Paul Reps, “Everything Is Best” from Zen Flesh, Zen Bones

这是一本关于启蒙的书，既是我的也是你的。我的还不完整，但到目前为止，花的时间比在市场上走一圈还长。例如，这本书至少已经制作了 15 年。

This is a book about enlightenment, both mine and yours. Mine is still incomplete, but so far has taken rather longer than a walk through the market. This book, for instance, has been at least fifteen years in the making.

它始于 1970 年左右，当时 Don Gause、Dani Weinberg（我的妻子）和我在瑞士度过了一个夏天。唐和我正在写一本关于解决问题的书（你的灯亮着吗？或如何弄清楚问题到底是什么），而丹妮则继续她对瑞士农民社区的人类学研究。多年来，唐和我一直在研究成功和不成功的问题解决方案，尤其是计算项目。达尼一直在研究将新技术引入农民社区的方式。

It started around 1970, when Don Gause, Dani Weinberg (my wife), and I spent a summer in Switzerland. Don and I were writing a book on problem solving (Are Your Lights On? or How to Figure Out What the Problem Really Is), and Dani was continuing her anthropological research on Swiss peasant communities. Over the years, Don and I had been studying successful and unsuccessful problem-solving efforts, particularly computing projects. Dani had been studying the ways in which new technology had been introduced into peasant communities.

比较死记硬背，我们梦想有一个能够最大限度地利用新技术系统成功引入的研讨会当我们比较成功和不成功的系统时，我们很快意识到，几乎所有的成功都取决于少数优秀技术人员的表现工作人员。其中一些是创新技术思想的源泉，一些是其他人思想的诠释者。有的是发明家，有的是谈判者，有的是老师，有的是团队领导。他们与不太成功的同事的不同之处在于罕见地结合了技术专长和领导技能。今天，我们会说他们的创新能力很强，但也有足够的激励和组织能力来使想法有效。

Comparing rotes, we dreamed of a workshop that would have the maximum possible leverage on the successful introduction of new technical system When we compared successful and unsuccessful systems, wequickly realized that almost all of the successes hinged on the performance of a small number of outstanding technical workers. Some of them were consistent sources of innovative technical ideas, some were interpreters of other people’s ideas. Some were inventors, some were negotiators, some were teachers, some were team leaders. What distinguished them from their less successful colleagues was a rare combination of technical expertise and leadership skills. Today, we would say that they were high in innovation, but with sufficient motivational and organizational skills to use in making ideas effective.

这些领导者既不是工程学院和科学学院培养出来的纯技术人员，也不是管理学院培养出来的传统领导者。他们是不同的品种，是杂交种。他们的共同点是对创意质量的关注。就像屠夫一样，他们希望店里的一切都是最好的。我们称他们为技术领导者。

These leaders were not the pure technicians produced by the engineering and science schools, nor were they the conventional leaders trained in the schools of management. They were a different breed, a hybrid. What they shared was a concern for the quality of ideas. Like the butcher, they wanted everything in their shop to be the best. We called them technical leaders.

Don、Dani 和我设计了一个新的领导力研讨会，名为“计算机编程中的技术领导力”，这是应 Dennis Davie 的邀请首次在澳大利亚举办的。十五名参与者中有十四名将其评为“我有过的最深刻的教育经历”。另一个人说这只是“我有过的最深刻的教育经历之一”。我们意识到我们已经找到了我们的筹码。

Don, Dani, and I designed a new leadership workshop, called “Technical Leadership in Computer Programming,” which was first given in Australia at the invitation of Dennis Davie. Fourteen out of fifteen participants rated it “the most profound educational experience I’ve ever had.” The other one said it was merely “one of the most profound educational experiences I’ve ever had.” We realized we had found our leverage.

在接下来的几年里，Daniel Freedman 和其他一些人加入了我们的团队，研讨会举办给了全世界数百名未来的技术领导者。一些电气和机械工程师和一些培训师溜进来了。除了一些技术资料外，这些新人发现一切都直接适用于他们的工作。因此，我们逐渐放弃了技术材料并扩大了受众范围。我们还拓宽了我们对可能性的看法。一方面，我们发现这种技术领导风格适用于许多与技术无关的问题。我们开始听到车间毕业生的故事，他们将其应用于技术工作以外的情况。

In the years that followed, Daniel Freedman and a few others joined our team, and the workshop was given to hundreds of would-be technical leaders all over the world. A few electrical and mechanical engineers slipped in, as did some trainers. Except for some technical material, these newcomers found everything directly applicable to their work. As a result, we gradually dropped technical material and broadened our audience. We also broadened our vision of what was possible. For one thing, we discovered that this technical leadership style was applicable to many problems that have nothing to do with technology. We began hear stories from workshop graduates who had applied it to situations other than those arising from their technical work.

这些人已经从普通的技术主管转变为解决问题的领导者，有能力让事情发生。他们中的许多人不了解自己的转变。好像有一天他们是主管，第二天他们是领导者，就像市场上的班赞一样。但是，如果领导力只能通过突然的、神秘的启蒙获得，一个人怎么能学会成为技术领导者呢？

These people had transformed themselves from ordinary technical supervisors into problem-solving leaders with the power to make things happen. Many of them didn’t understand their own transformation. It seemed as if one day they were supervisors and the next they were leaders, like Banzan in the marketplace. But if leadership were only attained through, a sudden, mystical enlightenment, how could one learn to become a technical leader?

多年来，我们从研讨会中学到的最大教训是，成为领导者不是发生在你身上的事情，而是你所做的事情。通常在车间里，有人似乎突然开悟了，但我们对此没有任何关系，就像屠夫与完成 Banzan 终生皈依的那一刻无关一样。我们的研讨会不教人们成为领导者；它们只是促进每个人独特的自我发展体验过程。本书采用相同的方法：将其视为您的个人领导力研讨会。

Over the years, the biggest lesson we have learned from our workshops is that becoming a leader is not something that happens to you, but something that you do. Often in a workshop, someone seems to attain a sudden enlightenment, but we have no more to do with that than the butcher had to do with the moment that completed Banzan’s lifelong conversion. Our workshops do not teach people to become leaders; they merely give a boost to each person’s unique experiential process of self-development. This book takes the same approach: Consider it as your personal leadership workshop.

通过与系统打交道，我了解到变化的过程始终是有机的：一次只改变一件事是不可能的。我的每一个行为都是我过去某个问题的解决方案。为了学习，我添加了新的行为来与这些有价值的旧行为一起服务。然而，就像种子一样，我已经具备了成长所需的所有行为，所以我只需要有选择地培养它们。我相信领导力涉及一个培育过程，而不是掌管人们的生活，所以这本书是指导你掌管自己发展的过程。它的方法，就像我们研讨会的方法一样，是有机的，旨在以一种温和、现实和有趣的方式适应您的独特系统。

From working with systems, I have learned that the process of change is always organic: It’s never possible to change just one thing at a time. Each of my behaviors is the solution to some problem from my past. To learn, I add new behaviors to serve alongside these valuable old ones. Yet, like a seed, I already have all the behaviors needed to grow, so I merely need to cultivate them selectively. I believe that leadership involves a nurturing process, not taking charge of people’s lives, so this book is a guide to the process of taking charge of your own development. Its methods, like the methods of our workshops, are organic, designed to fit with the unique system that is you in a way that is gentle, realistic, and fun.

然而，改变的过程并不总是那么有趣。因为改变往往很困难，所以本书还旨在提供情感支持。我提供了领导力模型，因此您将有机会摆脱一些可能阻碍您前进道路的旧神话。我提供了变化的模型，这样你就会更好地理解当旧的想法消失时会发生什么。我引用了其他人对他们成为技术领导者的感受的评论，所以你会知道你并不孤单。我知道你会找到自己独特的启迪，我希望这本书能成为你在市场上行走的好伙伴。

Nevertheless, the process of change won’t always feel like fun. Because change is often difficult, the book is also designed to provide emotional support. I offer models of leadership, so you’ll have an opportunity to let go of some old myths that may block your path. I offer models of change, so you’ll understand better what’s happening when old ideas fall away. I quote other people’s remarks about their feelings as they’ve become technical leaders, so you’ll know you’re not alone. I know you will find your own unique enlightenment, and I hope this book will be a welcome companion on your walk through the marketplace.

前言

Foreword

杰里·温伯格 (Jerry Weinberg) 讲述了一位天文学家在花园俱乐部发表演讲的故事。这位天文学家正在描述宇宙起源的“大爆炸”理论。谈话结束时，房间后面的一位女士说：“年轻人，事情不是这样的。世界实际上是在一只大乌龟的背上支撑的。”

Jerry Weinberg tells a story about an astronomer giving a talk at a garden club. The astronomer is describing the “big bang” theory of how the universe began. At the end of the talk a woman in the back of the room speaks out, “Young man, that’s not the way it is. The world is actually supported on the back of a large turtle.”

天文学家有点习惯了不寻常的理论，平静地回答说：“那只乌龟搁在什么上面？” 女人同样平静地回答：“当然是在另一只乌龟身上。” 现在天文学家确信他找到了她。“请问，那只乌龟搁在什么上面？” 女人安详地笑了笑，绝对自信地说：“哦，不，你不知道，一路下来都是海龟！”

The astronomer, somewhat used to unusual theories, replies calmly, “And what is that turtle resting on?” The woman responds just as calmly, “On another turtle, of course.” Now the astronomer is sure he has her. “And what is that turtle resting on, pray tell?” The woman smiles serenely and says with absolute confidence, “Oh, no, you don’t, it’s turtles all the way down!”

杰里·温伯格的书通常就像他的故事一样——一路都是乌龟。他的书很难一口气读完，因为他的每一章，就像他的轶事一样，都有多层次的意义。一遍又一遍地，我发现自己停下来思考——思考杰里刚才说的话，思考我对杰里所说的话的看法，思考我正在思考的事情。你明白我的意思。所以预先警告读者：杰里的写作方法常常会引发严肃的思考。

Jerry Weinberg’s books are often like his stories—turtles all the way down. His books are difficult to read at one sitting because each of his chapters, like his anecdotes, has multiple levels of meaning. Over and over I found myself stopping and thinking—thinking about what Jerry had just said, thinking about what I thought about what Jerry had said, thinking about what I was thinking about. you see what I mean. So the reader is forewarned: Jerry’s approach to writing often induces serious thinking.

在一个层面上，成为技术领导者是一个非常脚踏实地的操作指南。在第二个层面上，它是一组寓言，充满了牢记在心的类比——通过弹球、小工匠玩具和电热毯的故事传授管理艺术。在另一个层面上，这是一本关于管理技术项目的哲学和心理学的书。

On one level, Becoming a Technical Leader is an extremely down-to- earth, how-to guide. On a second level, it is a set of parables, full of analogies that stick in the mind—the art of management taught through stories about pinball, Tinkertoys, and electric blankets. On yet another level, this is a book about the philosophy and psychology of managing technical projects.

尽管我很喜欢这本书，但它还是有一些不妥之处。首先是它太长了。杰瑞在每一章中都包含了如此多的想法和如此多的思考和管理规则，如果你被要求快速阅读它，就像我写一篇开明的前言一样，你根本做不到。这本书的第二个错误是它太短了。就在你以为杰瑞要告诉你如何解决世界上所有重大问题的时候，你读完了这本书，发现杰瑞真正给你的是你自己思考的建议。

As much as I liked the book, there are some things wrong with it. The first thing is that it is too long. Jerry packs so many ideas and so many rules for thinking and managing into each chapter that if you are asked to read it quickly, as I was to write an Enlightened Foreword, you simply can’t do it. The second thing that’s wrong with this book is that it is too short. Just when you think Jerry is going to tell you how to solve all the world’s major problems, you have finished the book and have discovered that what Jerry has really given you is the recommendation that you think for yourself.

回想起来，我想我被标题误导了。我想你可以说这本书确实与成为技术领导者有关。但实际上，这本书最终是关于杰里所有书的主题：如何思考，以及如何在思考时思考你正在思考的事情。杰瑞一个接一个地指出，大多数解决管理和与人合作的实际问题的显而易见的解决方案往往都没有达到目标。因此，他提出了一种简单但截然不同的方式来看待我们都认为自己知道的事情。对我们来说幸运的是，杰里·温伯格 (Jerry Weinberg) 已将解决技术和管理的复杂性作为他毕生的工作，尤其是现代组织中出现的两者的奇怪混合。他所说的一切都触及到家。一遍又一遍，我发现自己又笑又尴尬。最后一点。除非转发者向特定读者推荐前言作者的书，否则任何自尊的前言都是不完整的。我已经考虑过了。在这样做的过程中，我得出的结论是，我唯一可以诚实地向他们推荐这本书的人是那些 (A) 管理人，(B) 被人管理，或 (C) 生活在或认识 A 类人的人或 B。如果你碰巧属于 A、B 或 C 类，那么这本书对你来说是必备的。- 肯·奥尔 我得出的结论是，我唯一可以诚实地向他们推荐这本书的人是那些 (A) 管理人，(B) 被人管理，或 (C) 生活在或认识 A 类或 B 类人的人。如果机缘巧合下，你属于 A、B 或 C 类，这本书对你来说是必备的。- 肯·奥尔 我得出的结论是，我唯一可以诚实地向他们推荐这本书的人是那些 (A) 管理人，(B) 被人管理，或 (C) 生活在或认识 A 类或 B 类人的人。如果机缘巧合下，你属于 A、B 或 C 类，这本书对你来说是必备的。- 肯·奥尔

In retrospect, I think I was misled by the title. I suppose you could say the book does have to do with becoming a technical leader. But in reality, this book is ultimately about what all Jerry’s books are about: how to think, and how to think about what you’re thinking about while you’re thinking. Turtle by turtle, Jerry points out that most of the obvious solutions to the real problems of managing and working with people tend to miss the mark. So he proposes simple, but radically different, ways of looking at things we all thought we knew. Fortunately for us, Jerry Weinberg has made unraveling the com plexities of technology and management his life’s work, in particular, the curious mixture of the two that occurs in modern organizations. Everything he says touches home. Over and over, I found myself laughing and being embarrassed at the same time. One final point. No self-respecting Foreword is complete unless the Forwarder recommends the book of the Forewordee to a specific audience. I have given this some thought. In doing so, I came to the conclusion that the only people to whom I could honestly recommend this book are those who (A) manage people, (B) are managed by people, or (C) live around or know people in category A or B. If you, by some chance of fate, fit into category A, B, or C, this book is a must for you. - Ken Orr

PART_ONE_DEFINITION

PART_ONE_DEFINITION

领导很熟悉，但不太了解。如果不是那么熟悉，就不会有这么多的领导神话。如果更好地理解，就不会有这么多误解。前五章的工作主要是澄清一些迷思和误解。

Leadership is familiar, but not well understood. If it were less familiar, there wouldn’t be so many leadership myths. If it were better understood, there wouldn’t be so many misconceptions. The job of these first five chapters is primarily to clear away some myths and misconceptions.

还有一些构建工作要做，模型的构建将使描述成为技术领导者需要做的事情变得更容易。这些模型将描述一般的领导力、技术领导者特有的特定领导风格，以及人们成为领导者的过程。这些模型将为本书的其余部分设置结构。

There is also some construction to do, construction of models that will then make it easier to describe just what needs to be done to become a technical leader. These models will describe leadership in general, a particular style of leadership that is characteristic of technical leaders, and also the process by which people become leaders. The models will set the structure for the remainder of the book.

最后，有一章将讨论我们从那些说他们不能或不会成为领导者的人那里听到的最常见的原因。在我们解决了这些原因之后，我们将准备好迎接成为技术领导者的任务。

Finally, one chapter will confront the most common reasons we hear from people who say they cannot, or will not, become leaders. After we’ve disposed of these reasons, we’ll be ready to tackle the task of becoming a technical leader.

第 1 章什么是领导力？

Chapter 1. What Is Leadership, Anyway?

如果你是一个好领导，

If you are a good leader,

谁话少，

Who talks little,

他们会说，

They will say,

当你的工作完成后，

When your work is done,

你的目标实现了，

And your aim fulfilled,

“我们自己做的。”

“We did it ourselves.”

——老子

- Lao Tse

领导力就像性。许多人讨论这个话题时遇到困难，但总能引起强烈的兴趣和感受。如果你在讨论领导力这个话题时遇到困难，这本书就是为你准备的。人人都说你应该享受性爱，那么当它不起作用时你能和谁谈谈呢？如果您发现领导混乱、令人尴尬，有时甚至令人痛苦，那么您并不孤单，尽管看起来可能是这样。

Leadership is like sex. Many people have trouble discussing the subject, but it never fails to arouse intense interest and feelings. If you have trouble discussing the subject of leadership, this book is for you. Everyone says you should enjoy sex, so whom can you talk to when it doesn’t work right? If you find leadership messy, embarrassing, and sometimes painful, you are not alone, though it may seem that way.

在这些封面之间，您会找到理解、帮助和同情。看起来非常性感的人在实际表现时往往会令人大失所望。看起来像领导者的人也是如此。他们相信他们应该凭直觉做好这件事，而不是靠练习——当然也不是靠读书。如果你对自己作为领导者的表现感到失望，这本书给你带来了一个简单的希望信息：不必如此。

Between these covers, you’ll find understanding, help, and sympathy. People who look really sexy are often great disappointments when it comes to actual performance. It’s the same with people who look like leaders. They believe they’re supposed to do it well by instinct, not by practice—and certainly not by reading books. If you are disappointed in your own performance as a leader, this book brings you a simple message of hope: It doesn’t have to be that way.

不情愿的领导者

THE RELUCTANT LEADER

根据弗洛伊德的说法，我们对性的偏见是在童年早期形成的。我认为这与我们对领导力的感受是一样的。如果你一直觉得一个人告诉另一个人该做什么有点不对劲，也许你的经历和我一样。

According to Freud, our prejudices about sex are formed in early childhood. I think it’s the same with our feelings about leadership. If you have always felt there was something slightly wrong about one person telling another person what to do, perhaps your experiences were like mine.

在文法学校，我是聪明的孩子之一。在老师眼里，这使我成为尖子生，但在学生眼里，这使我变得胆小怕事。每当老师们在课堂上挑衅我时，学生们就会在课间休息时揍我——如果我幸运的话。如果我运气不好，他们根本不会和我一起玩。

In grammar school, I was one of the smart kids. In the teachers’ eyes, this made me a leading student, but in the students’ eyes, it made me a ratfink. Whenever the teachers singled me out in class, the students punched me out in recess—if I was lucky. If I was unlucky, they wouldn’t play with me at all.

通过这种培训，我很快就了解了成为领导者的危险。虽然学校告诉我每个好公民都应该领导，但校园教会我要为任何领导的愿望感到羞耻。我学会了尽量不要成为领导者。如果领导强加于我，我总是坚决抵抗。只要有可能，我就假装它不存在来处理领导问题。为了确保我永远不必处理领导问题，我选择了计算机软件行业。

With that kind of training, I soon learned about the dangers of being a leader. Although school taught me that every good citizen is supposed to lead, the schoolyard taught me to be ashamed of any desire to lead. I learned to try not to become a leader. If leadership was thrust upon me, I always put up determined resistance. Whenever possible, I dealt with the question of leadership by pretending it didn’t exist. And to make doubly sure I would never have to deal with leadership questions, I chose a career in computer software.

它没有用。每当我在技术上做得相当不错时，我的同事们就会更加尊重我。因为他们尊重我，所以他们向我寻求建议和领导。如果我再聪明一点，我可能会把自己和他们隔离开来，拒绝提供或接受信息。

It didn’t work. Whenever I did a reasonably good technical job, my co-workers learned to respect me a bit more. Because they respected me, they looked to me for advice, for leadership. If I’d been smarter, I might have isolated myself from them, refusing to give or receive information.

但我很天真，而且我喜欢被问到。

But I was naive and besides, I liked to be asked.

有时我被要求教授课程——一种领导力。我被要求参加技术审查委员会——再次担任领导职务。我负责一个项目团队，然后是一个更大的团队。我有一些想法想要在比我自己的办公室更远的地方分享，所以我写了论文和书籍——更多的领导力。每次我意识到发生了什么，我就退缩了。有时我很暴力。

Sometimes I was asked to teach courses—a form of leadership. I was asked to sit on technical review committees—leadership again. I was put in charge of a project team, then a larger team. I had ideas I wanted to share even further than my own office, so I wrote papers and books—more leadership. Each time I realized what was happening, I backed off. Sometimes I was violent.

没有人想让我成为领导者，所以我陷入了悖论。我越是反对成为领导者，我就越是确定自己的方向——我就越是成为一名领导者。

Nobody was going to make me into a leader, so I was snared in a paradox. The more I struggled against becoming a leader, the more I was setting my own direction—and the more I was becoming a leader.

毕竟，领导者不就是不满足于按照别人设定的方向行事的人吗？

After all, isn’t a leader someone who isn’t satisfied with taking the direction set by others?

几年来，我通过退出任何可能导致其他人的事情来应对这个悖论。这种退缩就像通过假装它们不存在来处理性冲动一样。领导还在那里，但我不确定它的方向。有时方向是随机的，但大多数时候我很容易成为操纵者的猎物。最后，我不得不面对领导问题，无论多么尴尬。

I grappled with this paradox for several years by withdrawing from anything that might lead other people. This withdrawal was like dealing with sex drives by pretending they don’t exist. The leadership was still there, but I wasn’t determining its direction. Sometimes the direction was random, but most of the time I was easy prey to manipulators. In the end, I had to face the leadership issue, no matter how embarrassing it was.

面对领导问题

FACING THE LEADERSHIP ISSUE

我有一种处理棘手问题的奇特方式。每当我想学习某事时，我都会安排教授有关该主题的课程。在我教授完课程足以学到一些东西之后，我写了一本书。

I have a curious way of dealing with difficult issues. Whenever I want to learn about something, I arrange to teach a course on the subject. After I’ve taught the course enough to learn something, I write a book.

经过 20 年的领导力研讨会，我认为我已经学到了足够的知识来尝试写一本书。尽管我还有许多未解之谜，但我了解到我并不孤单。还有其他人在自己的生活中受到领导力问题的折磨：

After twenty years of running leadership workshops, I think I’ve learned enough to attempt a book. Although I still have many unanswered questions, I have learned that I’m not alone. There are others out there who are tortured by leadership questions in their own lives:

• 领导者真的像他们有时表现的那样愚蠢吗？

• Are leaders really as stupid as they sometimes behave?

• 我可以成为领导者而不变得像其他人一样吗？

• Can I be a leader without becoming like those other people?

• 我怎样才能成为领导者并同时保持我的技术技能？

• How can I be a leader and keep up my technical skills at the same time?

• 没有任何技术技能的领导者在高科技社会中有立足之地吗？

• Is there a place for a leader in high-tech society who never had any technical skills to begin with?

• 我牺牲了多少技术专长？

• How much of my technical expertise do sacrifice?

• 我会得到什么回报？

• What will I get in return?

• 如果我是领导者，我是否必须指挥周围的人？

• If I’m a leader, will I have to boss people around?

• 我可以通过读书学习领导力吗？

• Can I learn leadership from reading books?

• 我还能做什么来学习？

• What else can I do to learn?

• 为什么人们认为我是领导者，而我却不这么认为？

• Why do people see me as a leader, when I don’t feel that way?

• 当我自认为很有能力时，为什么人们不认为我是领导者？

• Why don’t people see me as a leader, when I feel quite capable?

• 如果我不想承担领导责任怎么办？

• What if I don’t want to assume leadership responsibility?

• 什么是领导力？

• What is leadership, anyway?

这些都是难题。也许最后一个是最难的。什么是领导力？

These are hard questions. Perhaps the last is the hardest of all. What is leadership, anyway?

传统但有缺陷的领导力观

A CONVENTIONAL BUT FLAWED VIEW OF LEADERSHIP

心理学家和管理理论家有许多领导力模型，其中一个典型的文本提供了这样的解释：

Psychologists and management theorists have dozens of models of leadership, with a typical one of their texts offering this explanation:

有两种主要的方法来识别一个组的领导者：

There are two principal ways to identify the leaders of a group:

  1. 要求成员确定他们认为哪些成员对领导团队最有影响力，或者
  2. asking the members to identify which members they regard as most influential in directing the group, or
  3. 要求观察员说出最有影响力的成员的名字，或记录有效影响行动的频率。
  4. asking observers to name the most influential members, or to record the frequency of effective influencing actions.

尽管它们看起来很科学，但这些模型是基于成员或观察者的意见，以及他们观察“有效影响行动”的能力。多年来，我开始看到这种方法的一些缺陷。

Although they appear to be scientific, these models are based on the opinions of the members or the observers, and on their ability to observe “effective influencing actions.” Over the years, I began to see some flaws in that approach.

例如，一家公司最近聘请我帮助一群计算机程序员提高他们解决问题的能力。由于软件产品中的一个细微错误，该公司每天损失数千美元的销售额。在程序员发现错误之前，该产品毫无用处。为了帮助小组，我在他们努力寻找错误的过程中对他们进行了录像。

For instance, a company recently retained me to help a group of computer programmers improve their problem-solving techniques. The company was losing thousands of dollars of sales each passing day because of a subtle error in its software product. Until the programmers could find the error, the product was useless. To help the group, I videotaped them as they struggled to find the error.

在一个小时的观察中，参与其中的四位程序员的“有效影响行为”是这样的：

In one hour of observation, the “effective influencing actions” of the four programmers involved looked like this:

阿尼 112 动作

Arnie 112 actions

菲利斯 52 行动

Phyllis 52 actions

韦伯 23 动作

Weber 23 actions

玛莎 0 次操作

Martha 0 actions

玛莎的行为很容易记录下来。整整一个小时，她都像个僵尸一样坐着，研究错误程序的打印输出。她什么也没说，没有做任何动作，甚至没有微笑或皱眉。毫无疑问，她对团队没有任何影响。

Martha’s actions were easy to record. She sat like a zombie through the entire hour, studying the printout of the erroneous program. She said nothing, made no gestures, and didn’t even smile or frown. Without question, she had no influence on the group whatsoever.

在用了一个小时的有效影响行动后，其他小组成员并没有比他们开始时更接近于解决问题。突然，玛莎将目光从列表上移开，用手指着其中一行，然后非常平静地说道：“这个词应该是‘87AB0023’，而不是‘87AB0022’。” 然后阿尼、菲利斯和韦伯又开始了他们激动的讨论。十分钟后，在他们确信玛莎确实是正确的之后，他们终止了会议。

After consuming an hour with their effective influencing actions, the other group members were no closer to solving the problem than when they started. All of a sudden, Martha lifted her eyes from the listing, pointed a finger at one line, and said, ever so quietly, “This word should be ‘87AB0023’, not ‘87AB0022’.” Then Arnie, Phyllis, and Weber resumed their agitated discussion. They terminated the meeting ten minutes later, after they had convinced themselves that Martha was indeed correct.

当我问这群人谁是他们最有影响力的成员时，他们都说，“Arnie”。然后我播放录像带，让他们特别注意解决问题的方法。看完录像后，Arnie、Phyllis 和 Weber 将答案改为“Martha”。为什么？因为就解决他们的问题而言，有效影响行动表应该是

When I asked the group who had been their most influential member, they all said, “Arnie.” Then I played the videotape, asking them to be especially alert to the method by which their problem was solved. After watching the tape, Arnie, Phyllis, and Weber changed their answer to “Martha.” Why? Because in terms of solving their problem, the table of effective influencing actions should have read

阿尼 0 次操作

Arnie 0 actions

菲利斯 0 次操作

Phyllis 0 actions

韦伯 0 动作

Weber 0 actions

玛莎 1 个动作

Martha 1 action

如果没有 Martha 的贡献，会议将毫无进展，但非编程心理学家可能会完全错过 Martha 的角色。当这些非技术心理学家观察我们的研讨会时，他们总是被团队在解决技术问题时的动态所迷惑。就好像心理学家正在观察来自另一个星球的人，他们的文化和语言表面上看起来和听起来像我们的，但实际上完全不同。

Without Martha’s contribution, the meeting would have gone nowhere, yet non-programming psychologists would have probably missed Martha’s role entirely. When such nontechnical psychologists observe our workshops, they are consistently befuddled by the dynamics of the teams as they solve technical problems. It’s as if the psychologists were watching people from another planet, people whose culture and language look and sound superficially like ours but are entirely different.

对比世界模型

CONTRASTING MODELS OF THE WORLD

为了认可团队中的领导力，你必须有一个以某种方式与团队文化相匹配的模型。例如，如果他们的“解决问题”模型过于简单，心理学家将难以理解技术环境中的领导力。有人曾经说过，学术心理学的中心教条是每个问题只有一个正确的解决方案——心理学家知道这一点。任何相信该简单模型的心理学家都难以以适用于现实世界情境的方式定义领导力。一方面，这样的人肯定不会承认玛莎是领导者。

In order to recognize leadership in a group, you must have a model that somehow matches the group’s culture. For instance, if their model of “problem solving” is too simple, psychologists will have trouble understanding leadership in technical environments. Someone once said that the central dogma of academic psychology is that there is one and only one correct solution to every problem—and the psychologist knows it. Any psychologist who believes that simple model will have trouble defining leadership in a way that works in real-world situations. For one thing, such a person would certainly never recognize Martha as a leader.

人们在世界上的行为方式有很多模型。即使在心理学学科中，也有几十个主要模型和数百个小变体。社会学家的模型不同于心理学家的模型，也不同于人类学家、经济学家、行政人员和看门人的模型。有这么多模型的原因是它们中的每一个都有用，但仅在某些情况下有用。当我们尝试应用与眼前情况不匹配的模型时，就会出现问题。

There are many models of how people behave in the world. Even within the discipline of psychology, there are dozens of major models and hundreds of minor variations. The sociologists’ models differ from those of the psychologists, as well as from the anthropologists, the economists, the executives, and the janitors. The reason there are so many models is that each of them is useful, but only in some contexts. The problems arise when we try to apply a model that doesn’t match the situation in front of our eyes.

在本书中，我将使用和开发一些模型来理解我们有时称之为“领导力”的难以捉摸的现象。要成为一名有效的领导者，您必须拥有多种模式供您使用，并且能够根据情况需要从一种模式适当地切换到另一种模式。我喜欢的大多数模型可能被认为是有机模型，与线性模型形成对比，但有时我可以非常恰当地使用线性模型。

In this book, I will use and develop a number of models for understanding that slippery phenomenon we sometimes call “leader- ship.” To be an effective leader, you will have to have many models at your disposal, and be able to switch appropriately from one to another as the situation demands. Most of the models I favor may be considered organic models, in contrast to linear models, but there are times when I can be quite appropriately linear.

有机模型可以在几个维度上与线性模型进行对比：解释事件的方式、定义人的方式、定义关系的方式以及对变化的态度。让我们依次比较两种类型的模型，然后看看它们如何影响领导力的定义方式。

Organic models can be contrasted with linear models on several dimensions: the way events are explained, the way a person is defined, the way a relationship is defined, and the attitude toward change. Let’s compare the two types of models on each of these in turn, then see how they affect the way leadership is defined.

一个事件的解释

Explanation of an event

线性模型得名于假设事件之间存在线性关系；也就是说，一种结果源于一种原因，反之亦然。有机模型的特征可能是“系统思考”：相信事件 X 是数百个其他因素的结果，包括时间的流逝。

Linear models get their name from the assumption of a linear relationship between events; that is, one effect stems from one cause, and vice versa. Organic models may be characterized by “systems thinking”: the belief that event X is the outcome of hundreds of other factors, including the passage of time.

线性模型的优势在于大量事件可以根据单一原因很好地理解它们的弱点来自更复杂的事件，不幸的是，其中包括涉及人的大多数关键事件。

The strength of linear models lies in the large number of events that can be well understood in terms of a single cause Their weakness arises from events of greater complexity, which include, unfortunately, most critical events involving people.

威胁/奖励模型是添加了道德的线性模型的示例；只有一个正确答案，看不到它的人要么是傻子，要么是坏人。当我们使用这个模型时，面对我们不能立即理解的事件，我们往往会感到愚蠢和羞愧。

The threat/reward model is an example of a linear model with morality added; there is one and only one right answer, and anyone who cannot see it must be either dumb or bad. When we use this model, we tend to feel stupid and ashamed in the face of events we don’t immediately understand.

相比之下，有机模型的优势在于它们使我们能够在我们不完全理解的复杂情况下感到舒适。当我们使用这些模型时，我们能够对许多可能的解释（其中许多可能同时成立）敞开心扉，直到我们有足够的信息来做出适当的选择。

The strength of organic models, by contrast, is that they enable us to be comfortable in complex situations that we don’t fully understand. When we use these models, we’re able to open our minds to dozens of possible explanations (many of which can be true simultaneously) until we have sufficient information to make an appropriate choice.

有机模型的一个弱点是它们可能会阻止我们采取任何行动。有效的领导者即使不了解所有可能的因素，也常常不得不采取行动。为了使用有机模型，您必须能够忍受偶尔的错误。

One weakness of organic models is that they may prevent us from acting at all. Effective leaders often have to act even when they don’t understand all possible factors. In order to use organic models, you must be able to live with the occasional error.

一个人的定义

Definition of a person

线性模型倾向于将个体归类。有机模型根据人的独特性来定义人，即他们的相同性和差异性。

Linear models tend to place individuals in categories. Organic models define people in terms of their uniqueness, that is, their sameness plus their differences.

线性方法有用的一面是它使我们能够快速有效地与人打交道。我们可以在早上点一杯咖啡，而无需考虑服务员的个性。

The useful side of the linear approach is that it allows us to deal with people quickly and efficiently. We can order a cup of coffee in the morning without considering the waiter in his full-blown individuality.

有机模型有用的一面是它允许不同的人找到在复杂情况下一起工作的共同基础。遵循有机模型的人倾向于将其他人视为共享相同的生命力、相同的精神基础，以及在他们独特的个体部分之间的相同类型的关系。他们不会将人与某种标准进行比较，因此他们不会试图将人们塑造成某种理想形象。这样的人倾向于将领导者的工作视为让人们接触到自己内心的和谐。

The useful side of the organic model is the way it allows different people to find a common basis for working together in complex situations. People who abide by the organic model tend to see other people as sharing the same life force, the same spiritual base, and the same kind of relationship among their unique individual parts. They don’t compare people to some standard, so they are not tempted to shape people to some ideal image. Such people tend to see the job of a leader as getting people in touch with their own inner harmony.

当线性模型滑向根据人应该成为什么来定义人时，它们就变得不那么有用了。如果人们的想法、感受或行为与这个理想不同，他们可能会被“对待”，试图缩小他们的规模，或扩大他们的规模。威胁/奖励模型是一个线性模型，它表示人们的行为完全由他们面临的威胁和奖励来定义。当我们在威胁/奖励模式之外运作时，我们倾向于将领导者的工作视为发出威胁和发放奖励。

Linear models become less useful when they slip over into defining people in terms of what they should be. If people differ in their thinking, feeling, or acting from this ideal, they may be “treated” with attempts to cut them down to size, or stretch them out. The threat/reward model is a linear model that says people’s actions are completely defined by the threats and rewards confronting them. When we operate out of the threat/reward model, we tend to see the leader’s job as issuing threats and doling out rewards.

当我们坚持威胁/奖励模型时，我们往往会低估自我价值和他人的价值。我们给自己——和其他人——这样的信息，比如“工作不够努力”、“我话太多”、“我太胖了”和“我无法让人们做我想做的事”。这些信息通常会导致沮丧、愤怒和不值得的感觉，但如果被问到，我们会否认这些感受。

When we hold to the threat/reward model, we tend to have low feelings of self-worth and the worth of others. We give ourselves—and others—messages such as don’t work hard enough,” “I talk too much,” “I’m too fat,” and “I can’t get people to do what I want.” These messages often lead to feeling frustrated, angry, and unworthy, though if asked, we will deny these feelings.

关系的定义

Definition of relationships

线性模型倾向于根据角色而不是人来定义关系：老板而不是实际施加影响的人。有机模型倾向于根据一个独特的人与另一个独特的人来定义关系。

Linear models tend to define relationships in terms of roles rather than people: the boss rather than the person actually exerting influence. The organic model tends to define relationships in terms of one unique person to another unique person.

线性模型的一个有用方面是它们允许规划大规模操作，而在这种情况下不可能全面考虑每种关系。当线性模型扩展到一对一关系时，它们就不那么有用了，在这种情况下，个性在理解交互时变得至关重要。

One useful side of linear models is that they allow planning of large-scale operations, where it would be impossible to consider each relationship in its full glory. Linear models are less useful when they are extended to one-to-one relationships, where individuality becomes critical in understanding the interaction.

坚持威胁/奖励极端的人往往认为权力存在于角色中，而不是关系中，因此他们非常重视头衔作为定义关系的一种方式。当事情变得艰难时，他们可能会援引自己的“权威”，或者屈服于他人的“权威”。尽管这种权力观在统计上很有用，但当应用于一对一的情况时，它就会分崩离析。在爱情、教学或领导中，认为一个人总是在上面而另一个人总是在下面的想法并不太有用。当我们确实以这种方式思考时，我们往往会体验到对他人的恐惧、愤怒、攻击性、内疚和嫉妒等情绪。

People who adhere to the threat/reward extreme tend to see power as existing in the role, rather than the relationship, so they put great store in titles as a way of defining relationships. When things get tough, they are likely to invoke their “authority,” or yield to someone else’s. Although this view of power can be useful statistically, it falls apart when applied to one-on-one situations. In love, or teaching, or leading, it’s not too useful to think in terms of one person always on top and the other always on the bottom. When we do think this way, we tend to experience emotions of fear, anger, aggression, guilt, and envy toward the other person.

有机模型的用处在一对一的情况下最为明显。这两个人，无论他们在当前情况下的角色如何，都被认为具有同等的生命意义。有机模型导致解决问题，每个人都能从中受益。当我们以这种方式对待他人时，我们最常见的情绪是发现的喜悦。然而，有时我们会沉浸在这种喜悦中，以致于如果有工作要做，我们就无法完成工作。

The usefulness of organic models is most clear in one-on-one situations. The two persons, regardless of their roles in the current situation, are presumed equal in life significance. Organic models lead toward problem solving in which everyone benefits. When we act this way toward other people, our most common emotion is joy of discovery. Sometimes, however, we get so wrapped up in this joy that we fail to get the job done, if there is a job to do.

改变态度

Attitude toward change

当我们检查变化的过程时，线性模型和有机模型形成鲜明对比。线性模型倾向于将变化视为一个有序的、一次一件事的过程。有机模型的基础是系统思考的基本思想：“一次只改变一件事是不可能的。” 线性模型往往在相对稳定的情况下最有效，但当事情开始发生变化时，它们就会给我们带来麻烦。

When we examine the processes of change, linear and organic models are in stark contrast. Linear models tend to see change as an orderly, one-thing-at-a-time process. Underlying organic models is the fundamental idea of systems thinking: “It is impossible to change just one thing at a time.” Linear models tend to be most effective in relatively stable situations, but when things start changing, they get us into trouble.

一种麻烦是当变化不适合我们的模型时，我们试图阻止它发生。面对变化时，我们可能会感到无助和无助。坚持有机模式的人和其他人一样需要安全感，但他们通过承担风险和容忍不确定性来获得安全感。

One kind of trouble is that when change doesn’t fit our model, we try to stop it from happening. When faced with change, we may feel paralyzed and helpless. People holding to organic models need security just as much as anyone else, but they obtain their security by taking risks and by tolerating ambiguity.

在威胁/奖励模型的影响下，我们可能会努力让所有人和关系永远保持不变，从而确保我们的安全。如果我们确实觉得需要改变，我们通常会直接针对其他人。我们通常会尝试通过“移除”他们的“不良”行为来改变他们。

Under the influence of the threat/reward model, we may try to assure our security by struggling to keep all people and relationships forever the same. If we do feel the need to change, we usually direct it at someone else. And we usually try to change them by “removing” their “bad” behaviors.

有机模型期望并接受变化作为宇宙的正常部分。一些有机模式走得更远，欢迎改变，将其视为进入未知世界和成长的机会。他们相信成长是一个自然过程，通过这个过程我们可以实现美妙的潜力，就像种子必须成长才能实现花朵的美妙潜力一样。我们有时会将这种有机模型称为种子模型。

Organic models expect and accept change as a normal part of the universe. Some organic models go even further, and welcome change as an opportunity to go into the unknown and grow. They have faith that growth is a natural process by which our wonderful potential is realized, in the same way a seed must grow to realize the wonderful potential of the flower. We’ll sometimes refer to such organic models as seed models.

领导力的有机定义

AN ORGANIC DEFINITION OF LEADERSHIP

这是对线性模型和有机模型之间差异的粗略描述，我们将在本书展开时详细说明。显然，没有人会在 100% 的时间里使用任何一种模型，这就是为什么领导力的定义如此难以确定的原因之一。

That’s a very rough sketch of the difference between linear and organic models, a sketch we will elaborate upon as the book unfolds. Obviously, no person uses either type of model one hundred percent of the time, and that’s one reason why the definition of leadership is so hard to pin down.

线性模型和有机模型导致了关于什么构成领导力的截然不同的想法。在极端情况下，领导力的威胁/奖励模型可能以“强制”和“判断”这两个词为特征，而种子模型则以“选择”和“发现”为特征。在种子模型中，领导力是创造一个让人们获得授权的环境的过程。

Linear and organic models lead to contrasting ideas of what constitutes leadership. In the extreme cases, the threat/reward model of leadership may be characterized by the words “force” and “judge,” and the seed model, “choose” and “discover.” In the seed model, Leadership is the process of creating an environment in which people become empowered.

例如，在玛莎进行观察之前，阿尼、菲利斯和韦伯的问题解决技巧毫无进展。经过她的观察，环境发生了变化，同样的功法变得强大起来。

For example, before Martha made her observation, Arnie, Phyllis, and Weber were getting nowhere with their problem-solving techniques. After her observation, the environment changed so that the same techniques became powerful.

但是 Arnie、Phyllis 和 Weber 也以一种令人惊讶的方式发挥了领导作用，他们创造了一种环境，让 Martha 可以自由地以一种对她来说很有影响力的方式工作。团体中的一些人根本不能容忍一个成员不“参与”，他们的意思是说很多话。说话不是玛莎的风格，其他人也知道这一点，所以他们让她一个人呆着。这也是领导力。与威胁/奖励模型中的领导人员不同，有机领导领导流程，领导人员要求他们放弃对自己生活的控制。领导这个过程是对人们的回应，给他们选择并让他们控制。它们被赋予力量的方式与园丁赋予种子力量的方式非常相似——不是通过强迫它们生长，而是通过挖掘潜藏在它们内部的力量。

But Arnie, Phyllis, and Weber were also exercising leadership, in a surprising way, by creating an environment in which Martha was free to work in a style that was powerful for her. Some people in groups simply cannot tolerate one member not “participating,” by which they mean doing a lot of talking. Talking wasn’t Martha’s style, and the others knew it so they left her alone. That’s also leadership. Instead of leading people, as in the threat/reward model, organic leadership leads the process, Leading people requires that they relinquish control over their lives. Leading the process is responsive to people, giving them choices and leaving them in control. They are empowered in much the same way a gardener empowers seeds—not by forcing them to grow, but by tapping the power that lies dormant within them.

种子意义上的领导力是通过他人创造和生产的。这是一个有机的定义，因为它通过创造一个环境而不是将自己局限于少数几个特定实例中的一些集中行动（威胁或奖励）来产生一些特定结果。

Leadership in the seed sense is creative and productive through other people. It is an organic definition, because it works through creating an environment rather than confining itself to a few focused actions—threats or rewards—in a few specific instances to create a few specific results.

对于陷入线性模型的人来说，这种有机的领导力模型可能看起来含糊不清，但它实际上比更传统的模型更适合于更精确的量化。它在技术工作中特别有用，因为与更线性的模型不同，它允许我们考虑创新。创新与重新定义任务或完成任务的方式有关。领导力的线性定义假设观察者对任务有完美的理解。这样的定义过滤掉了观察者以前没有见过或不理解的创新。这种盲目的旁观者显然看不到通过创新引领的可能性。在高科技和发现的时代，这种限制性定义实际上毫无用处。

To people ensnared by linear models, this organic model of leadership may seem vague and wishy-washy, but it actually lends itself to more precise quantification than the more conventional models. It’s especially useful in technical work because, unlike the more linear models, it allows us to take innovation into account. Innovation is concerned with redefining a task or the way the task is done. Linear definitions of leadership assume that observers have a perfect understanding of the task. Such definitions filter out innovations that the observer hasn’t seen before or doesn’t understand. Such blinded observers obviously cannot see the possibility of leadership through innovation. In an age of high technology and discovery, such constraining definitions are practically useless.

有机的领导模式涵盖了所有类型的工作，尤其是技术含量高的工作。它并没有得罪技术工作者，实际上可以用来衡量像玛莎这样的创新贡献。心理学家可能不同意我的方法，但我发现这是描述技术领导者和技术团队的实用方法。

The organic model of leadership covers all sorts of work, especially the highly technical. It does not offend technical workers, and can actually be used to measure innovative contributions such as Martha’s. Psychologists might not agree with my approach, but I have found it a practical way to describe technical leaders and technical teams.

问题

QUESTIONS

  1. 观察你认为是领导者的人。这个人的生活与你的生活有何不同？这些差异中的哪些是作为领导者的结果？其中哪些是成为领导者的原因？
  2. Observe someone you consider a leader. How is this person’s life different from yours? Which of these differences are a result of being a leader? Which of them are a cause of being a leader?
  3. 如果你提高了你的领导能力，你希望你的生活会怎样变得更好？这些改进中，哪些改进来自于你的行为改变，哪些来自于对他人行为改变的认识？
  4. How would you expect your life to be better if you increased your leadership skills? Which of these improvements will arise from your changed behavior, and which from recognition of the changed behavior of other people?
  5. 如果你的领导能力提高，你的生活会如何变得更糟？这些改变值得回报吗？你怎样才能改变，同时又不让这些改变对你产生如此不利的影响？
  6. How would your life change for the worse if your leadership skills increased? Will these changes be worth the rewards? How can you change, yet behave in such a way that these changes do not affect you so adversely?
  7. 列出您的存在似乎可以提高他人工作效率的情况。与此列表一起，确定您的存在似乎会降低工作效率的情况。您如何描述这些情况之间的差异？（例如，提高生产力可能涉及与您熟悉的人一起工作，或者解决一个新的和不同的问题。或者对您来说恰恰相反。）这些列表告诉您关于您自己和您所处环境的哪些信息授权你？
  8. Make a list of situations in which your presence seems to increase the productivity of others. Alongside this list, identify situations in which your presence seems to decrease the productivity. How can you characterize the differences between these situations? (For example, increases in productivity might involve working with people you know well, or working on a problem that is new and different. Or perhaps just the reverse is true for you.) What do these lists tell you about yourself and the environments that empower you?
  9. 根据前一个问题的两个列表，从统计上看，您是集团的资产还是负债？你是在寻找你的领导会积极的情况，还是你更经常寻找可以学习做得更好的情况？实际上，您是否从这些情况中吸取了教训，还是只是不断重复自己？
  10. Based on the two lists from the previous question, are you statistically an asset to groups, or a liability? Do you seek out situations in which your leadership will be positive, or do you more often look for situations in which you can learn to do better? Do you, in fact, learn from these situations, or do you just keep repeating yourself?

第 2 章领导风格模型

Chapter 2. Models of Leadership Style

如果一种特定的行为被一种文化认为是重要的，几乎

If a particular behavior is considered important by a culture, nearly

每个正常人都能获得令人印象深刻的能力。

every normal individual can attain impressive competence.

——霍华德·加德纳，《心智框架》

—Howard Gardner, Frames of Mind

有机模型认为，领导力是创造一个让人们获得授权的环境的过程。当人们被赋予权力时，他们可以自由地观看、聆听、感受和评论。他们也可以自由行动、行动、要求他们想要的东西、发挥创造力并做出选择。

The organic model says that leadership is the process of creating an environment in which people become empowered. When people are empowered, they are free to see, to hear, to feel, and to comment. They are also free to move about, to act, to ask for what they want, to be creative, and to make choices.

有机模型还告诉我们，每个人都是独一无二的，因此我们可以期待许多不同的领导风格。不信，花十分钟观察一组两个人。您将看到数十种不同的领导行为，在无数个人和技术细节上各不相同。那么，我们如何才能希望以一种有助于您发展自己的领导风格的方式来概括领导力呢？

The organic model also tells us that each person is unique, and so we can expect many different leadership styles. If you don’t believe it, spend ten minutes observing two people in a group. You will see dozens of different leadership actions, differing in myriad personal and technical details. How, then, can we hope to generalize about leadership in a way that will be helpful to you in developing your own leadership style?

在本章中，我将开发一个模型，我称之为 MOI 模型，以帮助你了解你与他人合作的独特风格。为了让模型更真实，我喜欢从个人经历入手。不过，和其他人一样，我很难弄清楚自己领导能力的来源。作为替代，我经常使用我的弹球能力，因为我可以毫无尴尬地追溯我的弹球生涯多年。

In this chapter, I’ll develop a model, which I call the MOI model, to help you understand your own distinctive style of working with other people. To lend reality to the model, I like to start with personal experience. Like everyone else, though, I have difficulty being clear about the source of my own leadership abilities. As a substitute, I often use my pinball abilities because I can trace my pinball career back many years without embarrassment.

动机

MOTIVATION

小时候，我的弹球技术是我为数不多的引以为豪的事情之一，但我妈妈不喜欢我玩弹球的想法。在电子游戏出现之前的日子里，弹球机出现在台球厅和保龄球馆，这些都是我冒着长得太快的危险的不正当聚会场所。于是，父亲弄来一台叫“五十二十”的机器，放在我们家的地下室里，希望能让我在家多呆几年。

As a kid, my pinball skill was one of the few things I was proud of, but my mother didn’t like the idea of my playing pinball. In the days before video games, pinball machines were found in pool halls and bowling alleys, iniquitous hangouts where I ran the risk of growing up a too fast. So, my father got a machine called Five-Ten-Twenty and put it in our basement, hoping to keep me safely at home for a few more years.

当然，我会留在家里玩免费的弹球，但我的父母担心如果我可以免费玩，我就不会了解金钱的价值。所以，我父亲让我自己付钱玩；那时候是五球五分钱。有时我在家里玩，有时我去台球馆。

Naturally, I would have stayed home to play free pinball, but my parents were afraid I wouldn’t learn the value of money if I could play for nothing. So, my father made me pay my own nickels to play; it was five balls for five cents in those days. Sometimes I played at home, and sometimes I went to the pool hall.

附近的另一个孩子奥蒙德也有一台弹球机，但他的父母似乎不那么困惑。奥蒙德可以免费玩一整天，尽管他让他的朋友们使用镍币。我多么讨厌奥蒙德。我多么羡慕他。在他自己的比赛中经常击败他让我感到非常满足，尽管我不得不为此特权付出五分钱

Another kid in the neighborhood, Ormond, also had a pinball machine, but his parents seemed less confused. Ormond could play all day for nothing, though he made his friends use nickels. How I hated Ormond. How I envied him. It gave me great satisfaction to beat him regularly at his own game, even though I had to pay a nickel for the privilege

奥蒙德很容易被打败；他是附近最差的弹球手。回想起来，我认为他的父母让他免费打球对他是一种伤害，因为奥蒙德没有动力，没有动力去学习打得更好。如果他做得不好，他只是重置机器并开始另一场免费游戏。另一方面，我在每场比赛中都投入了自己的钱，所以我下定决心要从每一个球中得到我所有的钱。当我变老——也变得更富有——我的弹球能力达到了一个稳定期多年。我花五美分还是五美元来玩一个下午的娱乐活动都无关紧要，所以没有推动改进的动力。然后，突然之间，弹球开始净化它污损的形象。您不再需要在自己家里玩游戏。

Ormond was easy to beat; he was the worst pinball player in the neighborhood. Looking back, I think his parents did him a disservice by letting him play for free, because Ormond had no motivation, no push, to learn to play better. If he wasn’t doing well, he just reset the machine and started another free game. I, on the other hand, had a nickel of my own money invested in every game, so I was determined to get my full penny’s worth out of every ball. When I got older—and richer—my pinball prowess hit a plateau for many years. It didn’t matter much whether I spent five cents or five dollars for an afternoon’s entertainment, so there was no push to improve. Then, all of a sudden, pinball began to purify its besmirched image. You no longer had to play in the privacy of your own home.

弹球变得有益健康，你甚至可以赢得奖杯。奖杯一直吸引着我，我的比赛突然好转了。尽管有两个不同的原因可以提高我的游戏水平——骄傲和金钱——但它们实际上是同一枚硬币的两面。

Pinball had become wholesome, and you could even win trophies. Trophies have always appealed to me, and my game took a sudden turn for the better. Although there were two different reasons to improve my game— pride and money—they really amounted to two sides of the same coin.

无论我是学会赢得奖杯还是摆脱财务困境，如果没有某种拉动或推动，我都会像被宠坏的奥蒙德一样，什么都不会改变。

Whether I learned to win a trophy or to stay out of financial trouble, without some sort of pull or push, I would have been like spoiled Ormond, and nothing would have changed.

理念

IDEAS

由于我改进了球技，我成为了在 Pinball Pete's 和 Red Baron 闲逛的孩子们心目中的英雄。他们拥有年轻人所有的原始技能和热情，但他们不明白这样一个祖父般的人怎么能如此持续地鞭打他们。

As a result of my improved play, I became something of a hero to the kids hanging out at Pinball Pete’s and at the Red Baron. They had all the raw skill and enthusiasm of youth, but they couldn’t understand how such a grandfatherly type could whip them so consistently.

他们的尊重感觉很好。这很像我早期的程序员生涯。如果你能表现，你就成为了领导者。这些孩子不听自己父母的话，但他们听我的话。他们想知道我的秘密，我很快发现自己在经营一家非正式诊所。

Their respect felt good. It was a lot like my early days as a programmer. If you could perform, you became the leader. These kids wouldn’t listen to their own parents, but they listened to me. They wanted to know my secrets, and I soon found myself running an informal clinic.

我有许多轻松的教练胜利。孩子们真的很想学习，他们的手很快，而且他们中的大多数人不戴眼镜也能看到球。我所要做的就是观察一个孩子几分钟，然后对不同的方法提出一点想法。这就像将蒲公英种子撒在新的早熟禾草坪上。

I had many easy coaching triumphs. The kids really wanted to learn, they had quick hands, and most of them could see the ball without glasses. All I had to do was watch a kid for a few minutes, then drop in a little idea about a different approach. It was like dropping dandelion seeds onto a new bluegrass lawn.

当然，我最大的秘密是，年长的人必须比孩子们更理性地看待弹球。我的眼睛昏花，我的腿累了，我的手也比以前慢了很多。没有想法，我就没有获胜的机会。

My biggest secret, of course, is that older folks have to take a more cerebral view of pinball than kids do. My eyes are dim, my legs get tired, and my hands are a lot slower than they used to be. Without ideas, I wouldn’t stand a chance of winning.

组织

ORGANIZATION

但是，即使我非常清楚地告诉他们该怎么做，有些孩子似乎也没有学会。以赫比为例。不管我告诉他多少次，赫比总是会把一只手从脚蹼上拿开，帮他梳理眼睛上的头发。大约每隔三次，球就会射过他固定不动的脚蹼。

But some of the kids didn’t seem to learn even when I told them very clearly what to do. Take Herbie, for instance. No matter how often I told him, Herbie would always take one hand off the flippers to brush his hair out of his eyes. About every third time, the ball would shoot pass his immobilized flipper.

或者带上沃恩。弹球的基本技术之一就是依次翻转两个脚蹼，但尽管被告知了一百遍，沃恩总是会兴奋不已，一下子打了两个脚蹼。

Or take Vaughn. One of the basic techniques of pinball is to flip the two flippers in sequence, but in spite of being told a hundred times, Vaughn would invariably get so excited that he punched both flippers at once.

或者阿尔弗雷德。如果你在一些关键情况下不敲击机器，你就不能玩获胜的弹球游戏。可怜的阿尔弗雷德实在是太胆小了，不敢给机器一个好的撞击，即使这会让他失去一场免费比赛。

Or Alfred. You can’t play winning pinball if you won’t bang the machine in a few crucial situations. Poor Alfred was just too timid to give the machine a good bump, even if it was going to cost him a free game.

另一方面，是阿尔弗雷德的妹妹温蒂。要打败弹球机，您必须保持冷静。我向 Wendy 解释了这个原理，但她忍不住用力敲打机器以发泄对机器的深深的不满。她也没有限制对机器的发泄。每场比赛结束后，Wendy 都会设法给机器快速踢一脚投币箱。一开始这没什么害处，但后来她开始上芭蕾舞课——并学习踢得更高。在一个特别低的分数之后，她设法用脚后跟穿过 Fireball 的后玻璃，成为唯一一位终身禁止进入 Pinball Pete's 的女性。

On the other hand, there was Alfred’s sister, Wendy. To beat a pinball machine, you have to keep your cool. I explained this principle to Wendy, but she couldn’t resist venting some deep frustration on the machine by banging it as hard as she could. She didn’t restrict her venting to the machine, either. After every game, Wendy managed to give the machine a swift kick in the coin box. This was harmless enough at first, but then she started taking ballet lessons—and learning to kick higher. After a particularly low score, she managed to put her heel through the back glass of Fireball and became the only female ever banned for life from Pinball Pete’s.

尽管我的教练无懈可击，但赫比、沃恩、阿尔弗雷德和温迪的比赛质量从未提高过。他们都缺乏一个有序的基础来构建更好的游戏。他们并不缺乏动力，因为他们确实想打得更好。他们的生活没有足够的组织来学习任何需要不平凡的努力的东西。

In spite of my flawless coaching, Herbie, Vaughn, Alfred, and Wendy never improved the quality of their play. They all lacked an orderly base on which to build a better game. They didn’t lack push, for they did want to play better. Their lives just weren’t sufficiently organized to learn anything that required a nontrivial effort.

领导力的 MOI 模型

THE MOI MODEL OF LEADERSHIP

为了发生变化，环境必须包含三个要素：

In order for change to occur, the environment must contain three ingredients:

• M：动机——战利品或麻烦，推动或拉动相关人员

• M: motivation–the trophies or trouble, the push or pull that moves the people involved

• O：组织——使想法能够付诸实践的现有结构

• O: organization–the existing structure that enables the ideas to be worked through into practice

• I：想法或创新——种子，未来的形象

• I: ideas or innovation–the seeds, the image of what will become

领导力也可能意味着阻止变革。如果你想阻止某些变化的发生，你必须对环境做以下三件事之一：

Leadership can also mean preventing change. If you want to stop some change from occurring, you must do one of three things to the environment:

• M：扼杀动机——让人觉得改变不会被欣赏；为他们做所有事情，这样他们就不会觉得有必要为自己做事；劝阻人们为了自己的利益而可能喜欢做的任何事情

• M: kill the motivation—make people feel that change will not be appreciated; do everything for them so they won’t feel the need to do things for themselves; dis- courage anything that people might enjoy doing for its own sake

• O：助长混乱——鼓励如此激烈的竞争以至于合作变得不可想象；使资源略低于必要的最低限度；压制具有一般价值的信息，或将其掩埋在大量无意义的文字和纸张中

• O: foster chaos—encourage such high competition that cooperation will be unthinkable; keep resources slightly below the necessary minimum; suppress information of general value, or bury it in an avalanche of meaningless words and paper

• I：抑制思想的流动——可以批评的时候不听；首先提出自己的想法，而且声音最大；惩罚提出建议的人；阻止人们一起工作；最重要的是，不能容忍笑声

• I: suppress the flow of ideas—don’t listen when you can criticize instead; give your own ideas first, and loudest; punish those who offer suggestions; keep people from working together; and above all, tolerate no laughter

无论是用于促进还是阻止变革，MOI 模型都为我们提供了一个领导风格的粗略模型。在法语中，moi的意思是“我”，我们可以通过将此人的行为分类为激励性、组织性或创新性来描述特定人在特定情况下的领导方法。

Whether used to foster or prevent change, the MOI model gives us a gross model of leadership style. In French, moi means “me,” and we can characterize a particular person’s approach to leadership in a specific instance by classifying that person’s actions as motivational, organizational, or innovational.

如果一个人的行为几乎完全是激励性的，那么他可能是一位销售巨星或一位有魅力的政治家，可以推销任何想法——如果她有一个想法可以推销的话。行动几乎完全有条理的人可能是一位非常高效的办公室经理，他使事情井井有条——针对去年的员工和去年的问题。一个人的所有行动都以创新为导向的人将是一个天才——充满创意但无法与他人合作，或为他人组织工作。

A person whose actions are almost totally motivational might be a sales superstar or a charismatic politician who could sell any idea—if only she had one to sell. Someone whose actions are almost entirely organizational might be an incredibly efficient office manager who keeps things super-organized—for last year’s staff and last year’s problems. A person whose actions are all directed toward innovation would be a genius—full of ideas but unable to work with other people, or to organize work for others.

为了使领导风格有效，必须在激励、组织和创新之间取得某种平衡。我喜欢 MOI 模型，因为它强调我们都具备领导力的要素。在我们每个人身上，某些元素比其他元素发展得更好，但任何人都可以通过增强我们最薄弱元素的力量来提高领导者的水平。宇宙先生的肌肉并不比我多，只是比我发达。

In order for a leadership style to be effective, there has to be some balance among motivation, organization, and innovation. I like the MOI model because it emphasizes that we all contain the ingredients for leadership. In each of us, some elements are better developed than others, but anyone can improve as a leader simply by building the strength of our weakest elements. Mr. Universe doesn’t have more muscles than I do, just better developed ones.

技术领导者做什么

WHAT TECHNICAL LEADERS DO

在咨询任务和研讨会中，丹妮和我观察到成千上万的技术人员试图解决问题——程序员、管理人员、工程师、旅行社、护士、设计师、建筑商、医生、系统分析师、架构师和许多其他人。我们观察到许多领导者创造了一种环境，使人们有权解决问题。

In consulting assignments and workshops, Dani and I have observed thousands of technical people attempting to solve problems— programmers, administrators, engineers, travel agents, nurses, designers, builders, doctors, systems analysts, architects, and many others. We have observed many leaders who create an environment in which people are empowered to solve problems.

这些领导者中有些是很好的激励者，但有些不能激励狗去追猫。有些是出色的组织者，但有些在早上找不到一双匹配的袜子。所有最成功的技术领导者都通过他们对创新的重视以及以更好的方式做事来赋予人们权力。

Some of these leaders are good motivators, but some couldn’t motivate a dog to chase cats. Some are excellent organizers, but some can’t find a matching pair of socks in the morning. All of the most consistently successful technical leaders empower people by the value they place on innovation, on doing things in a better way.

如果我们更仔细地观察技术领导者如何强调创新，我们会发现他们专注于三个主要领域：

If we look more closely at how technical leaders emphasize innovation, we find that they concentrate on three major areas:

• 理解问题

• understanding the problem

• 管理思想流

• managing the flow of ideas

• 保持质量

• maintaining quality

这些功能构成了我们所谓的解决问题型领导风格的特征。这是最好的技术领导者的风格。

These functions are the ingredients that characterize what we call the problem-solving leadership style. This is the style that characterizes the best technical leaders.

当然，不同的领导者以不同的方式完成这三项职能，这取决于他们在激励、组织和创新方面的个人技能。引入新的测量工具以提高质量涉及创建工具（I 策略）；教人们使用它并说服他们尝试（M 策略）；并创建一个结构来支持那些使用该工具的人（0 策略）。

Of course, individual leaders accomplish these three functions in different ways, depending upon their personal skills in motivation, organization, and innovation. Introducing a new measurement tool to improve quality involves creating the tool (an I-strategy); teaching people to use it and convincing them to try it (M-strategies); and creating a structure for supporting those who use the tool (an 0-strategy).

设置头脑风暴会议以增加想法的流动涉及选择头脑风暴技术的有效变体（I 策略）；安排时间、地点和人员（0 策略）；以及教授技术，也许实际上促进会议（都是 M 策略）。

Setting up a brainstorming session to increase the flow of ideas involves selecting an effective variation of the brainstorming technique (an I-strategy); scheduling a time, place, and people (an 0-strategy); as well as teaching the technique and perhaps actually facilitating the meeting (both M-strategies).

毫无疑问，你有更喜欢的领导方法，就像每个厨师都有更喜欢的食谱一样。要成为解决问题的领导者，您不必放弃自己的长处。事实上，你甚至不应该考虑它。人们不是通过消除旧行为来提高绩效，而是通过添加新行为来提高绩效。

You undoubtedly have preferred approaches to leadership, just as every cook has preferred recipes. To become a problem-solving leader, you don’t have to abandon your strengths. In fact, you shouldn’t even consider it. People improve their performance not by amputating their old behaviors, but by adding new ones.

要成为解决问题的领导者，您不需要突然皈依宗教。你只需要检查那些你缺乏策略的目的/手段组合，然后一次一个地填补漏洞。随着你掌握的每一种新方法，你都会有另一个可用的选择，这会增加你对解决问题的环境产生积极影响的机会。最终，您会以某种神秘的方式注意到，您所在的团队变得更有效率了。

To become a problem-solving leader, you don’t need some sudden religious conversion. You merely need to examine those ends/means combinations where you lack strategies, then fill in the holes, one at a time. With each new approach you master, you’ll have another available choice, which increases your chances of being a positive influence on the problem-solving environment. Eventually, you’ll notice that in some mysterious way, the teams on which you work have become more productive.

相信更好的方式

FAITH IN A BETTER WAY

尽管他们的风格各不相同，但解决问题的领导者有一个共同点：相信总有更好的方法。

In spite of all their differences in style, problem-solving leaders have one thing in common: a faith that there’s always a better way.

这种信仰从何而来？伯特兰罗素曾经说过，信仰是对没有证据的事物的信仰。尽管解决问题的领导者可能是有逻辑的人，但他们不能用逻辑来支持他们的信仰。也许它起源于早年的一些成功：一个有好主意的孩子成功地将不愉快的情况变成了快乐的情况。这种成功加强了孩子对思想的信心。有了这种信念，孩子就更有可能尝试用聪明的主意解决下一个问题。熟能生巧，成功产生更大的成功，一个新的解决问题的领导者诞生了。

Where does such faith originate? Bertrand Russell once said that faith is the belief in something for which there is no proof. Though problem-solving leaders may be logical people, they cannot support their faith with logic. Perhaps it originates with some early success in life: A child with a bright idea succeeds in transforming an unpleasant situation into a happy one. This success reinforces the child’s faith in ideas. Armed with this faith, the child is more likely to try solving the next problem with a clever idea. Practice makes perfect, success produces even greater success, and a new problem-solving leader is made.

这种自我强化的循环并不适用于所有人。许多孩子从未体会过听到他们的想法之一时的狂喜，更不用说用来解决问题了。一段时间后，他们不再尝试处理想法。他们中的一些人长大后试图阻止其他人。

This self-reinforcing cycle doesn’t work for everyone. Many children have never known the ecstasy of having one of their ideas heard, let alone used to solve a problem. After a while, they stop trying to work with ideas. Some of them grow up trying to stop others.

根据威胁/奖励模型，世界上想法的数量是有限的，因此对于每个成功成为解决问题领导者的人来说，必须有一百个其他人失败。一个人要在上面，许多人必须在下面。也许这就是为什么这么多人警告我们高科技的危险。如果通过创新取得的进步是以牺牲多数人为代价的，那么解决问题的领导力就很难成为社会可以培养的榜样。

According to the threat/reward model, the number of ideas in the world is limited, so for each person who succeeds as a problem-solving leader, a hundred others must fail. For one to be on top, many others must be on the bottom. Perhaps that is why so many people are warning us of the dangers of high technology. If progress through innovation is only for the few at the expense of the many, then problem-solving leadership would hardly be a model for society to cultivate.

我自己的信念说确实有更好的方法，一种可以由一个人学习和实践而不伤害他人的方法。我也相信所有人都可以学习解决问题的领导风格，即使他们在儿童或成人时曾受挫。这就是我正在研究的问题，也是我写这本书的原因。

My own faith says that there really is a better way, a way that can be learned and practiced by one person without harm to others. I also believe that all people can learn the problem-solving leadership style, even if they were discouraged as children or adults. That’s the problem I’m working on, and that’s why I’ve written this book.

问题

QUESTIONS

  1. 您如何用 MOI 术语来描述自己？五年前的你是什么样的？
  2. How would you characterize yourself in MOI terms? What were you like five years ago?
  3. 您愿意为改变您的 MOI 档案做多少？您计划在未来五年采取哪些具体行动？明年？下个月？明天？今天？
  4. How much are you willing to do to change your MOI profile? What specific actions do you have planned for the next five years? next year? next month? tomorrow? today?
  5. 您能想到触发您的 MOI 概况发生令人满意的变化的具体事件吗？这些事件有什么共同点吗？您可以做些什么来增加此类事件的发生频率？
  6. Can you think of specific events that triggered an agreeable change in your MOI profile? Do these events have anything in common? What can you do to increase the frequency of such events?
  7. 您在工作中的 MOI 概况是否与工作以外的生活不同？这告诉你关于你自己的什么？
  8. Do you have a different MOI profile at work than you have in your life outside of work? What does this tell you about yourself?
  9. 你目前的领导风格是否有助于你的幸福？为了周围人的幸福？让世界变得更美好？
  10. Is your current leadership style contributing to your happiness? to the happiness of the people around you? to making the world a better place for everyone?
  11. 目前，您改变的主要动机是来自对奖励的承诺还是对惩罚的恐惧？这是最适合您的模式吗？如果没有，您可以做些什么来获得更多的其他类型？完全是其他类型的动机怎么样，比如自我价值感的增强？
  12. At the moment, does your principal motivation for change come from promise of reward or fear of punishment? Is this the best mode for you? If not, what can you do to get more of the other kind? How about some other kind of motivation entirely, such as an increased sense of self-worth?

第 3 章解决问题的方式

Chapter 3. A Problem-Solving Style

“请你告诉我，我应该从这里走哪条路？”

“Would you tell me, please, which way I ought to go from here?”

“这在很大程度上取决于你想去哪里，”猫说。

“That depends a good deal on where you want to get to,” said the Cat.

“我不太关心在哪里——”爱丽丝说。

“I don’t much care where—” said Alice.

“那么你走哪条路都没有关系，”猫说。

“Then it doesn’t matter which way you go,” said the Cat.

“——只要我到达某个地方，”爱丽丝补充道作为解释。 *

“—so long as I get somewhere,” Alice added as an explanation.*

“哦，你肯定会那样做，”猫说，“只要你走得够久。”

“Oh, you’re sure to do that,” said the Cat, “if you only walk long enough.”

——刘易斯·卡罗尔，《爱丽丝梦游仙境》

—Lewis Carroll, Alice in Wonderland

成功的技术领导者采用我们称之为解决问题领导力的一般风格。他们专注于创新过程，主要通过三种方式进行：

Successful technical leaders employ a general style that we call problem-solving leadership. They focus on the process of innovation, and they do so in three major ways:

• 理解问题

• understanding the problem

• 管理思想流

• managing the flow of ideas

• 保持质量

• maintaining quality

在本章中，我们将探讨每个类别中的行动，以及领导者如何使用激励、组织或信息手段最终以更好的方式解决问题。

In this chapter, we’ll look at actions in each of these categories, and how leader’s may use motivational, organizational, or informational means to accomplish, in the end, a better way of solving the problem.

了解问题

UNDERSTANDING THE PROBLEM

有很多技术人员非常喜欢流浪，就像爱丽丝梦游仙境一样，他们不在乎去哪里，只要到达某个地方就可以了。计算机程序员称此过程为“黑客攻击”。苏是一名痴迷于创意的技术工作者，但她对自己的工作与外界的世界缺乏任何联系感。

There are many technical workers who enjoy wandering so much that, like Alice in Wonderland, they don’t much care where they go, so long as they get somewhere. Computer programmers call this process “hacking.” Sue is a technical worker who is obsessed with ideas, but she lacks any sense of connection between her work and the world outside.

她并不是特别想了解手头的问题；她唯一的目标是探索有趣的事物。如果她破解的时间足够长，她肯定会找到一些有趣的东西。

She doesn’t especially want to understand the problem at hand; her only goal is to explore interesting things. If she hacks long enough, she is sure to find something interesting.

像 Sue 这样的黑客可以成为解决问题的最佳团队成员——只要他们在一个有限的环境中进行黑客攻击，在这个环境中所有参与者都清楚地了解他们想要完成的事情。没有那个有限的环境，就会有很多黑客攻击，但事情只是偶然发生的。以下是我们通常看到的一些具体行动，这些行动创造了一种每个人都能理解问题的环境。

Hackers like Sue can make some of the best problem-solving team members—as long as they hack within a limited environment, one in which all participants clearly understand what they’re trying to accomplish. Without that limited environment, there’s a lot of hacking, but things get done only by accident. Here are some specific actions we commonly see that create the kind of environment in which everyone understands the problem.

仔细阅读规范。成功或失败往往取决于问题定义的微小差异。尽管有必要对问题进行概述，但大局往往取决于一个关键细节。解决问题的领导者认识到这一点并注意这些细节。相比之下，黑客会变得无聊，并希望在他们找到似乎可行的解决方案后立即赶往其他事情。对于最糟糕的黑客类型，解决方案的最终用户只是一个麻烦。

Read the specifications very carefully. Success or failure often turns on minuscule differences in problem definitions. Although it is necessary to have an overview of the problem, the big picture often turns on one critical detail. Problem-solving leaders recognize this and pay attention to such details. Hackers, by contrast, become bored and want to rush on to something else the instant they have a solution that seems to work. To the worst type of hacker, the ultimate user of the solution is merely a nuisance.

我记得一个要求 99.9% 可用性的计算机系统的投标，要满足这个要求既困难又昂贵。然而，其中一位设计工程师注意到公司对“可用性”的定义与工程师们所相信的并不完全一致。事实证明，如果公司至少提前一小时得到通知，则关闭系统是可以接受的，这使工程师能够设计错误检测方案，而不是错误预防方案。差额约为 400 万美元，但其中两名工程师仍想构建防错系统，因为这是一个更有趣的技术问题。他们不知道谁会支付额外的四百万美元，他们也不在乎。

I recall a bid for a computer system that called for 99.9 percent availability, a difficult and expensive requirement to meet. One of the design engineers, however, noticed that the company’s definition of “availability” was not quite what the engineers had believed. It proved to be acceptable to bring the system down if the company was notified at least an hour in advance, which enabled the engineers to design an error-detection scheme, rather than an error-prevention scheme. The difference was worth about four million dollars, but two of the engineers still wanted to build the error-prevention system because it was a more interesting technical problem. They had no idea who would pay the extra four million dollars, and they didn’t really care.

鼓励队友非常仔细地阅读规范。阅读规范显然是信息性的，但鼓励他人这样做是动机驱动的领导。当几句话可能造成 400 万美元的差异时，没有一双眼睛足够可靠。在我们的技术审查工作（组织特别会议以发现技术错误）中，我们已经看到通过有效的小组工作发现了数以万计的规范错误。有效解决问题的领导者知道如何组织环境，让所有人的眼睛都能全神贯注地工作。

Encourage teammates to read the specifications very carefully. Reading specifications is clearly informational, but encouraging others to do so is leadership by motivation. No one pair of eyes is sufficiently reliable when a few words may make a four million dollar difference. In our work with technical reviews (special meetings organized to catch technical errors), we have seen tens of thousands of specification errors detected by effective group work. Effective problem-solving leaders know how to organize the environment so that all eyes are operating at full power.

通过回顾原始问题来解决争论。除非团队的所有成员都对问题有共同的理解，否则解决问题的尝试只会浪费大量精力。大多数旷日持久的争论不是关于解决方案的相对价值，而是关于对问题的不同理解。解决问题的领导者能够读懂这些迹象，判断一个论点是基于问题定义的差异还是基于解决方法的差异。

Resolve arguments by referring back to the original problem. Unless and until all members of a team have a common understanding of the problem, attempts to solve the problem are just so much wasted energy. Most prolonged arguments are not over the relative value of the solution, but over different understandings of the problem. Problem- solving leaders are able to read the signs that tell whether an argument is based on a difference in problem definition or a difference in solution method.

向客户寻求有关规范的说明和其他信息。没有一个有价值的项目被完整和正确地描述过，即使是在书面文件中也是如此，但是有些人宁愿直接投入到他们所拥有的东西中，也不愿与其他人互动。有时，微不足道的互动可以真正带来回报；上周，我的旅行社打电话询问我是否真的需要在复杂的行程中确定具体的出发时间。因为她不怕花一分钟时间问，所以她得到了特价机票，为我节省了 450 多美元。

Seek clarifications and additional information about the specifications from the customer. No worthwhile project is ever described fully and correctly, even in a written document, but some people would rather plunge right in with what they have than interact with other people. Sometimes a trivial interaction can truly pay off; last week, my travel agent phoned to find out if I really needed a specific departure time on a complex itinerary. Because she wasn’t afraid to take one minute to ask, she got a special fare that saved me more than $450.

工作进行一段时间后，再参考规范，此时可以更好地理解某些要求的含义。复杂的问题从来没有从一开始就被理解，但我们常常认为它们是，这是通往灾难的必经之路。这就是为什么我们必须鼓励不断重新检查关于问题的假设。

Refer back to the specifications after work has proceeded for a while, when the implications of some of the requirements can be better understood. Complex problems are never understood right from the beginning, but we often think they are, which is a sure road to disaster. That’s why we must encourage constant re-examination of assumptions about the problem.

一位建筑商注意到装饰材料规格中的“等效”一词，从而在一栋公寓楼上节省了 33,000 美元。一位医生通过重读体检记录并注意到当时似乎无关紧要的症状挽救了一条生命。有效的领导者会在他们的工作中不断测试他们自己的理解。他们很自信，但对自己的智力局限性很现实。

A builder saved $33,000 on an apartment building by noticing the word “equivalent” in the specifications for finishing materials. A doctor saved a life by rereading the record of a physical examination and noticing a symptom that seemed irrelevant at the time. Effective leaders build continuous testing of their own understanding into their work. They are self-confident, but realistic about their own intellectual limitations.

管理思想的流动

MANAGING THE FLOW OF IDEAS

想法是解决问题的领导力的核心；它们是我们从问题定义到高质量解决方案的方法。想法太少意味着根本没有解决方案；太多的想法意味着混乱。没有领导来管理思想的流动，同一个房间里的两个技术专家进行争论，三个人聚集在一起，四个人聚集在一起。通过有效的想法管理，任何数量的人都能成为一个成功的解决问题的团队。以下是解决问题的领导者用来管理思想流的十二种典型行动。

Ideas are at the center of problem-solving leadership; they are the method by which we go from a definition of the problem to a high-quality solution. Too few ideas means no solution at all; too many ideas means chaos. Without leadership to manage the flow of ideas, two technical experts in the same room make an argument, three make a crowd, and four make a mob. With effective management of ideas, any number makes a successful problem-solving team. Here are twelve typical actions that problem-solving leaders use to manage the flow of ideas.

为团队贡献一个聪明的想法。虽然这是最明显的领导动作，虽然新点子有时很关键，但真正的新点子其实很少。几千年前，亚里士多德说：“同一个思想出现在世界上不是一次，也不是两次，而是无数次。” 在与高科技组织合作的三十年里，我看到的真正原创的想法还不到十个。例如，几乎所有计算机软件技术的新思想都是由查尔斯·巴贝奇 (Charles Babbage) 在一个多世纪前提出的。比聪明的新想法更重要的是创造一个环境，在这个环境中，解决问题的正确想法出现时会得到认可。

Contribute a clever idea to the team. Although this is the most obvious leadership action, and although new ideas are sometimes critical, there are actually very few truly new ideas. Several thousand years ago, Aristotle said, “It is not once, nor twice, but times without number that the same idea makes its appearance in the world.” In three decades of working with high-tech organizations, I’ve seen fewer than ten truly original ideas. Virtually all of the new ideas underlying computer software technology, for instance, were put forth by Charles Babbage more than a century ago. More important than the clever new idea is creating an environment where the right idea for solving the problem will be recognized when it comes along.

鼓励复制有用的想法。解决问题的领导者是根深蒂固的模仿者，尽管有些人不愿承认这一点。最好的人不仅承认它，而且将其培养为一门艺术。正如亚里士多德所理解的那样，大多数“新”想法实际上是来自其他背景的想法的副本，解决问题的领导者不断地在其他背景中寻找他们可以使用的想法。最好的老师永远不会停止研究同事的课本、讲座和练习。最好的计算机程序员在可以将旧程序用于新工作时绝不会编写新程序。最好的电路设计师知道哪些设计已经存在，以及它们是否可以用于不同的情况。解决问题的领导者对自己或其他人已经做好的事情再做一遍不感兴趣。

Encourage copying of useful ideas. Problem-solving leaders are inveterate copiers, though some do not like to admit it. The best ones not only admit it, they cultivate it as a fine art. As Aristotle understood, most “new” ideas are actually copies of ideas from other contexts, and problem-solving leaders are constantly searching other contexts for ideas they can use. The best teachers never cease to study the texts, lectures, and exercises of their colleagues. The best computer programmers never write a new program when they can use an old one for a new job. The best circuit designers know what designs already exist, and whether they can be used in different situations. Problem-solving leaders are not interested in doing again what has already been done well, by themselves or someone else.

详细阐述队友贡献的想法。没有一个想法在刚形成时是完美的；即使是复制的想法也必须适应新的环境。大多数解决问题的领导者花在完善想法上的精力是提出想法的一百倍。这就是爱迪生所说的“天才是百分之一的灵感加上百分之九十九的汗水”的意思。

Elaborate on an idea that a teammate contributed. No idea is perfect when it is first formed; even copied ideas must be adapted to new circumstances. Most problem-solving leaders devote a hundred times more energy to perfecting ideas than to proposing them. This is what Edison meant when he said, “Genius is one percent inspiration and ninety-nine percent perspiration.”

放弃自己的想法以支持团队想要开发的想法，并且在每个人都理解之前拒绝放弃一个想法。这些是解决任何复杂问题的阴阳。大的问题需要很多人的共同努力才能和谐共处。然而，团队合作的需要会产生与大多数人同行的巨大压力，如果大多数人坚持错误的想法，这可能会造成灾难性的后果。

Drop one’s own idea in favor of an idea the team wants to develop, and Refuse to let an idea drop until everyone understands it. These are the yin and yang of solving any complex problem. Large problems require the joint effort of many people working in harmony. However, the need for teamwork produces enormous pressures to go along with the majority, which can prove disastrous if the majority is stuck on an incorrect idea.

放弃所有想法或拒绝放弃任何想法都相对容易。难的是要取得平衡：当你只是自负时放手，但当其他人犯了致命错误时要坚持下去。我特别记得一位景观设计师，他是开发团队的一员，当他最喜欢的游乐场设计理念与项目的其余部分不相符时，他慷慨地放弃了。我的第一印象是他软弱无力，但后来他反对某张幻灯片。尽管他以一敌七，但他还是坚持了下来，直到有人终于明白为什么滑梯对儿童会有危险。

It’s relatively easy to let all your ideas drop, or to refuse to drop any of them. What’s hard is to strike a balance: to let go when you’re merely being egotistical, but to hold on when the rest of the group is plunging ahead with a fatal mistake. I particularly remember one landscape architect, part of a development team, who graciously let go of his favorite playground design concept when it didn’t fit with the rest of the project. My first impression was that he was weak and wishy-washy, but later he objected to a particular slide. Although he was one against seven, he persisted until someone else finally understood why the slide would be dangerous to children.

抗拒时间压力，花时间听别人解释他们的想法。景观设计师的队友值得称赞，他们花时间了解为什么滑梯是一个安全问题。在时间压力下，大多数想法在真正被理解之前就被放弃了，尽管他们中的一些人会节省足够的时间来为尝试理解坏想法一百次而付出代价。即使情况并非如此，当他们的想法因错误的原因而被放弃时，人们往往会失去对项目的奉献精神。最后，在人们倾听所有想法的环境中，项目进展得更快，即使这些想法被证明是不适用的。

Resist time pressure, and take the time to listen when other people explain their ideas. The landscape architect’s teammates deserve credit for taking time to understand why the slide was a safety problem. Under time pressure, most ideas get dropped before they’re actually understood, even though some of them would save enough time to pay for trying to understand the bad ideas a hundred times over. Even if this weren’t so, people tend to lose their dedication to a project when their ideas are dropped for the wrong reason. In the end, projects go faster in an environment where people listen to all ideas, even if the ideas turn out to be inapplicable.

测试其他人提供的想法。在任何给定的情况下，绝大多数的想法都是没有用的，但哪些是有用的呢？像 IBM 和通用电气这样的高科技公司拥有大型研究实验室，但它们的产品中很少有来自它们自己实验室的研究成果。研究人员的主要工作是紧跟各自领域的发展，批判性地分析每一项发展对公司的潜在利益。当一个想法看起来不错时，他们就会准备好迅速抓住它并使它变得更好。

Test ideas contributed by other people. In any given situation, the vast majority of ideas are not useful, but which ones are useful? High-tech companies like IBM and General Electric maintain large research laboratories, but few of their products originate in the research from their own labs. The researchers’ principal job is to stay on top of developments in their field, critically analyzing each one for its potential benefit to the company. When an idea looks good, they then are prepared to seize it quickly and make it better.

不要对队友的想法进行快速批评，以保持想法的流动。尽管测试很重要，但很少有想法如此危险，以至于我们不能在重新考虑我们对它们的最初反应所需的片刻中存活下来。批评是一回事；快速批评是另一个。高科技公司经常拒绝重要的想法，甚至在一些较小的公司证明它们可以付诸实践之前多次拒绝。例如，1948 年，IBM 决定不进入计算机业务，因为市场太小。使 IBM 成为当今计算机行业的主导力量的并不是第一，而是能够在其他人的测试证明这些想法可行后重新考虑早期的拒绝。

Withhold quick criticism of teammates’ ideas, in order to keep the ideas flowing. Although testing is crucial, few ideas are so dangerous they can’t be allowed to live for the few moments it takes to reconsider our initial reaction to them. Criticism is one thing; quick criticism is another. High- tech companies often reject important ideas, several times even, before some smaller company proves they can work in practice. In 1948, for example, IBM decided not to enter the computer business because the market was too small. What has made IBM the dominant force in the computer business today was not being first, but being able to reconsider early rejections after testing by others proved the ideas viable.

当你必须批评一个想法时，要明确你是在批评这个想法，而不是提出这个想法的人。解决问题的领导者很清楚并不是每个想法对每个问题都有用，但他们更清楚每个人都是有用的。他们知道像“这是一个愚蠢的想法”或“你真的不能相信”这样的评论往往会阻止进一步的贡献，所以他们以一种关心的方式提出批评。这意味着他们注意自己的用词选择，只批评思想，不批评人。

When you must criticize an idea, make clear that you are criticizing the idea, not the person who offered the idea. Problem-solving leaders are well aware that not every idea is useful for every problem, but they are even more aware that every person is useful. They know that remarks like “that’s a stupid idea,” or “you can’t really believe that,” tend to discourage further contributions, so they offer their criticisms in a caring way. This means that they pay attention to their choice of words, and criticize only ideas, never people.

在提供之前测试您自己的想法。解决问题的领导者的流行形象是一个聪明的年轻人，以每分钟两百字的速度倾诉聪明的年轻想法。通过计算“影响力”来衡量，这些人可能在领导力方面得分很高，但他们很少是真正的解决问题的领导者。恰恰相反。当被问到为什么他们说这么多时，这些喋喋不休的人通常会说：“嗯，没有其他人可以贡献什么。” 这是无稽之谈。没有人聪明到可以拥有所有的好想法，不断喋喋不休地说出你自己未经考虑的想法是阻止其他人想法的好方法。

Test your own ideas before offering them. The popular image of the problem-solving leader is a bright young person pouring out bright young ideas at two hundred words per minute. Such people may score high in leadership as measured by counting “acts of influence,” but they are rarely the true problem-solving leaders. Quite the contrary. When asked why they talk so much, these babblers will often remark, “Well, nobody else had anything to contribute.” This is nonsense. Nobody is bright enough to have all the good ideas, and a constant babble of your own unconsidered ideas is an excellent way to discourage other people’s ideas.

当时间和劳动力所剩无几时，停止研究新想法，投入其中。每个项目都会有一段时间，你必须真正完成工作，因为如果到那时你没有足够的想法，你就不会无论如何完成项目。一些未来的领导者对自己的形象如此夸张，以至于他们不能屈服于单纯的实施工作，但即使是上帝也会在六天后停止思考新物种。

When time and labor are running short, stop working on new ideas and just pitch in. There comes a time in every project when you have to actually do the work, because if you don’t have enough ideas by then, you won’t finish the project anyway. Some would-be leaders have such an inflated image of themselves that they cannot stoop to mere implementation work, but even God quit thinking up new species after six days.

鼓励团队放弃先前成功但无法扩展到新情况的想法。放弃你的坏主意已经够难的了，但你的好主意就是你的存货。然而，每一个伟大的想法都有其局限性。如果你每天必须吃三遍，即使是香蕉奶油派也会感到厌烦。

Encourage the team to drop ideas that had succeeded earlier, but cannot be extended to the new situation. It’s hard enough to let go of your bad ideas, but your good ideas are your stock-in-trade. Yet every great idea has its limits. Even banana cream pie gets tiresome if you have to eat it three times a day.
