It almost always helps, but as powerful as this transformation method is, it’s not flawless. We all have the ability to forget things.

我发现在转换完成后将步骤写在我的日记中很有帮助。然后，当我有机会练习时，我可以回到日记中看看我做得如何。这实现了我对潜意识做出的承诺，并承认我并不完美。例如，我可能会发现我想修改其中一个特定条件，或对其进行澄清。

I find it helpful, once the transformation is complete, to have the steps written down in my journal. Then, when I’ve had a chance to practice, I can come back to the journal and see how well I’m doing. This fulfills the promise I made to my unconscious, and acknowledges that I’m not perfect. I may find, for instance, that I want to revise one of the particular conditions, or clarify it.

例如，经过一些经验，我可以进一步具体化陈述，

For instance, after some experience, I may be able to further particularize the statement,

我很适合帮助他们。

It fits me to help them.

进入

into

*我们两个可以达成一个公开的、明确的、有限的帮助合同，

*The two of us can arrive at an open, explicit, and limited contract for help,

我对合同感觉很好。*

and I feel good about the contract.*

对其他人产生真正的兴趣

BECOMING GENUINELY INTERESTED IN OTHER PEOPLE

卡内基的另一项原则很简单：

Another of Carnegie’s principles is a simple one:

“真正对他人感兴趣。”

“Become genuinely interested in other people.”

没有这种真正的兴趣，任何行为，比如微笑、记住对方的名字，或者让对方觉得自己很重要，都将只是虚伪的噱头。我现在意识到，在我十岁的时候，我已经制定了一套生存规则，阻止我对其他人产生真正的兴趣。当卡内基说“微笑”时，我无法认真对待。我知道不真诚的微笑是什么样子，我不想参与其中。我不想记住我不喜欢的人的名字，也不想听别人谈论自己，也不想把我的谈话与他们的兴趣联系起来。

Without this genuine interest, any action, such as smiling, remembering the other person’s name, or making the person feel important, will be mere hypocritical gimmicks. I realize now that by the time I was ten I had developed a set of survival rules that prevented me from being genuinely interested in other people. When Carnegie said “Smile,” I couldn’t take it seriously. I knew what an insincere smile looked like, and I wanted no part of it. I didn’t want to remember the name of someone I didn’t like, nor listen to people talking about themselves, nor try to relate my conversation to their interests.

最重要的是，我不想让他们觉得自己很重要，因为在内心深处，我并不觉得自己很重要。卡内基专注于他人，但正如弗吉尼亚·萨提亚 (Virginia Satir) 所说，“自我价值是我们整个存在的中心。” 戴尔·卡内基可能没有注意到这一点，因为他似乎对自己的自我价值有一种强烈的发展和不容置疑的看法。此外，他似乎有一个关于“自私”的生存法则，正如他赞同这条狗没有别有用心的声明所证明的那样。我知道我的狗爱我，但我对它们想要哄骗我喂狗粮的愿望不抱任何幻想，如果可以的话。

Most of all, I didn’t want to make them feel important because deep down, I didn’t feel very important myself. Carnegie concentrated on others, but as Virginia Satir says, “Self-worth is at the center of our whole existence.” Dale Carnegie may have missed this point because he seems to have had a strongly developed and unquestioned view of his own self-worth. Also, he seems to have had a survival rule about “selfishness,” as evidenced by his approving statement that the dog has no ulterior motives. I know that my dogs love me, but I have no illusions about their desire to coax doggie treats out of me, if they can.

我们中的许多人都有一个元规则，它说，

Many of us carry a meta-rule that says,

不要自私。

Don’t be selfish.

由于这个元规则，如果我们花时间以任何方式发展自己，我们会感到内疚，无论是阅读杂志、锻炼、改变我们的生存规则，甚至只是思考一个特定的对话。但要成为解决问题的领导者——即赋予他人权力——我们必须在这些方面“自私”。正如精神病学家纳撒尼尔·布兰登 (Nathaniel Branden) 观察到的那样，

Because of this meta-rule, we feel guilty if we take time to develop ourselves in any way, be it reading a magazine, exercising, transforming our survival rules, or even just thinking about a particular conversation. But to become a problem-solving leader—that is, to empower other people—we must be “selfish” in just these ways. As the psychiatrist Nathaniel Branden observed,

如果一个人回顾人类进步的历史，回顾将我们从洞穴带到我们现在的文明水平的所有步骤，以及使这一进步成为可能的天才、大胆、勇气和创造力——一个人不禁会被震撼事实上，我们对那些一生主要致力于发现和实现自己的“命运”的人——艺术家、科学家、哲学家、发明家、实业家，他们的人生道路显然是自我实现（自我发展、自我实现）。[Branden，《浪漫爱情心理学》（洛杉矶：IP Tarcher, Inc.，1980 年），第 55-56 页。]

If one looks at the history of human progress, at all the steps which have brought us from the cave to our present level of civilization, and of the genius, daring, courage, and creativity that made this progress possible—one cannot help be struck by the fact of how much we owe to those whose lives were primarily given over to the task of discovering and fulfilling their own “destiny”—the artists, the scientists, the philosophers, the inventors, the industrialists whose life path was clearly one of self-actualization (self-development, self-fulfillment). [Branden, The Psychology of Romantic Love (Los Angeles: I.P. Tarcher, Inc., 1980), pp. 55-56.]

为什么以及何时应该阅读 DALE CARNEGIE

WHY AND WHEN YOU SHOULD READ DALE CARNEGIE

如果您已经拥有良好的自尊，您可以通过阅读如何赢得朋友和影响他人来学习如何成为有效的激励者。您还可以将卡内基的书用作自尊测试。如果你做出消极反应，就像我十岁时所做的那样，你内心深处的某个地方有一条生存法则，以一种或另一种形式，

If you already have well-developed self-esteem, you can learn a great deal about being an effective motivator by reading How to Win Friends and Influence People. You can also use Carnegie’s book as a test of self-esteem. If you react negatively, as I did at age ten, somewhere deep inside you have a survival rule that says, in one form or another,

我不值钱。

I’m not worth much.

如果你有这种感觉，它就会表现出来，就像一只经常被鞭打一次的狗身上表现出来的那样。

If you feel that way, it will show, just as it shows on a dog that has been whipped once too often.

这样的狗不会像卡内基描述的那样迎接你。它不爱自己，也没有特别的理由去爱人类。因此，即使它用狗的诡计来吸引你，你也不太愿意给它款待。出于同情，有些人会款待被鞭打的狗，但这真的是你想要影响他人的方式吗？

Such a dog doesn’t greet you the way Carnegie describes. It doesn’t love itself, and it has no particular reason to love human beings. So even if it makes a feeble attempt to charm you with its doggy wiles, you’re not too inclined to give it a treat. Some people will give a treat to a whipped dog, out of pity, but is that really the way you want to influence others?

如果你想学会激励他人，最好的方法就是改变你的生存法则，让你觉得自己像被鞭打的狗一样一文不值、无能为力。你可以从把“我不值钱”变成一个明智的指南开始，比如

If you want to learn to motivate others, the best way is to transform your survival rules that make you feel as worthless and powerless as a whipped dog. You might start by transforming “I’m not worth much” into a sensible guide, such as

我和其他所有人一样珍贵。

I’m exactly as precious as every other human being.

它确实有效，没有噱头。

It really works, without gimmicks.

问题

QUESTIONS

  1. 当您意识到这些规则时，请将您的日记用作记录您的生存规则的地方。确定您的生存规则之一并将其转化为指南。
  2. Use your journal as a place for recording your survival rules as you become aware of them. Identify one of your survival rules and transform it into a guide.
  3. 在尝试进行前面的练习时，您是否遇到任何元规则？如果是这样，请将其转换为元指南。
  4. In attempting to do the previous exercise, did you encounter any meta-rule? If so, transform it into a meta-guide.
  5. 阅读 Dale Carnegie 的《如何赢得朋友和影响他人》，找出适合您的规则。将它们转化为指南。
  6. Read Dale Carnegie’s How to Win Friends and Influence People and identify what rules turn up for you. Transform them into guides.
  7. 作为领导者，您可能会发现自己想要帮助人们将他们的规则转化为指南。在你深入了解这种帮助之前，找一个可以交换规则列表的朋友，并互相帮助将其中的一些转化为指南。
  8. As a leader, you may find yourself wanting to help people transform their rules into guides. Before you get too far into this kind of helping, find a friend with whom you can exchange lists of rules, and help each other transform some of them into guides.

第 14 章权力从何而来

Chapter 14. Where Power Comes From

即使在战争中，道德力量也占身体力量的四分之三。- 拿破仑

Even in war moral power is to physical as three parts out of four. - Napoleon

许多人发现很难接受影响他人不是问题的想法，一旦他们有自己的自尊。缺乏力量的人往往相信，只要别人给他们一些缺少的成分，一把秘钥，他们就会突然变得强大。这是一个危险的想法，主要是因为它蒙蔽了他们的双眼，阻碍了他们增加影响力的道路。这甚至可能导致他们在生活中做出一些改变时失去他们仅有的一点权力，比如担任领导职务。

Many people find it difficult to accept the idea that influencing other is not a problem, once they have their own self-esteem in order. People who lack power tend to believe that if only someone else would give them some missing ingredient, a secret key, they would suddenly become powerful. This is a dangerous idea, mostly because it blinds them and blocks their road to increasing their influence. It may even cause them to lose what little power they have when they make some change in their life, like assuming a leadership position.

在本章中，我们将探讨解决问题的领导者需要了解的关于权力的一些事情，尤其是权力从何而来和去向何方。

In this chapter, we’ll explore some of the things a problem-solving leader needs to know about power, especially where it comes from and where it goes.

权力作为一种关系

POWER AS A RELATIONSHIP

权力的起源既有争议又难以捉摸。毛子东（1938年11月6日在党的六届六中全会上的总结讲话）说，一切力量都来自枪杆子，但拿破仑估计只有百分之二十五。然而，在没有大炮的情况下，每个人似乎都不同意动力从何而来。

The origin of power is both controversial and slippery. Mao Zidong (concluding speech at the Sixth Plenary Session of the Sixth Central Committee of the Party, November 6, 1938) said that all power comes from the barrel of a gun, but Napoleon estimated that only twenty-five percent does. In the absence of artillery, however, everyone seems to disagree on where power comes from.

我记得有一次从一个乏味的计划会议中走出来，因为我感到无能为力。会后主席到我办公室找我对质，指责我滥用职权。无论发生什么事，他都没有勇气站起来离开会议。对他来说，我的离开意味着我拥有了难以想象的力量，而对我来说，这意味着我的无能为力。对我来说，他被任命为主席意味着他显然是拥有所有权力的人。

I recall once walking out of a tedious planning meeting because I felt powerless to accomplish anything. After the meeting, the chairman confronted me in my office and accused me of irresponsible use of power. He would never have the nerve to stand up and leave a meeting, no matter what was happening. To him, my leaving meant I possessed unimaginable power, while to me it meant I was powerless. To me, his being appointed chairman meant he was obviously the one who had all the power.

我们都错了，因为我们都认为权力是我们“拥有”的东西。权力不是占有，而是一种关系。由于我与任命他的组织的关系，我认为主席很有权力。我依赖于组织。能夺走我的生计，一定很厉害。我越不依赖，这个组织看起来就越不强大。我不觉得全国轮滑协会是一个强大的组织，但是，那么，我不滑冰。

We were both wrong, because we both thought power was something we “possess.” Power is not a possession, but a relationship. I saw the chairman as powerful because of my relationship to the organization that had appointed him. I was dependent on the organization. It could take away my livelihood, so it must be powerful. The less dependent I was, the less powerful the organization would seem. I don’t feel that the National Roller Derby Association is a powerful organization, but, then, I don’t skate.

董事长觉得我很有力量，因为他把自己的情况投射到我身上，就好像我是电影屏幕一样。当我的行为方式需要他的权力时，他断定我是一个有权势的人。如果一个女人在同样的情况下离开会议，他可能会认为她是“软弱的”。他可能不会把她当做一个屏幕来投射他对女性的刻板印象，而不是亲自认同她。

The chairman felt I was powerful because he projected his own situation onto me, as if I were a movie screen. When I acted in a way that would have required power from him, he concluded that I was a powerful person. If a woman had left the meeting in the same situation, he might have seen her as “weak.” Instead of identifying with her personally, he might have used her as a screen upon which to project one of his female stereotypes.

科技力量

POWER FROM TECHNOLOGY

技术领导者对权力有自己独特的看法。我特别记得我们一群人在看电影前吃晚饭时发生的争吵。“权力来自地位，”奥斯汀第十次争论道。“在我晋升之前，我无法在我的组织中实现目标。”

Technical leaders have their own special view of power. I especially recall an argument when a group of us were having dinner before a movie. “Power comes from position,” Austin argued for the tenth time. “Until my promotion, I couldn’t make things happen in my organization.”

“不是这样的，”凯文说，“在我没有升职之前，我真的可以凭借我的技术来完成一些事情。现在我什至不能使用它。”

“Not so,” Kevan said, “Before I was promoted, I could really accomplish things because of my technical skill. Now I can’t even use that.”

“我不同意你们两个，”伊娜贝尔说。“落井下石的时候，技术可能会有帮助，但除非你有个人实力，否则晋升到主管级别也无济于事。”

“I disagree with both of you,” said Inabelle. “Technical skill may help when you’re down in the pits, but unless you have personal power, promotion into the supervisory ranks won’t do anything.”

“听着，”我打断道，“我要用我个人的力量来叫暂停。如果我们不快点，我们看电影就要迟到了。”

“Listen,” I interrupted, “I’m going to use some of my personal power to call a time out. If we don’t hurry, we’ll be late for the movie.”

这部电影是 LT.，一个外星人与地球人相遇的故事。电影开始时，我无法摆脱权力的话题，这一定影响了我看待 ET 困境的方式。当他的宇宙飞船匆忙离开地球时，外星人意外落在了后面，这是无能为力的完美象征。

The movie was LT., the tale of one extraterrestrial’s encounter with Earthlings. As the movie began, I couldn’t get my mind off the subject of power, which must have influenced the way I saw E.T.’s predicament. When his spaceship makes a hasty departure from Earth, E.T. is accidentally left behind, the perfect symbol of powerlessness.

ET是裸体的。他没有工具。他迷失在离家数光年的陌生环境中。这一切已经够糟糕了，但人们不会放过他。整个美国政府都决心抓住外星人，这样他就可以像实验室青蛙一样被解剖了。情节就这样设定了：地球上最伟大的国家与一个迷失的、赤裸的、长相奇怪的小生物之间的权力斗争。

E. T. is naked. He has no tools. He’s lost in an alien environment light-years from home. All this is bad enough, but people won’t leave him alone. The entire United States government is determined to capture E. T. so he can be dissected like a laboratory frog. And so the plot is set: a power struggle between the greatest nation on Earth and one lost, naked, strange-looking small creature.

ET 不是悬疑片。从一开始，我就愿意和我的占星师打赌，政府从来没有机会。我知道这一点，观众中的每个孩子都知道这一点。这部电影之所以如此有趣，是因为政府中没有人知道这一点。

E.T. is not a suspense movie. Right from the beginning, I was willing to bet my astrogator that the government never had a chance. I knew that, and every kid in the audience knew that. What made the movie so much fun was that nobody in the government knew that.

电影结束后，我们讨论了悬念的角度。奥斯汀很困惑。“你怎么知道 ET 会赢？我认为政府拥有所有权力。”

After the movie, we discussed the suspense angle. Austin was perplexed. “How did you know E. T. would win? I thought the government had all the power.”

“不反对 ET 的个人权力，”Inabelle 回答道。

“Not against E.T.’s personal power,” Inabelle replied.

“不是个人力量，”凯冯纠正道。等。有过人的技术。

“Not personal power,” Kevan corrected. “ET. had a superior technology.

“个人实力？技术？我会称之为魔术！这是不现实的。”

“Personal power? Technology? I’d call it magic! It was unrealistic.”

“并非不切实际，”我说，“只是面目全非。”

“Not unrealistic,” I said, “merely unrecognizable.”

“你是什么意思？”

“What do you mean?”

“这叫做克拉克第三定律：任何足够先进的技术都与魔法无异。”

“It’s called Clarke’s Third Law: Any sufficiently advanced technology is indistinguishable from magic.”

凯文打断了他的话。“就像经理和程序员一样。对我的经理来说，我的技术工作简直就是魔法。”

Kevan interrupted with a clarification. “It’s just like managers and programmers. To my manager, my technical work is pure magic.”

“嗯，反之亦然，”奥斯汀辩解说。“我们经理有很大的组织权力，这是你们程序员所不了解的。我们可以调动资源来完成任务。你可别小看它！”

“Well, it works the other way, too,” Austin defended. “We managers have lots of organizational power, which you programmers don’t understand. We can mobilize resources to get things done. And don’t you underestimate it!”

“噢，你听起来就像电影里那些官僚一样。”

“Aw, you sound just like those bureaucrats in the movie.”

“不要点名，”我推荐道。“奥斯汀和他的经理们感到很沮丧，因为程序员不遵守游戏规则——他们的权力游戏。程序员不是在权力斗争中，他们只是想写程序。ET不是在争权夺利，他只是想回家。一旦 ET 决定他必须回家，政府就无能为力了。”

“No name calling,” I refereed. “Austin and his managers are frustrated because the programmers don’t play by the rules of the game—their power game. The programmers aren’t in a power struggle, they just want to write programs. E.T. is not in a power struggle, he just wants to go home. Once E.T. decides he has to go home, the government is powerless.”

“但是程序员的力量从何而来？” 奥斯汀想知道。

“But where does programmer power come from?” Austin wanted to know.

我解释说，维克多雨果曾经说过，这个世界上没有什么比时机成熟的想法更强大的了。在我们这个时代，思想就是技术，尤其是信息处理技术。程序员分享了这种技术力量，就像外星人利用某种神秘的生命力一样。唯一不同的是，ET 知道自己在做什么，而程序员通常是不自觉地去做。典型的程序员认为技术力量是理所当然的——直到它消失。

I explained that Victor Hugo once said that nothing in this world was so powerful as an idea whose time has come. In our time, the idea is technology, especially information processing technology. The programmer partakes of this technology power, in much the same way that E.T. tapped into some mysterious life force. The only difference is that E.T. knew what he was doing, while programmers usually do it unconsciously. The typical programmer takes technology power for granted—until it disappears.

“就像当他们成为经理时，”凯文说，“他们的大脑变得软弱无力。”

“Like when they become managers,” Kevan said, “and their brains go soft.”

“凯文，我认为你对权力的看法过于简单，无法让你理解为什么程序员在决定接受监督职位时往往会失去权力——‘权力职位’。” “然后我开始向他们解释权力是一种关系。

“Kevan, I think your view of power is too simplistic to let you understand why programmers often lose power when they decide to accept supervisory positions—’positions of power.’ “ I then proceeded to explain to them about power as a relationship.

专业知识就是力量

EXPERTISE AS POWER

凯文对此并不满意。“这对我来说听起来太抽象了。你们只是不想承认像我这样的专业程序员拥有一些你们没有的东西。”

Kevan wasn’t happy with this. “That sounds too abstract for me. You guys just don’t want to admit that an expert programmer like me possesses something that you don’t have.”

“你确实拥有一些东西，但那是专长，而不是力量。您从该专业知识中获得的任何力量都基于您与他人之间的关系。如果你是登山队的领队，你的编程专业知识将无济于事

‘You do possess something, but it’s expertise, not power. Any power you get from that expertise is based on a relationship between you and someone else. If you were the leader of a mountain-climbing team, your programming expertise would contribute no power whatsoever

“但我不是登山队的队长。我是一个编程团队的领导者，所以我的专长就是力量。”

“But I’m not the leader of a mountain-climbing team. I’m the leader of a programming team, so my expertise is power.”

“对于你的特定团队来说可能是这样，但不一定对所有团队都如此。这完全取决于领导者与团队其他成员的关系。”

“It may be, for your particular team, but it doesn’t have to be for all teams. It all depends on the relationship of the leader to the other members of the team.”

“给我一个例子。”

“Give me a for instance.”

“让我试试，”奥斯汀说。“如果你的整个团队都是新手程序员，你的专业知识会给你相当大的力量；但如果其他团队成员也是专家，他们就会不太重视你的技术专长。在这种情况下，他们会更加关注组织能力，比如获得额外硬件、延长日程或获得更有趣任务的能力。”

“Let me try,” said Austin. “If your whole team consists of novice programmers, your expertise will give you considerable power; but if the other team members are also experts, they will attach less importance to your technical expertise. In that case, they’ll pay more attention to organizational power, like the power to acquire extra hardware, to extend the schedule, or to capture a more interesting assignment.”

“我可能欠你一个道歉，奥斯汀。我开始明白我们是如何同时正确的，但这确实令人费解。”

“I may owe you an apology, Austin. I’m beginning to see how we can both be right at the same time, but it sure is puzzling.”

“权力的概念似乎总是有这个令人费解的方面，”我说，“因为人们不习惯从关系的角度来思考。”

“The idea of power always seems to have this puzzling aspect,” I said, “because people aren’t used to thinking in terms of relationships.”

“比如我从组员升为组长？我确实经历过权力的丧失，这就是为什么我如此强烈反对奥斯汀的论点。”

“Like when I was promoted from team member to team leader? I definitely experienced a loss of power, which is why I came on so strong against Austin’s argument.”

“确切地。你的专长没有改变，但它不再那么重要，因为其他人的期望发生了变化。”

“Exactly. Your expertise didn’t change, but it no longer counted for so much because other people’s expectations changed.”

凯文笑了。“你知道，我真的很难向团队证明我的技术能力没有下降，但我所做的只是让他们相信我是一个软弱的领导者。”

Kevan laughed. “You know, I really struggled to demonstrate to the team that my technical skill hadn’t diminished, but all I did was convince them that I was a weak leader.”

“当然，”伊娜贝尔说。“如果你真的有力量，你不必费力去展示它。这就是个人力量的意义所在。”

“Of course,” said Inabelle. “If you really have power, you don’t have to struggle to show it. That’s what personal power is all about.”

“好吧，”奥斯汀说，“如果当我们试图获得权力时会发生这种情况，我们应该怎么做呢？”

“Well,” said Austin, “if that’s what happens when we try to acquire power, how are we supposed to go about it?”

“听着，”凯冯说。“我不在乎获得权力，但我不想失去我拥有的权力。我怎样才能在不失去完成工作的能力的情况下承担更多的责任？”

“Listen,” said Kevan. “I don’t care about acquiring power, but I don’t want to lose what power I have. How can I get more responsibility without losing my power to get things done?”

保持动力

KEEPING POWER

“伊娜贝尔走在正确的轨道上，”我说。“保持权力的第一步是停止如此努力地抓住它。”

“Inabelle is on the right track,” I said. “The first step in keeping power is to stop trying so hard to hang onto it.”

“这不是悖论。它直接源于权力作为一种关系的观念。对权力的渴望不是对事物的渴望，而是对关系的渴望。”

“It’s not a paradox. It follows directly from the idea of power as a relationship. The desire for power is not a desire for a thing, but for a relationship .”

”。而且您不会像保持或建立事物那样保持或建立关系！” 伊娜贝尔补充道。

”. and you don’t keep or build relationships the same way you keep or build things!” Inabelle added.

“确切地。假设你想要某样东西，但你还没有弄清楚它是什么。你认为你不满足是因为你没有能力得到你想要的，但问题是你无法想象你真正想要的是什么。”

“Exactly. Suppose you want something, but you haven’t figured out what it is. You think you’re dissatisfied because you don’t have the power to get,what you want, but the problem is that you can’t visualize what you really want.”

“所以只要我被这种幻觉蒙蔽了双眼，每当有什么变化，我就有失去力量的危险？”

“So as long as I’m blinded by this illusion, I’m in danger of losing power whenever something changes?”

“如果你不知道自己想要什么，那么权力对你来说就像法拉利对盲人司机一样毫无用处。你可能会不小心沿着赛道行驶，但你可能会撞到某个地方。”

“If you don’t know what you want, power is as useless to you as a Ferrari to a blind driver. You might accidentally steer along the track, but you’ll probably crash somewhere.”

“所以如果我专注于我想要的东西，力量就会降临到我身上？”

“So if I concentrate specifically on what I want, power will come to me?”

“不必要。我的视力很好，但我可能会撞坏法拉利。看得清楚是必要的，但即使看得清楚，也未必能阻止力量的流失。”

“Not necessarily. I can see perfectly well, but I’d probably crash a Ferrari. Seeing clearly is necessary, but even when you see clearly, you may not be able to prevent the loss of power.”

“那我还要做什么？”

“Then what else do I have to do?”

“只要你一直这么问，你就太盲目了，无法理解答案。如果您正在寻求升职以获得更多权力，那就算了！远离权力的诱惑，更多地了解自己。”

“As long as you keep asking that, you’re too blind to understand the answer. If you’re seeking a promotion in order to obtain more power, forget it! Step away from the lure of power and learn more about yourself.”

“这就是我所说的个人力量，”伊娜贝尔说。

“That’s what I meant by personal power,” Inabelle said.

“现在这对我来说很有意义，”凯文说。“当我接受升职时，我真的不知道我为什么这么做，但我确实对变得强大的想法感到受宠若惊。”

“That makes sense to me, now,” said Kevan. “When I accepted a promotion, I really had no idea why I did it, but I sure was flattered by the idea of being made powerful.”

“所以当你看到获得权力的机会时，问问自己你想要权力的目的是什么。如果你不知道这一点，当你的旧力量开始崩溃时，你肯定会动摇并迷失方向，因为在你的新力量开始增长之前，它必须如此。”

“So when you see a chance for power, ask yourself what you want power for. If you don’t know that, you’re sure to falter and lose your way when your old power starts to crumble, as it must before your new power starts to grow.”

伊娜贝尔笑了。“这让我想起了 ET 他不想要权力，但因为他知道自己真正想要什么，所以他在他们自己的游戏中击败了‘强大’。”

Inabelle smiled. “That reminds me of E.T. He didn’t want power, but because he knew what he really wanted, he beat the ‘powerful’ at their own game.”

“我看不懂这部电影，”奥斯汀抱怨道，“所以这真的没什么用。”

“I didn’t understand the movie,” Austin complained, “so that really isn’t very helpful.”

“好吧，”我说，最后一次尝试，“ET。真的很想回家。你真正想要的是什么？”

“Well,” I said, giving it one last try, “ET. really wanted to go home. What do you really want?”

问题

QUESTIONS

  1. 当你玩游戏时，你对比分有多少兴趣，对比赛有多少兴趣？当是团队比赛时，你对球队的表现感兴趣多少，对自己的数据感兴趣多少？这对您影响游戏结果的能力有何影响？当你在一个团队中工作时呢？
  2. When you play games, how much are you interested in the score and how much in the play? When it is a team game, how much are you interested in the team’s performance and how much in your own statistics? How does this affect your power to influence the outcome of the game? What about when you work in a group?
  3. 你在工作中的主要动力来源是什么？这种权力基于什么关系？
  4. What is your principal source of power at work? What relationships is that power based on?
  5. 你现在想抓住什么力量？如果你放手，可能发生的最糟糕的事情是什么？最好的东西？
  6. What power are you now trying to hang onto? What is the worst thing that might happen if you let go? the best thing?
  7. 如果你中了五百万美元的彩票，你会做什么？是什么阻止你没有钱做这件事？
  8. What would you do if you won five million dollars in a lottery? What keeps you from doing it without the money?
  9. 你最后一次放弃一些权力是什么时候？发生了什么？
  10. When was the last time you gave away some power? What happened?
  11. 上一次你有能力做某事但没有做是什么时候？发生了什么？
  12. When was the last time you had the power to do something, but withheld it? What happened?

第 15 章权力、不完美和一致性

Chapter 15. Power, Imperfection, and Congruence

一个成熟的人是一个成熟的人，他能够根据对自己、他人和他所处环境的准确认识做出选择和决定；谁承认这些选择和决定是他的；谁为他们的结果承担责任。——弗吉尼亚·萨提亚，《造人》

A mature person is one who, having attained his majority, is able to make choices and decisions based on accurate perceptions about himself, others, and the context in which he finds himself; who acknowledges these choices and decisions as being his; and who accepts responsibility for their outcomes. —Virginia Satir, Peoplemaking

我自己处理个人权力的方法背后的主要假设是，每个人都想感到自己有用，想做出贡献，这当然源自种子模型。我们中的许多人都认识一些人，他们很难坚持这个假设，因为他们看起来冷漠、不合作，甚至具有破坏性。如果每个人都如此热切地想做好事，怎么会有这么多人在做这样一件悲惨的工作？

The chief assumption underlying my own approach to personal power is that everyone wants to feel useful, to make a contribution, which of course derives from the seed model. Many of us know people who make this a difficult assumption to hold because they seem apathetic, uncooperative, or even destructive. If everyone wants so intensely to do good, how can so many people be doing such a miserable job?

更糟糕的是，如果我如此热切地想做好事，为什么我经常失败得这么惨？为什么我说错话，两个小时后才想到正确的事？为什么我恰恰在错误的时刻说了正确的话？当我感到如此无能时，我身上所有这些个人力量在哪里？

Even worse, if I want so intensely to do good, why do I so frequently fail so miserably? Why do I say the wrong thing and think of the right thing two hours later? Why do I say the right thing at precisely the wrong moment? Where’s all this personal power in me when I feel so inept?

机械问题

A MECHANICAL PROBLEM

我们知道低自尊是许多问题的根源，但问题与低自尊之间的关系并不总是容易察觉。许多问题都是机械性的问题，看起来与自尊一点关系也没有。我所说的机械问题是指一个看似深奥而复杂的问题，但最终可以通过一些技术性的东西、一个噱头来解决，没有太大的情绪或心理动荡。

We know that low self-esteem underlies so many of these problems, but the relationship between the problem and the low self-esteem is not always easy to perceive. Many problems are mechanical problems, which don’t appear to have anything to do with self-esteem at all. What I mean by a mechanical problem is one that may seem deep and complex, but turns out to be solved by something technical, a gimmick, with no great emotional or psychological turmoil.

机械问题的解决方案更可能涉及物理学而不是心理学。我们都倾向于使用我们最了解的解决方案类型来解决问题，这就是为什么技术领导者倾向于看到问题的机械方面。例如，当程序员遇到问题时，他们解决问题的第一次尝试几乎总是涉及编写程序。让我举个例子。

The solutions to mechanical problems are more likely to involve physics than psychology. We all tend to solve problems using the type of solution we know best, which is why technical leaders tend to see the mechanical side of problems. For instance, when programmers are having a problem, their first attempt to solve it will almost always involve writing a program. Let me give an example.

当我写《计算机编程心理学》时，我讲了一个年轻程序员的故事，他身上的气味太难闻以至于其他人都拒绝和他一起工作。这些年来，我收到的关于这个故事的信比我写过的任何其他东西都多。典型的信件会说：“你怎么知道的？拉尔夫为我工作，如果我不对他的体味采取措施，每个人都威胁要辞职。我应该怎么办？”

When I wrote The Psychology of Computer Programming, I told the story of a young programmer who smelled so bad that other people refused to work with him. Over the years, I’ve received more letters about that story than anything else I’ve ever written. The typical letter says, “How did you know? Ralph works for me, and everyone is threatening to quit if I don’t do something about his body odor. What should I do?”

从表面上看，这似乎是一个简单的机械问题，有一个简单的机械解决方案，就像肥皂和水一样。对程序员来说，最重要的解决方案在于不同的方向：设计软件，使 Ralph 的程序以最小的方式与其他程序连接。这样，Ralph 就可以以最少的方式与其他程序员建立联系——一种简洁、机械的解决方案。

On the surface, this seems to be a simple mechanical problem with a simple mechanical solution, like soap and water. To programmers, the forst solution lies in a different direction: Design the software so that Ralph’s program connects in a minimal way with the other programs. That way, Ralph connects in a minimal way with the other programmers—a neat, mechanical solution.

不幸的是，程序逻辑并不总是允许这样一个干净的解决方案，这就是为什么程序员最终不得不向他们的经理抱怨的原因。但经理也可以使用机械解决方案：肥皂和水。只要对拉尔夫说，“你们小组中的几个人告诉我，他们在你附近工作时会因为你身上散发出的气味而生病。我们喜欢你的工作，但显然如果其他人不能与你一起工作，我们就不能成为一个富有成效的团队。我们能做些什么来解决这个问题？” 如果问题是如此机械化，为什么经理不这样做呢？事实上，甚至不清楚经理为什么给我写信。为什么同事不这样做？

Unfortunately, program logic doesn’t always allow such a clean solution, which is why the programmers are eventually driven to complain to their manager. But the manager has access to a mechanical solution, too: soap and water. Just say to Ralph, “Several people in your group have told me that they get sick working near you because of the odor given off by your body. We like your work, but obviously we can’t be a productive group if other people can’t work with you. What can we do to solve this problem?” If the problem is so mechanical, why doesn’t the manager do this? In fact, it’s not even clear why the manager writes to me. Why don’t the co-workers do this?

首先，他们都为拉尔夫感到尴尬，因为他们认同他的处境。如果闻起来像那种味道的是我怎么办？好吧，如果是呢？如果你的气味对其他人没有吸引力，你作为人的价值会下降吗？只有当你的自尊心很低时。否则，您会很高兴听到这些信息，为您没有早点知道而感到遗憾，然后采取措施解决这种情况。

First, they are all embarrassed for Ralph because they identify with his situation. What if it were me who smelled like that? Well, what if it were? Does your value as a human being drop if your smell is not attractive to other people? Only if your self-esteem is low. Otherwise, you’ll appreciate hearing the information, be sorry that you weren’t aware sooner, and then do something about the situation.

在一个案例中，经理接受了我的建议并直接告诉程序员，程序员按照我的预测做了。原来，他的爱好是鞣制皮革。他使用的化学品让他的手散发出令人作呕的气味——令人作呕，也就是说，让其他人感到恶心。他一直在研究这种气味，但根本没有意识到这一点。他很感激他的经理让他知道，并去看了他的医生，他开了一种药丸来改变他的皮肤对化学物质的反应方式——如果有的话，这是一种机械解决方案。（需要明确的是，事情并不总是这么简单，但如果有人觉得自己没有足够的能力直接解决问题，那就永远不会这么简单。）

In one case where the manager took my advice and told the programmer directly, the programmer did just as I predicted. It turned out that his hobby involved tanning leather. The chemicals he used gave his hands a sickening smell—sickening, that is, to other people. He worked with the smell all the time and simply wasn’t aware of it. He was grateful that his manager made him aware, and visited his physician, who prescribed a pill that changed the way his skin reacted to the chemicals—a mechanical solution if there ever was one. (Just to be clear, it’s not always this simple, but it will never be if someone doesn’t feel sufficiently powerful to address the problem directly.)

程序员不能直接处理这个问题的另一个原因是他们无法面对如果 Ralph 反应不佳可能发生的情况。他们知道，如果有人告诉他们关于他们自己的不愉快的真相，人们有时会做出糟糕的反应。他们不知道的是，这种不良反应源于一个人的自卑。如果拉尔夫对出于真诚关心的信息而生气，那不是他们的问题。拉尔夫的愤怒对他们的伤害怎么可能比目前的情况更严重呢？他们是否宁愿他被解雇，而不知道原因，只是为了维护自己微不足道的自尊？

Another reason programmers can’t deal with this problem directly is that they just can’t face what might happen if Ralph should react badly. They know that people do sometimes react badly if told an unpleasant truth about themselves. What they don’t know is that this bad reaction emanates from a person’s low self-esteem. If Ralph gets angry in response to information given out of genuine caring, it’s not their problem. How can Ralph’s anger harm them worse than the present situation? Would they prefer that he be fired, without knowing the reason, just to preserve their own minuscule self-esteem?

成熟的行为模式

MATURE PATTERNS OF BEHAVIOR

为什么拉尔夫的机械问题这么难处理？同样，此类问题不是由事件（机械部分）引起的，而是由对事件的反应引起的。使用一些行为模式，我们可以将事件变成一个问题。使用其他人，我们可以使问题消失。俗话说，选择是问题的一部分还是解决方案的一部分。

Why is Ralph’s mechanical problem so hard to handle? Once again, such problems are not caused by the event—the mechanical part—but by-the reaction to the event. Using some patterns of behavior, we can make the event into a problem. Using others, we can make the problem disappear. The choice, as the saying goes, it to be part of the problem or part of the solution.

作为问题一部分的行为模式被称为功能失调，是不成熟的人的特征，个人能力低下。作为解决方案一部分的行为模式被称为功能性行为模式，是成熟人士的特征，具有很高的个人权力。当然，这些只是简化，因为没有人在所有问题情况下都具有同等的功能。我学会了相当有效地处理臭臭的程序员问题，但是当一只蜘蛛爬上我的裤腿时，我就不是成熟的典范了。相反，成熟度是行为的统计集合，我们可以一次改进一点点的行为。

Behavior patterns that are part of the problem are called dysfunctional and characterize the immature person, with low personal power. Behavior patterns that are part of the solution are called functional and characterize the mature person, with high personal power. Of course, these are simplifications, because no person is equally functional in all problem situations. I’ve learned to deal rather effectively with the smelly programmer problem, but when a spider crawls up my pant leg, I’m not the model of maturity. Maturity is, rather, a statistical collection of behaviors, behaviors we can improve a little at a time.

弗吉尼亚·萨提亚 (Virginia Satir) 列出了一份行为清单，可以帮助一个人“以相对称职和准确的方式与世界打交道”。她说这样的人会

Virginia Satir has composed a list of behaviors that help a person “deal in a relatively competent and precise way with the world.” She says that such persons will

  1. 与他人打交道时要清楚。
  2. be clear when they deal with others.
  3. 注意他们自己的想法和感受。
  4. be aware of their own thoughts and feelings.
  5. 能够看到和听到外面的东西。
  6. be able to see and hear what is outside themselves.
  7. 对待他人的行为与他们自己不同，并且是独一无二的。
  8. behave toward other people as separate from themselves and unique.
  9. 将差异视为学习和探索的机会，而不是威胁或冲突信号。
  10. treat differentness as an opportunity to learn and explore rather than as a threat or a signal for conflict.
  11. 在他们的背景下处理人和情况，而不是他们希望它如何或期望它如何。
  12. deal with persons and situations in their context, in terms of how it is rather than how they wish it were or expect it to be.
  13. 为自己的感受、想法、听到和看到的事情承担责任，而不是否认或将其归咎于他人。
  14. accept responsibility for what they feel, think, hear, and see, rather than denying it or attributing it to others.
  15. 有开放的技术来给予、接受和检查与他人的意义。
  16. have open techniques for giving, receiving, and checking meaning with others.

这种对成熟度的描述强调了社交和沟通技巧，这就是为什么噱头并不是特别重要的原因。如果你有这些社交和沟通技巧，你很快就会发明你需要的噱头。让我们看看在臭程序员的情况下它是如何工作的。

This description of maturity emphasizes social and communication skills, which is why gimmicks are not terribly important. If you have these social and communication skills, you will soon invent the gimmicks you need. Let’s see how that works in the case of the smelly programmer.

处理您自己的机械问题

DEALING WITH YOUR OWN MECHANICAL PROBLEMS

首先，假设你是拉尔夫。你拥有所有这些社交和沟通技巧，但你晒黑了皮革，闻不到自己的手。您会注意到其他人对您的行为很特别 (c)，并且您可以与其他人核实发生了什么 (h)。因为你会以直接、清晰的方式行事 (a)，而无需判断他们的反应 (f)，他们很可能不会害怕向你提供你需要但无法通过你自己的鼻子获得的可靠信息。一旦你掌握了这些信息，你将能够承担起处理它的责任，而不是责怪其他人没有足够爱你来忍受你的气味 (g)。

First, suppose you are Ralph. You have all these social and communication skills, but you tan leather and can’t smell your own hands. You would notice that other people were acting peculiarly toward you (c), and you would be able to check with others about what was going on (h). Because you would be acting in a straight, clear manner (a), without judgment of their reactions (f), chances are they would not be afraid to give you the reliable information you need but cannot obtain through your own nose. Once you have that information, you will be able to take responsibility for dealing with it, rather than blaming the others for not loving you sufficiently to put up with your odor (g).

其次，假设你闻到了拉尔夫的气味。你会发现 Ralph 不是你 (d)，也不是对你的威胁 (e)。您将能够以一种很可能会被听到 (h) 和被听到而不会受到指控 (f) 的方式向他提供信息，因此很可能会采取行动。

Second, suppose you were subjected to Ralph’s odor. You would see that Ralph was not you (d) and not a threat to you (e). You would be able to give him information in a manner that would likely be heard (h), and heard without accusation (f ), so it would likely be acted upon.

显然，即使只有一个成熟的人在场，也会大大增加快速、干净、人道地解决这个问题和其他类似问题的机会。换句话说，创造解决问题的环境的第一步是在你自己的成熟上努力，但这不是靠噱头就能实现的。从某种意义上说，拥有令人愉悦的体味是一种交流噱头。许多关于权力和影响力的书籍都会告诉您个人仪容仪表的重要性。这些书是正确的，但它们对未来的领导者有多大用处？如果你没有自我价值感和更一般的社交和沟通技巧，梅西百货的所有除臭剂和香水都无法掩盖你的不足。如果你有它们，你很快就会弄清楚你需要知道的关于美容的一切。

Clearly, the presence of even a single mature person greatly increases the chance of a rapid, clean, and humane solution to this problem and others like it. In other words, the first step in creating a problem-solving environment is to work on your own maturity, but this can’t be accomplished through gimmicks. Having a pleasant body odor is, in one sense, a communication gimmick. Many books on power and influence inform you of the importance of personal grooming. These books are correct, but how useful are they to the would-be leader? If you don’t have a sense of your own self-worth and the more general social and communication skills, all the deodorant and perfume in Macy’s won’t hide your deficiency. If you do have them, you’ll figure out soon enough everything you need to know about grooming.

比如几年前有一个客户跟我说，虽然我表面上看起来很开心，但我笑得不够多，这让一些人觉得我可能在生气。我立刻意识到，我脸上酸溜溜的表情是一种习惯，是我不喜欢自己或不喜欢别人的日子留下来的。我改变了对自己和人类的看法，但没有告诉我的脸。于是我就解决了这个问题，现在我的笑容和我内心的感受更加吻合了——也就是我为人处事更加清晰了。我的客户的成熟使她能够清楚地告诉我，而不用担心她知道我真的很开心，尽管出于某种原因没有表现出来。这反过来又使我有可能增加我的成熟度——这是她个人力量影响的一个例子。

For instance, a few years ago a client told me that even though I seemed happy underneath, I didn’t smile enough, which made some people feel that I might be angry. I immediately realized that the sour expression on my face was a habit, left over from the days when I didn’t like myself or others. I had changed my opinion of myself and humanity, but hadn’t informed my face. So I worked on the problem, and now my smiles are a lot more congruent with my inner feelings—that is, I am more clear in dealing with others. My client’s maturity made it possible for her to tell me clearly and without fear that she knew I was really happy, though not showing it for some reason. This in turn made it possible for me to increase my maturity—an example of the effect of her personal power.

当你内心感到快乐时记得微笑是一个机械问题，就像处理手上的难闻气味一样。当我说我“在这个问题上做了一些工作”时，我的意思是我使用了机械设备来帮助我记住该做什么，就像制革匠可能会提醒他服用他的除臭药一样。例如，我在拇指上包了绷带，每当我发现自己在摆弄它时，我就会记得开心和微笑，因为我实际上并没有受伤。很快我就看到任何人身上的绷带都会提醒我微笑，很快我就会在看到男人脸上和女人腿上的剃刀划痕时微笑。过了一会儿，微笑的习惯在 75% 的情况下取代了皱眉的习惯，我可以省去这些噱头了。

Remembering to smile when you feel happy inside is a mechanical problem, like taking care of a bad odor on your hands. When I say I “worked a bit on the problem,” I mean that I employed mechanical devices to help me remember what to do, just as the tanner might to remind him to take his anti-smell pill. For example, I put a bandage on my thumb, and whenever I noticed myself fiddling with it, I remembered to be happy and smile because I wasn’t actually wounded. Soon I reached the point where seeing a bandage on anybody reminded me to smile, and soon I was smiling at the sight of razor nicks on men’s faces and women’s legs. After a while, the smiling habit had replaced the frowning habit in seventy-five percent of the cases, and I could dispense with the gimmicks.

我必须总是自然和自发的

I must always be natural and spontaneous

当我在记住微笑方面变得更加成功时，我感到自己的成功笼罩着阴影。最终我将这个影子追踪到一条规则：

While I was becoming more successful at remembering to smile, I felt a shadow over my successes. Eventually I tracked down this shadow to a rule:

在与他人打交道时，我必须始终自然而然。

In dealing with other people, I must always be natural and spontaneous.

当应用到改变我的交互行为时，这条规则变成了一个严重的元规则。每当我练习一些技巧来改善我的互动时，我都觉得自己不真诚、错误，而且很糟糕。这条规则是如此强大，它经常阻止我思考与他人互动时我在做什么。

When applied to changing my interactive behavior, this rule became a crippling meta-rule. Whenever I would practice some gimmick to improve my interactions, I felt that I was insincere, wrong, and just plain bad. The rule was so powerful it often blocked me even from thinking about what I was doing when interacting with other people.

我承认这条规则有生存价值，并开始改造它：

I acknowledged that this rule had survival value, and started to transform it:

在与他人打交道时，我总是自然而然。

In dealing with other people, I CAN always be natural and spontaneous.

但是当我试图将其更改为

But when I tried to change this to

在与他人打交道时，如果我愿意的话，有时我可以表现得自然而自发。

In dealing with other people, I can SOMETIMES be natural and spontaneous, if I choose to.

我对这种转变感觉不对。我知道我可以一直很自然（你可能无法做任何其他事情，但每个人都可以很自然）。这就是我一直想做出的选择。所以我被困住了。

I didn’t feel right about the transformation. I knew that I could always be natural (you may not be able to do anything else, but everyone can be natural). And that’s the choice I wanted to make, always. So I was stuck.

我与负责照顾小孩的苏珊讨论了这种感觉。当我说我不诚实地练习微笑时，她笑着说：“是什么让你认为当你内心感到微笑时皱眉是自然的？”

I discussed this feeling with Susan, who works with little kids. When I said that I felt dishonest to practice smiling, she smiled and said, “What makes you think it’s natural to frown when you feel smiley inside?”

“这一定是自然的，”我回答说，“因为我是自发地做的。”

“It must be natural,” I replied, “because I do it spontaneously.”

“你也会自然而然地说英语，但你肯定学会了如何去做。我想你也学会了皱眉。您将“自然”与“在我意识到之前就在生命的早期学习”混淆了。事实上，你学到的是不自然的，因为自然的东西是一致的，从外部展示内部真正发生的事情。”

“You also speak English spontaneously, but you certainly learned how to do that. I think you learned how to frown, too. You’re confusing ‘natural’ with ‘learned early in life, before I was aware of it.’ In fact, what you learned was to be unnatural, because the natural thing is to be congruent, to show on the outside what’s truly going on inside.”

苏珊的线索让我的转变重回正轨。我没有正确完成第一步。我未能从规则的明确陈述开始，所以我重新开始

Susan’s clue got my transformation back on track. I hadn’t done the first step properly. I had failed to start with a clear statement of the rule, so I began again with

在与他人打交道时，我必须始终保持一致。

In dealing with other people, I must always be congruent.

我很容易将这条规则转化为以下指南：

I readily transformed this rule into the following guide:

在与他人打交道时，我想尽可能地保持一致，我可以通过改变旧规则和修改我早年养成的习惯，使规则和习惯更符合今天的我，以及这个人我想成为明天。

In dealing with other people, I want to be as congruent as I can, which I can achieve by transforming old rules, and modifying habits I learned early in life, into rules and habits more congruent with the person I am today, and the person I want to be tomorrow.

这种转变感觉棒极了。

This transformation felt terrific.

我必须总是非常有效

I must always be perfectly effective

了解到我想要保持一致，而不是自发的，我在学会微笑时取得了快速进步——直到我达到大约 75% 的稳定状态。我知道得更多，但我没能做得更好。我的老规矩，“我必须总是非常有效”，每当我忘记展示内心的微笑时，这让我感觉非常非常糟糕。

Having learned that I want to be congruent, rather than spontaneous, I made rapid progress in learning to smile when I felt like smiling—until I reached a plateau at about seventy-five percent. I knew better, but I failed to do better. My old rule, “I must always be perfectly effective,” was making me feel very, very bad every time I forgot to show my interior smile.

在一些朋友的帮助下，我成功地将这条规则与威胁/奖励模型联系起来。威胁/奖励模型说在任何交易中我必须是赢家或输家。如果我不能完全有效，那么我显然不能成为赢家，所以我必须成为输家。我觉得自己像个失败者。

With the help of some friends, I succeeded in relating this rule to the threat/reward model. The threat/reward model says that in any transaction I must be either a winner or a loser. If I fail to be perfectly effective, then I obviously can’t be a winner so I must be a loser. And I felt like a loser.

种子模型是一个选择模型。诚然，我可以选择感觉自己像个赢家或输家，但我还有第三种选择：感觉自己像个学习者。即使我觉得自己是个失败者，我也会觉得自己是个学习者。

The seed model is a choice model. It’s true that I can choose to feel like a winner or a loser, but I also have a third choice: to feel like a learner. Even if I feel like a loser, I can also feel like a learner.

当问题定义不同时，学习几乎是不可能的。据我所知，要获得清晰、通用的定义，唯一的方法就是集中精力控制沟通的质量。与往常一样，我唯一的影响力是我自己，但质量决定质量。如果我的交流质量很高，我就会收到高质量的交流——我可以从中学习做得更好。

When problem definitions differ, learning is almost impossible. The only way I know to arrive at clear, common definitions is to concentrate on controlling the quality of communication. As always, the only leverage I have is on myself, but quality breeds quality. If my communications are of high quality, I’ll receive high-quality communications—from which I can learn to do even better.

当我能够保持一致时，即使沟通出现问题，我也会有更可靠的信息来学习下一次如何做得更好。假设我开始与 Rod 进行艰难的互动时大喊：“如果不是你装病，我们会如期进行。你为什么不振作起来？当 Rod 对我大喊大叫或沉默时，我无法知道他是对我消息的形式还是内容做出反应。互动不是很好，但我不知道是罗德还是我。

When I’m able to be congruent, then even if the communication is bungled, I’ll have more reliable information to use in learning how to do it better the next time. Suppose I start a difficult interaction with Rod by shouting, “We would be on schedule if it weren’t for your malingering. Why don’t you get your act together?” When Rod shouts back at me, or clams up, I have no way of knowing whether he’s reacting to the form or the content of my message. The interaction doesn’t come out well, but I don’t know whether it’s Rod or me.

假设我以更一致的陈述开始相同的互动，“我感到生气，因为我们没有按时完成工作，我不知道为什么会这样。当我四处寻找原因时，我注意到你这个月已经缺席了六次。您是否认为您的缺席导致了日程安排问题？还是有别的事？”

Suppose I start the same interaction with the more congruent statement, “I feel angry because we’re not getting the job done on time, and I don’t know why it’s happening. When I look around for reasons, I notice that you’ve been absent six times this month. Do you feel that your absence is contributing to the schedule problem? Or is there something else?”

Rod 现在可以使用准确的问题陈述。假设回复是“哎呀，我不知道我们遇到了日程安排问题。我们不是要到下周五吗？” 现在您有几个机会来清理交叉线。

Rod now has an accurate problem statement to work with. Suppose the reply is “Gee, I didn’t know we were having a schedule problem. Don’t we have until next Friday?” Now you have several opportunities to clear up crossed wires.

但如果 R​​od 大声回应，或者沉默不语，那么我就更清楚问题确实出在他的某个地方，而不是在我或我与他的互动中。我仍然可能是错的——我可能不像我想的那么一致——但我有了一个更好的开始。

But if Rod shouts back, or clams up, then I have a better idea that the problem does lie somewhere within him, not within me or my interaction with him. I could still be wrong—I may not have been as congruent as I thought—but I’m off to a better start.

一致的回报

THE PAYOFF FOR BEING CONGRUENT

与任何沟通技巧一样，保持一致并不是您可以百分百学到的东西。但回报是如此之大，你不必是完美的。即使一个人设法在其他人以扭曲的方式行事时以一致的方式行事一次，其结果也值得一千次失败。

As with any communication skill, being congruent is not some-thing you ever learn one-hundred percent. But the payoff is so great, you don’t have to be perfect. Even if one person manages to act once in a congruent manner when the rest of the group is acting in a twisted way, the results can be worth a thousand failures.

许多年前，当我在纽约的 IBM 系统研究所任教时，几位教职员工抱怨一名学生“试图逃避惩罚”。来自堪萨斯州的学生史蒂夫已经好几个星期没有交任何作业，愤怒的教员们提议让他回家。史蒂夫不在我的任何班级，所以我对这种情况并没有那么激动。当我提出也许我们不明白这个问题时，我被有力地提醒说所有的学生都是从 IBM 的精英员工中精心挑选出来的。史蒂夫当然可以完成这项工作，只要他有动力。

Many years ago, when I was teaching at the IBM Systems Research Institute in New York, several faculty members complained about a student who was “trying to get away with something.” Steve, a student from Kansas, had failed to turn in any of his assignments for several weeks, and the outraged faculty members proposed sending him home. Steve wasn’t in any of my classes, so I didn’t get quite so emotional about the situation. When I suggested that perhaps we didn’t under- stand the problem, I was forcefully reminded that all of the students had been carefully selected from among IBM’s elite employees. Steve could certainly do the work, if only he was motivated.

即便如此，我争辩说，将他送回家可能会毁了他的职业生涯，所以我们应该加倍确定我们了解情况。他们勉强同意让我和他谈话，但我是他最后的机会。在我的办公室和他谈了一个小时后，我觉得我们毫无进展。我以为我以一致的方式开始问史蒂夫，“发生了什么事？你能解释一下你为什么不做这项工作吗？” 但史蒂夫否认有任何问题。然而，我注意到史蒂夫看起来一点问题都没有。他僵硬地坐在椅子上，似乎无法直视我的眼睛。我开始说服自己，他有事要隐瞒，而且这不是什么体面的事。我正要开始指责他不诚实时，我意识到我正在推断他的内心，

Even so, I argued, sending him home would probably destroy his career, so we should be doubly sure that we understood the circumstances. They reluctantly agreed to allow me to speak with him, but I was to be his last chance. After an hour with him in my office, I felt we were getting nowhere. I thought I started out in a congruent fashion by asking Steve, “What’s going on? Can you explain why you’re not doing the work?” but Steve denied that there was any problem. I noticed, however, that Steve didn’t look like there was no problem. He sat stiffly in his chair, and couldn’t seem to look me in the eye. I began to convince myself that he had something to hide, and that it wasn’t something honorable. I was about to start accusing him of dishonesty when I realized that I was making inferences about what was inside him, rather than making statements about what was inside of me.

所以我决定尝试以更一致的方式重新开始对话。“史蒂夫，”我说，“我坐在这里越来越生气，因为我觉得我在努力帮助你，而你甚至不跟我说发生了什么事。你告诉我没有问题，但对我来说似乎有问题。其他教员想把你赶出研究所，送你回家。如果发生这种情况，您可能会丢掉工作。对我来说，这听起来像是一个严重的问题，但你说不是。我缺少什么需要帮助你？”

So I decided to try restarting the conversation on a more congruent note. “Steve,” I said, “I’m sitting here getting angrier and angrier because I feel I’m trying to help you and you won’t even talk to me about what’s going on. You’re telling me that there’s no problem, but to me it seems that there is a problem. The other faculty members want to throw you out of the Institute and send you home. If that happens, you’ll probably lose your job. To me that sounds like a serious problem, but you say it isn’t. What am I missing that I need to help you?”

就在这时，史蒂夫的表情从生硬的回避变成了暴怒。他看着我的眼睛大喊：“你他妈的以为你是谁？是什么让你认为你可以帮助我？你以为自己高大威猛，其实你什么都不是！没有人！” 然后他不再说话转身离开了。

At this point, Steve’s appearance changed from stiff avoidance to violent anger. He looked me in the eye and shouted, “Who the hell do you think you are? What makes you think you can help me? You think you’re so big and powerful, but you’re nobody! Nobody!” Then he stopped talking and turned away.

我的第一个——我的“本能”——冲动是冲他大喊大叫，但不知何故我意识到他痛苦不堪。尽管我不知道疼痛是什么，但我还是克服了“自然”的训练，什么也没说，伸手轻轻地放在他的手臂上。

My first—my “natural”—impulse was to shout back at him, but somehow I realized that he was in terrible pain. Even though I didn’t know what the pain was, I overcame my “natural” training, said nothing, and reached out and laid my hand gently on his arm.

突然，他开始浑身发抖，然后抽泣着说着难以理解的话。我坐在那里，我的手放在他的胳膊上，直到他恢复到可以说话的程度。然后他告诉了我整个故事。

Suddenly, he started shaking all over, then sobbing and uttering incomprehensible words. I sat there, my hand on his arm, until he recovered himself sufficiently to talk. Then he told me the whole story.

在他前往研究所的前一周，史蒂夫的妻子被诊断出患有晚期癌症。她预计不会活超过六个月。他自然决定不去研究所，但她坚持要他去，认为拒绝这个机会会损害他的职业生涯。她走后，三个孩子就靠他养活了，做好自己的工作显得尤为重要。

A week before he left for the Institute, Steve’s wife had been diagnosed as having terminal cancer. She wasn’t expected to live more than six months. He naturally decided he would not attend the Institute, but she insisted that he go, arguing that he would hurt his career by refusing this opportunity. After she was gone, he would be the sole support for their three children, so it was doubly important that he do well in his work.

对我来说，很容易看出他做出了错误的决定，但史蒂夫被悲伤蒙蔽了双眼，无法违背她表达的意愿，于是他去了纽约上学。在这种情况下，家庭作业看起来毫无意义，史蒂夫什么也做不了，只能坐在旅馆房间里哭泣。他不敢告诉任何人，所以他的老师们做了最坏的打算。

To me, it was easy to see that he had made the wrong decision, but blinded by grief and unable to go against her expressed wishes, Steve went to school in New York. Under the circumstances, the homework assignments looked meaningless, and Steve couldn’t bring himself to do anything but sit in his hotel room and weep. He was afraid to tell anyone, so his teachers assumed the worst.

当史蒂夫攻击我以为我可以提供帮助时，他是完全正确的。我根本无法帮助他的妻子从癌症中康复，这是一个比他的学业大得多的问题。如果我没有在他攻击我时抵制我攻击他的“自然”本能，整个故事可能会是一个更大的悲剧。我帮不了他妻子的癌症，但我可以用一种破坏性较小的方式帮助他治疗他妻子的癌症。

When Steve attacked me for assuming I could help, he was exactly correct. There was no way in the world I could help his wife recover from cancer, which was a problem infinitely greater than his schoolwork. Had I not resisted my “natural” instinct to attack him when he attacked me whole story might have been an even greater tragedy. I couldn’t help with his wife’s cancer, but I could help him deal with his wife’s cancer in a less destructive way.

了解情况后，IBM 安排将史蒂夫送回堪萨斯州，让他带薪休假与妻子度过最后的日子。一年后，他得以重返研究所，重新开始。你可能必须在 100% 的时间里成功才能变得完美，但你不必在 100% 的时间里成功才能变得强大。

Once the circumstances were understood, IBM arranged to send Steve home to Kansas, giving him paid leave to be with his wife in her final days. A year later, he was able to return to the Institute and make a fresh start. You may have to succeed one hundred percent of the time to be perfect, but you don’t have to succeed one hundred percent of the time to be powerful.

问题

QUESTIONS

  1. 回想一下您知道该做什么但忘记去做的情况。遗漏了什么可能让你在正确的时间想起？
  2. Recall a situation when you knew what to do but forgot to do it. What was missing that might have made you remember at the right time?
  3. 回想一下你不知道该做什么的情况。你做了什么？如果在你不知道该做什么的时候出现这种情况，你现在会怎么做？
  4. Recall a situation when you didn’t know what to do. What did you do? What would you do now if the situation arose when you didn’t know what to do?
  5. 想想你因为另一个人的机械问题而遇到的问题。为什么不能面对？可能发生的最坏情况是什么？面对它！
  6. Think of a problem you’re having because of another person’s mechanical problem. Why can’t you face it? What’s the worst that can happen? Face it!
  7. 回想一下当你无法做出贡献时你在某个团体中的感受。
  8. Recall how you felt in some group when you couldn’t make a contribution.
  9. 当你在某件事上失败时，你会给自己什么信息？这些消息背后的规则是什么？
  10. What messages do you give yourself when you fail at something? What rules are behind those messages?
  11. 当你“输了”时回想一下最近的一次电力交易。你从那次交易中学到了什么？通过以新的眼光复习，您现在可以学到什么？
  12. Recall a recent power transaction when you “lost.” What did you learn from that transaction? What can you learn now by reviewing it in a new light?
  13. 你内心发生的哪些事情通常不会表现在外面？你怎么能改变它？你想改变它吗？
  14. What things are going on inside you that don’t usually show on the outside? How can you change that? Do you want to change that?

8 你内心正在发生哪些你试图不表现出来的事情？你怎么知道它在工作？如果你把这种能量投入到其他事物中会发生什么？

8 What things are going on inside you that you’re trying not to show? How do you know it’s working? What would happen if you put that energy into something else?

第四部分：组织

PART FOUR: ORGANIZATION

组织通常是即将到来的技术领导者掌握的 MOI 模型的最后一个组成部分。技术领导者本身就是创新者，并且能够以身作则激励他人，他们常常认为组织是多余的，或者考虑起来不太好。他们对组织在成功解决问题中的作用视而不见，因此当组织问题出现时，他们无助地跌跌撞撞。

Organization is usually the last component of the MOI model to be mastered by upcoming technical leaders. Innovators themselves, and capable of motivating others by example, technical leaders often regard organization as superï¬‚uous, or not quite nice to think about. They are quite blind to the role of organization in problem-solving success, so they stumble helplessly when organizational problems arise.

在接下来的章节中，我们将探讨为什么组织权力很重要，如何将现有权力转化为组织权力，以及如何学习成为有效的组织者。

In the following chapters, we’ll look at why organizational power is important, what can be done to convert existing power to organizational power, and how to learn to be an effective organizer.

第 16 章获得组织权力

Chapter 16. Gaining Organizational Power

的确，如果各国学者的心态，如最近的战争所揭示的那样，往往显得低于文化程度较低的民众的水平，那是因为一切权力都存在内在的危险，而不是纪律严明并指向更高的目标，只有这些目标才配得上它。——居里夫人，《智力合作》

Indeed, if the mentality of the scholars of the various countries, as revealed by the recent war, often appears to be on a lower level than that of the less cultured masses, it is because there is a danger inherent in all power that is not disciplined and directed toward the higher aims which alone are worthy of it.—Marie Curie, “Intellectual Cooperation”

帮助他人的能力大部分来自个人力量，但断言不需要其他任何东西就太天真了。在大型组织中，领导者可以使用许多资源——支付培训费用、支持人员、办公空间、提高工作效率的工具，以及接触乐于助人的人。这种资源分布不均，成为问题解决型领导者的要求之一就是获得组织权力，从而为其他创新者争取资源。

Much of the ability to help other people arises from personal power, but it would be naive to assert that nothing else is required. In large organizations, there are many resources available to a leader—money to pay for training, support staff, office space, tools to make work more efficient, access to helpful people. Such resources are not evenly distributed, and one of the requirements for becoming a problem-solving leader is to acquire organizational power so as to obtain resources for other innovators.

大多数进入领导职位的创新者对组织权力知之甚少或一无所知。他们面对的竞争对手可能缺乏技术人才，但在为员工获取稀缺资源方面更有经验。因此，就在技术力量即将流失之际，新的领导者需要新的力量。由于技术力量不会立即消失，如果新领导人了解力量转换，可能还有时间交易其他好东西。

Most innovators who move into leadership positions know little or nothing about organizational power. They face competitors who may lack technical talent but have more experience obtaining scarce resources for their people. Thus, the new leader needs new powers just when technical power is about to slip away. Since technical power doesn’t disappear instantly, there may still be time to trade other goodies, if the new leader understands about power conversion.

转换功率

CONVERTING POWER

我是在采访 Faultless Computers 的顶级女工程师 Edrie 时第一次了解到电源转换的。所以她不会被电话打扰，我们在自助餐厅角落的一张桌子旁工作。不幸的是，人事部的阿特伍德无意中听到了采访的一部分，并邀请自己加入我们。阿特伍德喝咖啡的时候，埃德里试图安慰我。“这样想吧。在喝一杯咖啡的时间里，您将获得人事专家的官方观点。你会看到，阿特伍德会非常高兴有观众。”

I first learned about power conversion when interviewing Edrie, the top woman engineer at Faultless Computers. So she wouldn’t be interrupted by phone calls, we were working at a table in the corner of the cafeteria. Unfortunately, Atwood from Personnel overheard part of the interview and invited himself to join us. While Atwood was getting his coffee, Edrie tried to console me. “Think of it this way. In the time it takes to drink a cup of coffee, you’ll get the official view of a personnel professional. You’ll see, Atwood will be only too happy to have an audience.”

“但我不想浪费你更多的时间，”我道歉。

“But I don’t want to waste more of your time,” I apologized.

“不用担心。如果我不认为我能从阿特伍德那里得到一些关于公司政策的有用信息，我就不会让他加入我们。”

“Don’t worry. If I didn’t think I’d get some useful information about company policies out of Atwood, I wouldn’t have let him join us.”

当阿特伍德回来时，我问他 Faultless 在他们的领导者身上寻找什么。

When Atwood returned, I asked him what Faultless looks for in their leaders.

“当然，”他说，“许多领导素质是无形的，但我们可以根据他们的经验，准确地挑选出优秀的领导者。”

“Of course,” he said, “many leadership qualities are intangible, but we can pick good leaders with high accuracy based on their experience.”

“真的？” 我说。“你在寻找什么样的体验？”

“Really?” I said. “What kinds of experience are you looking for?”

好吧，它不一定是任何特定的工作经验。例如，如果一个男人已婚，并且可能是父亲，他通常会比未婚的人成为更好的领导者。”

Well, it doesn’t have to be any particular job experience. For instance, if a man is married, and possibly a father, he’ll generally make a better leader than someone who isn’t.”

“哦，”埃德里说。“那么身为母亲的女性一定是真正的好领导，因为母亲通常是包揽所有工作的人。” “恐怕我没有太多作为领导者的母亲的经验。你知道我们对你这样有能力的未婚女性没有任何的好感，但是对于未婚妈妈我们自然是无可奈何的。而且我们不会雇佣太多已婚女性。”

“Oh,” said Edrie. “Then women who are mothers must really be good leaders, since the mother is usually the one who does all the work.” “I’m afraid I haven’t much experience with mothers as leaders. You know that we have nothing against competent unmarried women like yourself, but naturally we have nothing to do with unmarried mothers. And we don’t hire too many married women.”

Edrie 怒火中烧，但似乎不想说话，所以我继续说下去。“为什么你认为父亲是很好的领导材料？因为他们有太多的经验可以诱使母亲做所有的孩子的工作？”

Edrie was seething, but didn’t seem to want to speak, so I continued. “Why do you think fathers are such good leadership material? Because they have so much experience conning mothers into doing all the work with the kids?”

“我几乎不这么认为。. . . 哦，我明白了，这是个笑话。不，恐怕我不能告诉你父亲身份如何使一个人成为优秀的领导者。我自己就是单身汉。”

“I hardly think so. . . . Oh, I see, it’s a joke. No, I’m afraid I can’t tell you just what it is about fatherhood that makes a man a good leader. I’m a bachelor myself.”

“你有很多孩子吗？”

“Do you have many kids?”

嗯，真的。. . 哦，这是另一个笑话吗？我当然希望这是个玩笑。”

“Well, really . . . oh, is that another joke? I certainly hope it is a joke.”

Atwood 和我似乎不在同一个波长上，而 Edrie 甚至都没有调谐。在长时间沉闷的沉默之后，Atwood 请求将业务压到人事部，并告辞了。“终于一个人了，”我说，我知道埃德丽很欣赏我的笑话。但她只是盯着空荡荡的门口。

Atwood and I didn’t seem to be on the same wavelength, and Edrie wasn’t even tuned in. After a long heavy silence, Atwood pleaded pressing business down in Personnel and excused himself. “Alone at last,” I said, knowing Edrie appreciated my jokes. But she just stared at the empty doorway.

“艾德丽？你在吗？”

“Edrie? Are you there?”

“哦对不起。我在想阿特伍德说的话。”

“Oh, sorry. I was thinking about what Atwood said.”

“关于父亲成为更好的领导者？别担心——我敢肯定他都湿了。”

“About fathers making better leaders? Don’t worry about it—I’m sure he’s all wet.”

“不，他可能是对的。”

“No, he’s probably right.”

“这让我感到惊讶，来自一位热心的女权主义者。为什么当父亲应该提高领导能力？”

“That surprises me, coming from an ardent feminist. Why should fatherhood increase leadership ability?”

“这很简单。这是功率转换的问题。”

“That’s easy. It’s a matter of power conversion.”

“能量转换？”

“Power conversion?”

“是的，你知道。将一种形式的力量转化为另一种你更看重的力量的能力。就像将溪流中的水能转化为电能来照亮你的房子。”

“Yes, you know. The ability to convert one form of power into another that you value more. Like converting water power from a stream into electric power to light your house.”

“这与已婚男人成为更好的领导者有什么关系？”

“What does that have to do with married men being better leaders?”

“嗯，在这个国家，已婚男人比单身男人更有优势。他们对女性拥有权力，并将其转化为支持他们工作的服务。单身男人光是照顾好自己就有很多工作要做，所以他们处于劣势。”

“Well, in this country, married men have an advantage over single men. They have power over a woman, which they convert into services that support them in their work. Single men have much more work to do just taking care of themselves, so they are at a disadvantage.”

“是的，但是那些传统的已婚男人支持他们的妻子，不是吗？” 有赡养妻子的重担，不是吗？”

“Yes, but those traditional married men supporting their wives, don’t they?” have the burden of supporting their wives, don’t they?”

“这种负担通常比在公开市场上获得相同服务的成本要低得多。因此，已婚男人将一小部分金钱权力连同大部分传统的男性支配权力转化为时间和其他服务，以帮助他在事业上取得进步。”

“That burden is usually much less than the cost of obtaining the same services on the open market. So the married man converts a small part of his money power along with a large part of his traditional male dominance power into time and other services that help him advance in his career.”

“所以这就是你所说的权力转换的意思：你使用你以一种形式拥有的权力来获得你想要更多的另一种形式的权力。”

“So that’s what you mean by power conversion: You use power you have in one form to gain power in some other form you want more.”

“确切地。”

“Exactly.”

“很多男人会有不同的看法。他们会说，已婚妇女正在将她对男人的性权力转化为金钱权力——保证终生供养。”

“A lot of men would see it differently. They would say that the married woman is converting her sexual power over the man into money power—a guaranteed lifetime of support.”

“现在很难保证，”Edrie 纠正道，“但是，是的，有些女人也这么看。两个人同时使用权力并将其转化为他们都更想要的东西，这并不矛盾。”

“It’s hardly a guarantee these days,” corrected Edrie, “but, yes, some women see it that way, too. There’s no contradiction in both people using power at the same time and converting it into something they both want more.”

Edrie 的功率转换示例

Edrie’s examples of power conversion

我问埃德丽她是否可以给我其他她自己职业生涯中的权力转换的例子。

I asked Edrie if she could give me other examples of power conversion from her own career.

“当然，几十个。从我出生的那一刻起，我就把父母对我的爱转化为他们对我正确教养的支持，这帮助我成为了一名工程师。”

“Sure, dozens. From the moment I was born, I converted my parents’ love for me into their support for my proper upbringing, which helped me to become an engineer.”

“这没什么不对，是吗？”

“There’s nothing wrong with that, is there?”

“一点都不。我并没有说电源转换有什么问题，尽管有些转换是不赞成的。”

“No, not at all. I didn’t say there was anything wrong with power conversion, though some conversions are looked on with disapproval.”

“像男性权力转化为金钱权力？”

“Like male power into money power?”

“有些人不同意，是的。但更不赞成用性权力来换取公司中的职位权力。这就是为什么关于女工程师与老板睡觉的谣言如此有害的原因。社会普遍不赞成这种特殊的权力转换。”

“Some people disapprove of that, yes. But even more disapprove of trading sexual power, say, for positional power in a company. That’s why rumors about women engineers sleeping with their bosses are so harmful. The society in general disapproves of that particular power conversion.”

“你受过这样的谣言吗？”

“Did you suffer from rumors like that?”

“据我所知，但其他人知道。我的事业稳步上升。”

“Not that I know of, but others have. My career has progressed steadily upward.”

“你很幸运。”

“You’ve been lucky.”

“与其说幸运不如善于将我拥有的力量转化为更有用的形式。我的意思是我很幸运，生来聪明，我把它转化为奖学金——金钱的力量。最近，我做了逆向转换——金钱的力量回到了脑力。”

“Not so much lucky as adept at converting what power I had into more useful forms. I mean I was lucky to be born bright, which I converted into scholarships—money power. More recently, I’ve done the reverse conversion—money power back to brain power.”

Edrie 解释说，当她参加我们的解决问题领导力研讨会时，她的经理拒绝支付她的学费或给她请假。她告诉他她会为自己支付费用并利用她的假期。她的经理知道如果她自己付钱，他的经理会发现，他会被叫来解释。他真的没有什么理由不付钱，而且公司的官方政策鼓励参加像PSL这样的课程，所以他付了钱。她利用公司等级制度的力量迫使她的经理付钱。

Edrie explained that when she took our Problem-Solving Leadership Workshop, her manager had refused to pay her tuition or give her time off. She told him she’d pay for herself and use her vacation. Her manager knew that his manager would find out if she paid her own way, and that he would be called in to explain. He really didn’t have any good reason for not paying, and the official company policy encourages attendance at courses like PSL, so he paid. She used the power of the company hierarchy to force her manager into paying.

“一路走好！” 我说。

“Nice going!” I said.

埃德里咯咯地笑了起来。“这很有趣，不是吗，我认识的每个人都非常欣赏这种特殊的功率转换。但如果我告诉他们，我的老板把我送到班级是为了奖励我和他上床……”

Edrie chuckled. “It’s funny, isn’t it, how everybody I tell admires that particular power conversion. But if I told them that my boss sent me to the class as a reward for sleeping with him …”

“我猜你必须非常了解当地文化才能玩这个游戏。”

“I guess you have to know the culture pretty well to play this game.”

“这并不总是那么冒险，但你必须知道你有什么权力。如果我现在想去工作坊，我只需在自己的凭证上签名即可。我可以将自己的职位权力转化为更多的技术能力，而无需任何人提问。但这里的很多人都可以做到这一点，但永远不会利用它。”

“It’s not always so risky, but you do have to know what power you have. If I want to go to a workshop now, I can simply sign my own voucher. I can convert my own position power into more technical competence for myself, without anyone asking questions. But lots of people here can do that and never take advantage of it.”

“也许他们拥有比技术能力更重要的东西。”

“Perhaps they have things they value more than the technical competence.”

“是的，他们中的很多人利用他们的消费能力去参加可能很有趣的愚蠢会议，并且可能会增强他们的重要性。但我个人认为他们是在将地位权力浪费在没有进一步转化价值的事情上。”

“Yes, a lot of them use their spending power to go to boondoggle meetings that may be fun, and may enhance their sense of importance. But I personally think they’re wasting their position power on something that has no further conversion value.”

收集点

Collecting points

“也许他们正在向高层管理人员购买积分。”

“Maybe they’re buying points with upper management.”

“哈！不要和我谈积分。当我第一次来这里工作时，我是他们的象征性女工程师。他们一直给我分配那些男人都不会做的不重要的任务。然后，当一项重要的新任务出现时，我的老板会告诉我，我没有任何在危急情况下工作的经验。当我抱怨我永远无法摆脱那个循环时，我的老板说我在积累积分。两年下来，我肯定有几百万积分，还不算利息。”

“Ha! Don’t talk to me about points. When I first came to work here, I was their token woman engineer. They kept giving me the unimportant assignments that none of the men would do. Then, when an important new assignment came along, my boss would tell me that I didn’t have any experience working in critical situations. When I complained that I could never get out of that loop, my boss said I was accumulating points. After two years of that, I must have had a few million points, not counting interest.”

“那你把它们变成了什么？”

“So what did you convert them into?”

“没有什么。积分不转换。至少，我从未听说过任何人将点数转换为有用的东西的经过验证的案例。分数只是当权者用来让他们下面的人做愚蠢事情的虚构。我知道。我浪费了两年时间收集积分。”

“Nothing. Points don’t convert. At least, I’ve never heard of an authenticated case of anyone converting points into anything useful. Points are just a fiction that people in power use to keep those below them doing stupid things. I know. I wasted two years collecting points.”

“嗯，如果你的积分都不能兑换，那除了一些无关紧要的任务，你是怎么得到的？”

“Well, if you couldn’t convert your points, how did you get anything besides unimportant assignments?”

“当我终于意识到自己是多么愚蠢时，我盘点了我必须转换的力量。我意识到，如果我一直在做一些重要的事情，我本可以威胁要辞职，让他们拿着包。我很确定我唯一的选择就是辞职并在另一家公司重新开始。”

“When I finally realized how dumb I’d been, I took an inventory of what power I had to convert. I realized that if I had been working on something crucial, I could have threatened to quit and leave them holding the bag. I was pretty sure my only course was to quit and start again at another company.”

“但我知道你没有放弃。发生了什么？”

“But I know you didn’t quit. What happened?”

“是我们的朋友阿特伍德给了我这个主意，就在这家自助餐厅里。我偷偷问了他离职时公司的积休工资政策，他晕了过去。事实证明，如果我退出，他会因为平权行动而惹上很多麻烦，这是我没有意识到的。所以想了想，我就去找老板说，如果我找不到更好的工作，我就辞职。”

“It was our friend Atwood who gave me the idea, right here in this cafeteria. I asked him confidentially about the company policy on pay for accumulated vacation when you resign, and he went into a tizzy. It turns out that he was going to get into a lot of trouble over affirmative action if I quit, something I hadn’t realized. So after thinking it over, I just went up to my boss and told him that if I didn’t get a better assignment, I was going to resign.”

“你明白了吗？”

“And you got it?”

“他试图告诉我当时没有可用的东西，但如果我有耐心，他肯定会在一两个月内得到一些东西。”

“He tried to tell me there was nothing available right then, but that if I was patient, he would be sure to have something in a month or two.”

“所以你等了？”

“So you waited?”

“你一定在开玩笑！一旦我知道我拥有所有的权力，我就坚持说，如果那天我没有得到它，我就会离开。然后他“想起”了一件事——我们最热门项目的设计工作。这是最好的功率转换。”

“You must be kidding! Once I knew that I had all the power, I just insisted that if I didn’t get it that day I was leaving. Then he ‘remembered’ something—a design job on our hottest project. That’s power conversion at its finest.”

“是的，但代价是什么？如果你搞砸了任务怎么办？”

“Yes, but at what cost? What if you had screwed up the assignment?”

“哦，当然，如果我做不到，那我一开始就不应该去那里。也许他们让我作为他们象征性的女工程师留在身边，但这不是我想留在身边的原因。我想成为一名称职的工程师，而不是一名女工程师。这种转变之所以奏效，是因为他们在玩那个女工程师游戏。”

“Oh, sure, if I couldn’t do it, then I shouldn’t have been there in the first place. Maybe they were keeping me around as their token woman engineer, but that’s not why I wanted to be kept around. I wanted to be known as a competent engineer, not a woman engineer. The conversion only worked because they were playing that woman engineer game.”

“就是那个试图让你远离 PSL 的老板吗？”

“Was that the same boss who tried to keep you out of PSL?”

“是的。”

“Yep.”

“好吧，我知道你不相信积分，但也许你的转化积累了一些负面积分？”

“Well, I know you don’t believe in points, but perhaps your conversion accumulated some negative points?”

“哦，我确实相信负分。”

“Oh, I do believe in negative points.”

“嗯，看来你跟你老板积攒了不少。”

“Well, it sounds like you accumulated quite a few with your boss.”

“真的。但是当我把我所有的技术能力都转换过来接他的工作时，它们都被取消了！”

“True. But then they were all canceled when I converted all my technical competence and took his job!”

使用电源

USING POWER

自从我遇到 Edrie 以来，每当我被要求帮助识别技术级别和文件中的潜在领导者时，我都会使用电源转换的概念。我首先寻找个人力量，它几乎可以转化为任何东西。接下来，我寻找能量转化的经验，可以转化为获取能量为自己所用，转化为获取能量为他人所用。这些东西需要很长时间才能学习，但当一个人加入任命的领导者行列时，就立即需要它们。它们很难教，有些明星永远学不会使用它们。

Ever since I met Edrie, I’ve used the concept of power conversion whenever I’m asked to help identify potential leaders among the technical rank and file. I first look for personal power, which can be converted into almost anything. Next, I look for power conversion experience, which can be translated from obtaining power for one’s own use to obtaining power for the use of others. These things take a long time to learn, but they are needed immediately when one joins the ranks of appointed leaders. They are hard to teach, and some stars never learn to use them.

当然，还有许多其他必要的品质，比如无私。研究埃德丽的故事，您可能会觉得她使用权力策略来推进自己的事业。这样的人可能不会用这种才能来帮助别人。艾德丽在成为队长后，确实会运用个人的权力和权力转换技能为队员获取资源，但并不是每个新任队长都会这样转变。

There are, of course, many other necessary attributes, like unselfishness. Studying Edrie’s tale, you may get the impression that she used her power tactics to advance her own career. Such a person might not use this talent to help others. Once Edrie became a team leader, she did apply her personal power and power conversion skills to obtain resources for her team members, but not every new team leader makes this switch.

一些新的团队领导只是继续使用他们的策略来获得他们需要的东西，而不是他们的团队成员需要的东西。有些人很愚蠢，有些人很自私，但大多数人还不了解领导者的角色，即创造一个人人都有权的环境。只有这样，他们才能约束自己的力量，并将他们的力量引向更高的目标。

Some new team leaders merely continue to use their tactics to obtain what they need, not what their team members need. Some are foolish, some are selfish, but most don’t yet understand the leader’s role, to create an environment in which everyone is empowered. Only in that way can they discipline and direct their power toward higher aims.

问题

QUESTIONS

I. 在你目前的环境中，你拥有多少种不同的力量？你在做什么将它们转换成更有用的形式？

I. How many different kinds of power do you hold in your present environment? What are you doing to convert them into more usable forms?

  1. 你要用它做什么？
  2. What are you going to use it for?
  3. 您当前的环境如何支持您努力完成的事情？您如何将其转换为更具支持性的方式？
  4. How does your present environment support the things you are trying to accomplish? How can you convert it into one that will be more supportive?
  5. 由于年龄、身高、性别、肤色、语言、宗教、吸引力、教育或个人习惯，你失去了多少力量？你能为这个做什么？
  6. How much power do you lose from your age, height, sex, skin color, language, religion, attractiveness, education, or personal habits? What can you do about it?
  7. 你和你的老板持多少分？你希望和他们一起买什么？你打算什么时候兑现？
  8. How many points do you hold with your boss? What do you expect to buy with them? When are you going to cash them in?

第 17 章问题解决团队的有效组织

Chapter 17. Effective Organization of Problem-Solving Teams

组织团队解决问题的最佳方式是什么？与其直接回答问题，我更喜欢使用练习通过模拟来探索问题。尽管以下练习模拟决策制定，但结果同样适用于团队承担的任何问题解决任务。在进一步阅读之前，您可能希望自己尝试练习。

What is the best way to organize a team for solving problems? Rather than answer the question directly, I prefer to use an exercise to explore the question through simulation. Although the following exercise simulates decision making, the results apply equally well to any problem-solving task undertaken by a team. You may wish to try the exercise yourself before reading further.

排名世界纪录

Ranking World Records

按照 1980 年吉尼斯世界纪录中所列的大小，对以下项目的测量值进行排序。使用整数 1 到 10，每个一次，对项目进行排名，最小的测量值排名 1，最大的测量值排名 10。最高的树

Rank the measurements of the following items by size, as listed in the 1980 Guinness Book of World Records. Use integers 1 through 10, once each, to rank the items, with the smallest measurement ranked 1 and the largest, 10. Tallest tree

最长的香蕉劈开

Longest banana split

最高的烟囱

Tallest chimney

最长的水母

Longest jellyfish

最高的喷泉

Tallest fountain

最大摩天轮（直径）

Largest Ferris wheel (diameter)

最高的移动式起重机

Tallest mobile crane

最长的飞盘投掷

Longest Frisbee throw

最高的水坝

Tallest dam

最长的酒吧（卖饮料）

Longest bar (for selling drinks)

当我们的研讨会使用此模拟时，会以多种方式做出相同的决定，因此我们可以比较团队可以用来解决问题的不同组织：单独、通过投票、任命强有力的领导者和协商一致。

When our workshops use this simulation, the same decision is made in several ways, so that we can compare different organizations that a team can use to solve problems: individually, by voting, with a strong appointed leader, and by consensus.

•个人：第一步是让团队中的每个成员单独对十个项目进行排名。这些个人排名为以后与各种团队排名的比较提供了一个基线。

• Individual: The first step is to have every member of a team rank the ten items, working alone. These individual rankings provide a base line for later comparison with the various team rankings.

•投票：团队中的个人完成后，他们无需讨论即可进行投票，将团队的知识集中在第二个排名中。不经讨论而投票是汇集信息以做出共同决定的最简单的可能方法。这是一种机械的方法，避免了个人力量差异等所有心理问题。

• Voting: Once the individuals on a team are finished, they take a vote, without discussion, to pool the team’s knowledge in a second ranking. Voting without discussion is the simplest possible method of pooling information to make a common decision. It is a mechanical method, avoiding all psychological issues like differences in personal power.

收集到选票后，每个团队都组织起来以小组为单位解决问题。我们为每个团队分配不同的组织形式。

After the votes have been collected, each team organizes itself to solve the problem as a group. We assign a different organizational form to each team.

•强有力的领导者：一种团队形式使用指定的领导者，其工作是私下听取每个团队成员的意见，并根据个人喜好做出最终的排名决定。（我们将这种形式标记为“强有力的领导者”。）

• Strong leader: One team form uses an appointed leader whose job is to listen to each team member’s opinions, privately, and make the final ranking decision according to personal preference. (We labeled this form “strong leader.”)

•共识：在共识形式中，团队中的每个人都必须完全同意团队的排名。

• Consensus: In the consensus form, everyone on the team must agree totally with the team’s ranking.

组织形式的范围

A SPECTRUM OF ORGANIZATIONAL FORMS

已经使用了许多其他形式，但这四种形式——单独工作、投票、强有力的领导者和共识——形成了一个很好的讨论范围。当允许团队自由选择组织时，他们通常会采用某种形式，可以将其分析为这些形式的组合。

Many other forms have been used, but these four—working individually, voting, strong leader, and consensus—form a good spectrum for discussion. When teams are allowed a free choice of organization, they generally adopt some form that can be analyzed as a combination of these forms.

最后，在团队以他们特定的方式对十个项目进行排名后，所有排名将按照 0（随机）到 100（完美）的等级进行评分。（本章末尾是正确的排名和评分程序，以备你想知道自己的表现如何。）

Finally, after the team finishes ranking the ten items in their particular manner, all rankings are scored on a scale of 0 (random) to 100 (perfect). (At the end of this chapter are the correct rankings and a scoring procedure, in case you want to find out how well you did.)

个人评分及投票

Individual scores and voting

个人得分为其他组织形式提供了比较标准。如果小组方法不能比个人单独工作做得更好，那么最好的小组方法显然是让成员单独工作。该练习旨在让没有人成为拥有完美知识的“专家”，但几乎每个人都会有一些部分知识可供分享。

The individual scores provide a standard of comparison for the other organizational forms. If the group method cannot do better than the individuals working alone, then the best group method would obviously be to have the members work alone. The exercise is designed so that nobody will be an “expert” with perfect knowledge, but almost everybody will have some partial knowledge available for sharing.

在投票中，来自每个参与者的部分信息流入“投票箱”，这是一台机械地列出决定的计算机。不允许讨论，因此这种方法衡量的是信息，而不是一个有说服力的成员对结果的影响。投票几乎总是会在团队中最好和最差的个人之间产生排名。如果我们检查成员得分的平均值，投票通常会使该平均值提高大约 10 分。

In the voting, partial information from each participant flows into the “ballot box,” a computer that tabulates the decision mechanically. No discussion is allowed, so this method measures information, rather than the influence of one persuasive member on the result. Voting almost invariably produces a ranking between the best and worst individual on the team. If we examine the average of the members’ scores, voting usually improves this average by about ten points.

在什么情况下投票会证明是一个好的组织选择？如果可预测的时间很重要，那么只要人们理解并接受投票程序，投票就是一种更好的方法。如果我们需要保证我们不会做出真正糟糕的决定，投票可能会有帮助，但为了获得这种保证，我们通常会牺牲获得更好决定的任何可能性。换句话说，投票可以确保不比平庸的决定更糟。

Under what circumstances would voting prove a good choice of organization? If predictable time is important, voting is a superior method, as long as people understand and accept the balloting procedure. Voting may be helpful if we need assurance that we won’t make a really poor decision, but to obtain this assurance, we will generally sacrifice any possibility of obtaining a superior decision. In other words, voting can be a way of ensuring no worse than a mediocre-plus decision.

例如，当满足以下一项或多项条件时，投票可能优于某种强有力的领导者方法：

Voting may be preferred, for instance, over some kind of strong leader method when one or more of the following are true:

• 在政治上，任命一名成员取代另一名成员并不是一个好主意

• politically, it wouldn’t be a good idea to appoint one member over another

• 我们可能无法事先知道谁是消息最灵通的人

• we may not know in advance who is the best-informed person

• 我们可能不知道谁会是最有效的领导者

• we may not know who would he the most effective leader

• 我们可能担心并怀疑可能影响公开讨论的联盟

• we may fear and suspect coalitions that could sway an open discussion

• 没有人愿意承担个人责任

• nobody is willing to take individual responsibility

• 让每个人都感受到决策的一部分很重要

• it is important to make everyone feel a part of the decision

投票是一种一致的方法。如果共识破裂，它通常比共识决定更有效。如果领导者消息灵通，或者当领导者消息灵通但不能或不愿使用其他团队成员的信息时，它优于强势领导者。另一方面，当团队工作得一般时，投票几乎肯定会产生比其他策略更糟糕的决定。

Voting is a consistent method. It generally works better than a consensus decision if the consensus breaks down. It is superior to a strong leader if that leader is poorly informed, or when the leader is moderately informed but unable or unwilling to use information from other team members. On the other hand, voting almost certainly produces a worse decision than other strategies when a team works even moderately well.

投票的另一个缺点是没有信息从一个成员流向另一个成员。在决策过程之后，人们与以前一样了解情况或了解情况。在某种程度上，决策过程应该对参与者有教育意义，投票失败了。

Another drawback of voting is that no information flows from one member to another. After the decision process, people are just as well or as poorly informed as before. To the extent that the decision process is supposed to be educational for the participants, voting fails.

坚强的领袖

The strong leader

强大的领导结构可能会或可能不会教给参与者比他们开始时知道的更多，这取决于领导者的风格。决策的质量还取决于领导者的风格和知识的结合。拒绝改变自己观点的领导者，如果他们是团队中知识最渊博的成员，可能会做得很好，但如果他们是知识最少的成员，则可能会做得很糟糕。有这样顽固的领导，我们看到团队分数低至5（当领导得分为3时）和高达95（当领导得分为90时）。

The strong leader structure may or may not teach the participants more than they knew when they started, depending on the leader’s style. The quality of the decision also depends on a combination of the leader’s style and knowledge. Leaders who resist changing their own opinion may do well if they are the most knowledgeable members of their team, but may do terribly if they are the least knowledgeable. With such stubborn leaders, we have seen team scores as low as 5 (when the leader’s score was 3) and as high as 95 (when the leader’s score was 90).

不那么顽固的领导者可能会受到团队成员信息的影响。他们通常会产生类似于共识分数的分数模式，始终高于投票分数。这样的领导者个人得分为 0，团队得分为 85，个人得分为 50 的领导者团队得分为 95。然而，在某些情况下，领导者允许自己受到影响，违背自己的判断. 我们曾经有一位个人得分为 88 分的领导者，他听取了一些知识较少的队友的意见，并得出了 57 分的团队得分。

Less stubborn leaders can be influenced by information from the team members. They typically produce a pattern of scores that resembles the consensus scores, consistently higher than the voting score. Such leaders can have a personal score of 0 yet produce a team score of 85, and leaders with a personal score of 50 can produce a team score of 95. In some cases, however, the leaders allow themselves to be influenced against their own judgment. We once had a leader with a personal score of 88 who listened to some less knowledgeable team- mates and produced a team score of 57.

共识

Consensus

我们的共识方法要求每个小组成员在每个项目成为小组决策的一部分之前同意每个项目的排名。对于没有共识决策经验的人来说，这种方法有时既费时又令人沮丧。然而，它对解决问题的领导者很有吸引力，因为它通常会产生高质量的决策。但是，要做到这一点，参与者必须遵循某些准则：

Our method of consensus requires that each group member agree with each item’s ranking before it becomes part of the group decision. For people not experienced at consensus decision making, this method can at times be both time-consuming and frustrating. It appeals to problem-solving leaders, however, because it typically produces high- quality decisions. For this to happen, though, participants have to follow certain guidelines:

• 请记住，并非每个排名都需要在每个细节上得到每个人的完全认可，但每个团队成员原则上都应该同意每个排名。

• Keep in mind that not every ranking need meet everyone’s complete approval in every detail, but that every team member should agree in principle with each ranking.

• 避免争论你自己的观点，仅仅因为它们是你自己的。相反，用逻辑和事实来支持你的每一个立场。

• Avoid arguing for your own opinions, just because they are your own. Instead, back up every position you take with logic and facts.

• 避免为了避免冲突而改变主意。鼓励他人为您提供事实和逻辑，您可以根据这些事实和逻辑改变观点。

• Avoid changing your mind only to avoid conflict. Encourage others to give you facts and logic on which you can base a change of opinion.

• 鼓励他人在改变主意之前使用事实和逻辑。

• Encourage others to use facts and logic before changing their minds.

• 避免使用旨在减少冲突的技术，例如投票、平均或交易选票。使用事实，无论它们看起来多么微不足道。

• Avoid techniques designed to reduce conflict, such as voting, averaging, or trading votes. Use facts, no matter how insignificant they may seem.

• 认为意见分歧是有帮助的，只要它们能得到事实或逻辑的支持。

• Consider differences of opinion as helpful, as long as they can be supported by fact or logic.

• 不要为了示好而隐瞒信息。

• Don’t withhold information just to be nice.
