They find all kinds of excuses for not submitting new combinations, but as they sit and support one another in sticking with all-Ys, the other teams invariably discover better combinations and pass them by.

被发现玩 all-Ys 是一种毁灭性的情感体验。结果，我们研讨会的毕业生形成了一个全球支持网络，反对成功带来的自满情绪。每当一名毕业生陷入一种做事方式时，无论多么成功，另一名毕业生都会打断他说：“你又在玩全 Y 的游戏！” 当然，许多人一生都可以通过采用保守策略来完美生存，但他们并不想成为解决问题的领导者。在这项业务中，您需要竭尽全力才能留在同一个地方。

It’s a devastating emotional experience to be caught playing all-Ys. As a result, graduates of our workshops formed a worldwide network of support against the complacency that comes with success. Whenever a graduate gets locked into one way of doing things, no matter how successful, another graduate interrupts to say, “You’re playing all-Y’s again!” Many people, of course, can survive perfectly well by playing the Conservative strategy all their lives, but they aren’t trying to be problem-solving leaders. In this business, it takes all the running you can do just to stay in the same place.

解决问题的领导力的悖论是你必须改变才能保持不变。很容易陷入构建类似于皮特随机数网络的支持系统的陷阱。不知不觉中，您会寻求那些会给您想要的答案的人的支持。最糟糕的是你对此毫无意识。在不知道自己在做什么的情况下，您会陷入一种固定的模式：要么拼命地抓住现有的东西，要么抓住每一个机会，只是为了改变而改变。

The paradox of problem-solving leadership is that you have to change in order to remain the same. It’s awfully easy to fall into the trap of building a support system that’s just like Pete’s Random Number Network. Unconsciously, you seek support from those people who will give you the answer you want to hear. The worst part about that is that you are unconscious about it. Without knowing what you are doing, you slip into a fixed pattern: either hanging on desperately to what you have, or changing at every opportunity just for the sake of change.

多年来，许多学生向我咨询有关预期的职业变化的建议。多年后，他们中的许多人告诉我，他们听从了我的建议，而且效果非常好。奇怪的是，在这种情况下，我总是像皮特的网络一样行事。我没有给出数字五，但不管他们怎么说，我总是说同样的话：“做你真正想做的事。”

Over the years, many students have asked me for advice about contemplated career changes. Many of them have told me, years later, that they followed my advice, and it worked out perfectly. The curious thing is that in such matters, I always act just like Pete’s network. I don’t give the digit five, but no matter what they say, I always say precisely the same words: “Do whatever you really want to do.”

黄金法则说，己所不欲，勿施于人。“做你真正想做的事”是我想要的建议，尽管它有时让我害怕。这不是保守派的建议，他们总是希望你做能让你保持不变的事情，但这也不是激进派的建议，他们总是希望你改变。相反，它是第三种也是最好的支持者的建议，我将其简单地称为朋友。

The Golden Rule says to do unto others as you would have them do unto you. “Do what you really want to do” is the advice I want, even though it sometimes frightens me. It’s not the advice of the Conservative, who always wants you to do what will keep you the same, but it’s not the advice of the Radical, either, who always wants you to change. Instead, it’s the advice of the third and best kind of supporter, whom I call, simply, a Friend.

问题

QUESTIONS

  1. 列出您个人支持系统中的所有人。想想你正在考虑的一些改变，并根据他们是否会支持你做出改变或保持不变来对所有人进行分类。如果您正在考虑不止一项更改，请对每项更改进行此分类。
  2. Make a list of all the people in your personal support system. Think of some change you are contemplating and classify all the people in terms of whether they will support you in making the change or in staying the same. If you are contemplating more than one change, do this classification for each.
  3. 使用您的支持系统中的人员列表，描述您正在做什么以使其保持良好的工作状态。它有什么不足的地方吗？您正在做什么来添加零件来弥补这些缺陷？
  4. Using the list of people in your support system, describe what you are doing to maintain it in good working condition. Are there any areas in which it is deficient? What are you doing to add parts to remedy those deficiencies?
  5. 去年，您的支持系统发生了怎样的变化？最近五年？明年会有怎样的变化？
  6. How has your support system changed in the last year? the last five years? How will it change in the next year?
  7. 如果您失去工作，请列出所有您可以寻求支持的人？每个人会给你什么样的支持？您想获得什么样的支持，但您的名单上没有人支持？
  8. Make a list of all the people you could go to for support if you lost your job? What kind of support would each one give you? What kind of support would you like to have, but for which there is nobody on your list?
  9. 对于您在新社区获得一份更好的新工作的情况，请执行与上一个练习相同的练习。
  10. Do the same as the previous exercise for the case where you were offered a new and better job, but in a new community.

结语

Epilogue

现在，我已经在胜利与和平中统治了大约五十年，我的臣民爱戴我，敌人惧怕我，盟友尊敬我。财富和荣誉，权力和享乐，都在等待着我的召唤，我的幸福似乎也不缺少任何尘世的祝福。在这种情况下，我认真地数了数落在我身上的纯真幸福的日子：共计十四天。哦人类，不要把你的信心寄托在这个世界上！—Abd-el-Raharn，（公元 912-961 年）

I have now reigned about fifty years in victory and peace, beloved by my subjects, dreaded by my enemies, and respected by my allies. Riches and honors, power and pleasure, have waited on my call, nor does any earthly blessing appear to be wanting for my felicity. In this situation, I have diligently numbered the days of pure and genuine happiness which have fallen to my lot: they amount to fourteen. O man, place not thy confidence in this present world!—Abd-el-Raharn, (912-961 A.D.)

关于成为解决问题的领导者，我已经把我知道的大部分都告诉了你，但我不能告诉你的一件事是你是否会喜欢它。不是每个人都喜欢当领导者，但很多人很快意识到他们不喜欢。到他们这样做的时候，他们通常已经失去了让他们回到原来状态的技能、态度或幻想。他们应该在采取行动之前审视自己的动机，但他们当然没有。

I’ve told you most of what I know about becoming a problem-solving leader, but the one thing I can’t tell you is whether you’re going to like it. Not everyone likes being a leader, but many are slow to realize that they don’t. By the time they do, they’ve usually lost the skills or attitudes or illusions that would let them move back to their old status. They should have examined their motives before they made their move, but of course they didn’t.

尽管几十年来我一直是领导者的顾问，但这些人对我来说仍然是个谜。为什么有智慧的人会为了组织他人生活的可疑乐趣而冒着失去幸福的风险？是不是领导并没有看上去那么开心？还是不那么聪明？毫无疑问，一千年后，有抱负和智慧的领导人会明白阿卜杜勒-拉哈姆不是在开玩笑，不是吗？

Although I’ve been a consultant to leaders for many decades, these people remain a complete mystery to me. Why would any intelligent human being risk losing happiness for the questionable pleasure of organizing other people’s lives? Is it that leaders are not as happy as they seem? or not as intelligent? Surely, after a thousand years, aspiring leaders with any intelligence would have learned that Abd-el-Raham wasn’t kidding, wouldn’t they?

如果我建议那些不听历史上伟大领袖的话的人，他们当然也不会听我的，如果我建议他们重新考虑成为领袖的整个想法。理性无法抹去非理性做出的决定，所以与其理性，让我再告诉你两个故事。这些故事是关于两位杰出的领导者——Rosy 和 Dave——他们帮助我了解了自己的动机。

People who won’t listen to the great leaders of history certainly won’t listen to me if I advise them to reconsider the whole idea of becoming a leader. Rationality can’t erase a decision that wasn’t arrived at rationally, so rather than be rational, let me tell you two more stories. These stories are about two remarkable leaders—Rosy and Dave—who helped me learn about my own motives.

罗西的回应

ROSY’S RESPONSE

我十七岁时在一家医院遇到了罗西。看到她的第一眼，我就知道为什么她被称为“Rosy”。手术后我躺在床上，麻醉剂使我昏昏沉沉，但对我是死是活感到非常好奇。一个遥远的，回荡的声音问，“你醒了吗？” 我不知道答案，我不确定我是否想知道。

I met Rosy in a hospital when I was seventeen. The first moment I saw her, I knew why she was called “Rosy.” I was lying in bed, after the operation, groggy from the anesthetic, but terribly curious about whether I was alive or dead. A distant, echoing voice asked, “Are you awake?” I didn’t know the answer, and I wasn’t sure I wanted to know.

这听起来像天使的声音，让我担心不已。然后一双温柔的手摇了摇我的肩膀。我的身体挣扎着想要入睡，但我必须知道。她真的是天使吗？我真的在天堂吗？

It sounded like an angel’s voice, which worried me no end. Then a pair of gentle hands shook my shoulders. My body struggled to return to sleep, but I had to know. Was she truly an angel? Was I really in heaven?

我睁开眼睛，看到她蓬松的珊瑚色头发像生锈的光环一样环绕在她的脸上。我死了，她是我的天使。

I opened my eyes and saw her fluffy coral hair encircling her face like a rusty halo. I had died, and she was my angel.

我很满足。我笑了。她回以微笑——并量了我的体温。温度计告诉我，我毕竟还活着，但我不在乎。我恋爱了，她会照顾我。

I was content. I smiled. She smiled back—and took my temperature. The thermometer informed me that I was alive after all, but I didn’t care. I was in love, and she would take care of me.

接下来的十天充满了痛苦、不适和尴尬，但我希望它们永远持续下去。我希望 Rosy 站在我的床边，为我的额头降温，握着我的手，为我注射吗啡。

The next ten days were filled with pain, discomfort, and embarrassment, but I wanted them to last forever. I wanted Rosy standing at my bedside, cooling my brow, holding my hand, injecting my morphine.

每天我都变得更快乐，也更相爱。第十天就寝时间，罗西端着一盘果子露和一颗安眠药来了。她看着我吃药，然后问了一个熟悉的问题：“你认为你需要再打一针止痛药吗？”

Every day I grew happier, and more in love. At bedtime on the tenth day, Rosy arrived with a dish of sherbet and a sleeping pill. She watched while I took the pill, then asked the familiar question: “Do you think you need another shot for pain?”

我给出了熟悉的回答，在我们短暂的恋情中，她第一次皱起眉头。“你真的需要吗？”

I gave the familiar answer, and for the first time in our short romance, her face wrinkled into a frown. “Do you really need it?”

“哦，是的，”我恳求道。“我非常需要它。”

“Oh yes,” I implored. “I need it very much.”

“那样的话，”她说，她那天使般的声音永远消失了，“你最好别再吃了。”

“In that case,” she said, her angelic voice forever lost, “you’d better not have any more.”

接下来的四天是无法估量的噩梦。我恳求道。我调侃道。我低声说。我喊道。我敲了敲墙。我尖叫。我要求。我求。我哭了。罗西仍然像天堂一样遥远。

The next four days were a nightmare of incalculable proportions. I pleaded. I teased. I whispered. I shouted. I pounded on the wall. I screamed. I demanded. I begged. I wept. Rosy remained as remote as the heavens.

在无情的四天里，我永恒的爱变成了彻头彻尾的恨，我抓住一切机会和途径表达这种恨。但在无情的四天里，她破解了我刚开始的吗啡成瘾。离开医院后，我再也不想见到罗西了。我从没干过。她使我摆脱了吗啡成瘾的生活，我将永远爱她。

In four ruthless days, my undying love turned to unmitigated hate, a hate that I took every opportunity and avenue to express. But in four ruthless days, she cracked my incipient morphine addiction. When I left the hospital, I never wanted to see Rosy again. I never did. She saved me from a life of morphine addiction, and I’ll always love her for it.

罗西不仅救了我。她教会了我一个原则，我称之为罗西的回应：

Rosy did more than save me. She taught me a principle that I’ve come to call Rosy’s Response:

如果你非常想要某样东西，也许你不应该拥有它。

If you want something that badly, perhaps you shouldn’t have it.

在 Rosy 回复我的整个生命中，当我正要做一些强迫症时，其他一些人有勇气向我提供 Rosy 的回应。不幸的是，我从来没有听过。如果我没有被绑在床上，身体的每个孔都插着一根管子，我也不会听 Rosy 的歌。

Throughout the life that Rosy returned to me, a few other people have had the courage to offer me Rosy’s Response just as I was about to do something obsessive. Unhappily for me, I’ve never listened. If I hadn’t been strapped into bed with a tube in every bodily aperture, I wouldn’t have listened to Rosy, either.

戴夫的偏差

DAVE’S DEVIATION

这就是 Rosy's Response 的问题。它只对不需要它的人或被绑在床上的人有效。痴迷的人不听。如果你要帮助他们避免伤害自己，你必须找到另一种方法：比如戴夫的偏差，它帮助我克服了成为经理的痴迷，在 23 岁时。

That’s the trouble with Rosy’s Response. It only works on people who don’t need it, or people who are strapped to the bed. Obsessed people don’t listen. If you’re going to help them avoid injuring themselves, you’ve got to find another approach: like Dave’s Deviation, which helped me conquer my obsession to become a manager at age 23.

我在 IBM 工作。计算机领域是一片广阔的天地，工作不到两年，我的起薪就翻了一番。我想我知道关于计算机的所有知识，而且我渴望征服新世界。环顾四周，我认为只有一种方法可以真正在 IBM 取得成功，那就是管理。

I was working for IBM. The field of computers was wide open, and I had doubled my starting salary in less than two years on the job. I figured I knew about all there was to know about computers, and I itched for new worlds to conquer. Looking around, I decided there was only one way to really get ahead in IBM, and that was management.

在我的半年度评估中，我向我的老板戴夫表达了我的渴望。戴夫是一名地区经理，在 IBM 晋升。在我眼里，他很酷，很强大，很有钱。我想和他一样，甚至更甚。

In my semiannual appraisal, I expressed my eagerness to Dave, my boss. Dave was a district manager who had risen through the IBM ranks. In my eyes, he was cool, powerful, and rich. I wanted to be just like him, only more so.

“你想在管理方面走多远？” 戴夫问。

“And just how far do you want to go in management?” Dave inquired.

“天空是极限！我打算成为 IBM 的总裁。”

“The sky’s the limit! I intend to be president of IBM.”

“你为什么要这么做？”

“And why do you want to do that?”

我犹豫了。为什么真的？“其实，我不知道为什么，但我知道我想要它，我不想再浪费时间摆弄这些东西了。那不是通往顶峰的道路。这是一条死胡同。”

I hesitated. Why indeed? “Actually, I don’t know why, but I know I want it, and I don’t want to waste any more time twiddling with bits. That’s not the way to the top. It’s a dead end.”

戴夫耐心地等着我说完。他知道打断那些痴迷的人是没有任何好处的。“你想让我为你做什么？”

Dave waited patiently for me to finish. He knew there was no percentage to be gained in interrupting the obsessed. “What do you want me to do for you?”

“我希望你能给我找一份管理工作。尽早！”

“I want you to find me a job in management. As soon as possible!”

“我会尽力做到这一点，”他说，“但前提是你已经为我做了些什么。”

“I’ll try to do that,” he said, “but only after you’ve done something for me.”

“那是什么？我会做任何事情。”

“What’s that? I’ll do anything.”

“你是个好作家。我要你坐下来给我写两份清单。第一个列表应该是您想成为经理的所有原因。第二个应该是您作为领导者拥有的所有资产和负债。当你把这些名单带给我时，我们会讨论如何让你开始管理。”

“You’re a good writer. I want you to sit down and write me two lists. The first list should be all the reasons you want to be a manager. The second should be all the assets and liabilities you have as a leader. When you bring me those lists, we’ll discuss how we can get you a start in management.”

回想起来，我现在明白了，如果 Dave 向我提供 Rosy 的回应，我会拒绝，就像我拒绝 Rosy 一样。Dave 非常重视我的技术贡献。他不想失去我，但他一定对我领导一个童子军窝的想法感到震惊，更不用说一个 IBM 员工团队了。戴夫没有把我绑在床上，我本可以离开去做任何其他工作，而且薪水可能更高。我什至可以找到一些愚蠢到足以给我升职的经理。

Looking back, I understand now if Dave had offered me Rosy’s Response, I would have resisted, just as I resisted Rosy. Dave genuinely valued my technical contributions. He didn’t want to lose me, but he must have been appalled at the idea of me leading even a Cub Scout den, let alone a team of IBM employees. Dave didn’t have me strapped to the bed, and I could have left for any number of other jobs, probably at higher pay. I could even have found some manager stupid enough to give me the promotion I thought I wanted.

列出资产和负债

LISTING ASSETS AND LIABILITIES

戴夫的转移产生了正确的效果。我没有反抗，而是冲回办公室开始乱写笔记。我从我的理由开始：尊重、权力、金钱。一个好的开始，所以我转向了我的资产和负债。

Dave’s diversion had the right effect. Instead of resisting, I rushed back to my office and started scribbling notes. I started with my reasons: respect, power, money. A good start, so I turned to my assets and liabilities.

我的资产主要是技术性的：我很快就能掌握复杂的想法。我可以写出人们能看懂的英语。我可以编写有效的计算机程序。

My assets were mostly technical: I was quick to master complex ideas. I could write English that people could understand. I could compose computer programs that worked.

在将我的责任付诸纸面之前，我犹豫了很久。当然，我知道它们是什么，但我不想让其他人知道。一方面，我还年轻，似乎没有人尊重我。另一方面，我似乎无法让任何人按照我的方式做事，即使我的想法很棒。最后，我的个人生活对我的工作造成了很大的拖累，尤其是与被两个穿着尿布的孩子绑在家里的年轻妻子不断争吵。

I hesitated a long time before committing my liabilities to paper. Sure, I knew what they were, but I didn’t want other people to know. For one thing, I was young, and nobody seemed to respect me. For another, I couldn’t seem to get anyone to do things my way, even though my ideas were terrific. Finally, my personal life was a big drag on my work, especially the constant bickering with a young wife bound to the house by two children in diapers.

清楚地看到我的负债让我意识到我看起来不是进入管理层的好选择。如果戴夫按原样阅读这份清单，我的经理生涯就会胎死腹中。也许我可以通过巧妙地重写列表来掩盖我的弱点。

Seeing my liabilities in black and white made me realize that I didn’t look like a good bet to move into management. If Dave read this list as it was, my career as a manager would be stillborn. Perhaps I could conceal my weaknesses by cleverly rewriting the list.

当我进行重写时，我想到将我的弱点与我的其他列表（原因列表）联系起来。我想出了以下内容：

As I worked on this rewrite, it occurred to me to relate my weaknesses to my other list, the list of reasons. I came up with the following:

  1. 我想要经理应有的尊重，否则没有人会尊重如此年轻和浮躁的人。
  2. I want the respect due a manager because otherwise nobody would respect someone so young and impetuous.
  3. 我想要经理的权力，因为除了从权威职位上命令他们，我不知道还有什么其他方法可以让人们做事。
  4. I want the power of a manager because I don’t know any other way to get people to do things than by ordering them from a position of authority.
  5. 我想要钱，因为我可以让我的个人生活井井有条——雇一个保姆，买第二辆车，买房子。
  6. I want money because I can then get my personal life in order—hire a sitter, get a second car, buy a house.

终于让我厚厚的头骨裂开的是第三个项目。当我回想起它时，一个内心的声音对我说：“如果你连自己的事情都不能管理，你凭什么认为你可以管理别人？”

It was the third item that finally cracked my thick skull. As I read it back to myself, an inner voice said to me, “If you can’t even manage your own affairs, what makes you think you can manage others?”

这个问题扼杀了我的痴迷。我回顾了其他项目，并意识到我对 Dave 问题的回答太糟糕了，无法提供。我不得不说，“戴夫，我希望你让我成为一名经理，因为我缺乏领导力的所有基本素质。最重要的是，我是如此失控，以至于我不知道我为什么要做我正在做的事情，也不知道它对其他人有什么影响。”

That question killed my obsession. I reviewed the other items and realized that my answer to Dave’s questions was too devastating to deliver. I would have to say, “Dave, I want you to make me a manager because I lack all the essential qualities of leadership. Most of all, I’m so out of control that I don’t know why I’m doing what I’m doing, or what effect it has on other people.”

我从来没有给戴夫他的名单，而且出于某种原因，他也从不索要。以他自己的方式，戴夫比罗西对我的帮助更多。他一定有，因为当时我对他的愤怒比对她的愤怒还要大。她阻止了我伤害自己，但他阻止了我伤害别人。每个人都使用了在这种情况下唯一可行的方法。

I never gave Dave his lists, and for some reason, he never asked for them. In his own way, Dave had helped me more than Rosy had. He must have, because at the time, I was more furious with him than I had been with her. She had stopped me from hurting myself, but he had diverted me from hurting others. Each used the only method that would have worked under the circumstances.

治疗你的痴迷

TREATING YOUR OBSESSION

我发现如果不履行道德义务将 Rosy 和 Dave 传递给我的东西传递给我，就不可能完成这本书。从 Rosy 那里，我了解到幸福不是通过吗啡从外界获得的。从戴夫那里，我了解到领导力不是通过任命从外部获得的。被任命为领导者就像吸毒一样：它可能会让你经历一些开始的痛苦，但更有可能让你对你最需要的信息麻木不仁。

I find it impossible to finish this book without fulfilling a moral obligation to pass on what Rosy and Dave passed on to me. From Rosy, I learned that happiness doesn’t come from outside through morphine. From Dave, I learned that leadership doesn’t come from outside through appointment. Being appointed the leader is just like taking drugs: It may carry you through some pain of getting started, but it is more likely to deaden your senses to the very information you most need.

如果你无法像别人看待你那样看待自己，那么你将永远无法成为领导者——这是瘾君子做不到的。对领导力的幻想可能是毁灭性的，但对自己的幻想是最糟糕的上瘾形式。作为一个作家，我可以揭露你对领导力的一些幻想，但只有你才能化解你对自己的幻想。我能做的最好的事情就是告诉你什么有时对我来说是成功的。

You’ll never be much of a leader if you lack the ability to see yourself as others see you—something no junkie can do. Illusions about leadership can be devastating, but illusions about myself are the worst form of addiction. As a writer, I can expose some of your illusions about leadership, but only you can dissolve your illusions about yourself. The best I can do is tell you what sometimes succeeds for me.

每当我对带头的想法很着迷时，我要做的第一件事就是注意到我很着迷。我可能会在会议上说些聪明的话，或者向人们提供改变他们生活轨迹的建议。这可能是一件很棒的事情，也可能很糟糕。重要的是我想到这样做时的感受，而我对吗啡的体验帮助我从内心认识到一种痴迷。

Whenever I feel obsessed with the idea of taking the lead, the first thing I have to do is notice that I am obsessed. I might be about to say something clever in a meeting, or offer people advice on altering the course of their lives. It might be a wonderful thing to do, or it might be awful. What matters is how I feel as I think of doing it, and my experience with morphine helps me to recognize an obsession from the inside.

为自己争取了片刻的自制力，在说或做可能会后悔的事情之前，我问自己三个问题：

Having bought myself a moment of self-control and before I say or do something I may regret, I ask myself three questions:

  1. 我为什么要这样做？
  2. Why do I want to do this?
  3. 我必须贡献哪些资产？
  4. What assets do I have to contribute?
  5. 我带来了什么责任？
  6. What liabilities do I bring?

当我问过这些问题时，这些问题对我很有用，我会向你推荐它们。所以你有权问我为什么要写这本书，我带来了什么资产和负债？

The questions have served me well, when I’ve asked them, and I recommend them to you. That’s why you have a right to ask me why I wanted to write this book, and what assets and liabilities did I bring?

资产和负债应该通过你对这本书的体验来说明，但只有我能说明我的动机。在很多时候，我都希望这本书能赚很多钱，让我看起来很聪明，吸引人们参加我的研讨会，产生咨询业务，或者迫使某人后悔他们不想和我一起工作。这不是世界上最崇高的动机清单，它们本身并不能真正证明我写它或你读它的努力是合理的。

The assets and liabilities should speak for themselves through your experience with the book, but only I can speak for my motives. At various times, I’ve hoped this book would earn a lot of money, make me look brilliant, induce people to attend my workshops, generate consulting business, or force somebody to regret they didn’t want to work with me. That’s not the world’s most noble list of motives, and by themselves wouldn’t really justify the effort for me to write it or for you to read it.

那我为什么要这么做？

So why did I do it?

我认为我写这本书是出于感激，感谢 Rosy 和 Dave 以及所有其他曾经领导过我的人。如果我将他们教给我的快乐传递给你，而你又将这种快乐传递给其他人，他们将得到最好的报酬。除此之外，还有什么真正重要的原因呢？

I think that I wrote this book out of gratitude, to Rosy and Dave and all the other people who have been my leaders. They would be best paid if I passed the happiness they taught me on to you, and if you, in turn, passed this happiness on to others. Besides that, what other reason really matters?

参考书目

Bibliography

我已经阅读了数百本有关领导力方面的书籍，但我所学到的关于领导力的大部分知识并非来自书本。书籍无法替代与人打交道的经验，所以既然您已经阅读了这本关于领导力的书，请在阅读更多之前出去与人互动。

I’ve read hundreds of books on aspects of leadership, yet most of what I’ve learned about leadership has not come from books. Books are no substitute for experience working with people, so now that you’ve read this book on leadership, go out and interact with people before you read any more.

当你准备好阅读更多关于领导力的书籍时，你可能想阅读我推荐的一些。

When you are ready to read more books on leadership, you may want to read some I recommend.

你接下来应该阅读哪本书很难说，因为关于技术领导者必不可少的主题的书籍太多了，但以下参考书目包含我们研讨会毕业生认为有用的书籍。我已经对每个列表进行了注释，以便您了解自己正在进入的内容。他们都不会浪费你的时间。

What specific book you should read next is difficult to say because there are so many books on subjects essential to the technical leader, but the following bibliography consists of books that our workshop graduates have found useful. I’ve annotated each listing to give you some idea of what you’re getting into. None of them will waste your time.

Bolman、Lee G. 和 Terrence E. Deal。

Bolman, Lee G., and Terrence E. Deal.

理解和管理组织的现代方法。旧金山：Jossey-Bass，1984 年。

Modern Approaches to Understanding and Managing Organizations. San Francisco: Jossey-Bass, 1984.

如果您想追求领导力的组织方面，请从 Bolman 和 Deal 清晰的文字开始。他们调查了使组织运作的重要理论模型，将每个模型都视为图片的一部分。他们实现了四种主要组织模式的综合，然而，没有一种模式充分处理了创新的作用。

If you wish to pursue the organizational side of leadership, start with Bolman and Deal’s clearly written text. They survey the important theoretical models of what makes organizations tick, putting each into perspective as only part of the picture. They achieve a synthesis of four major organizational models, none of which, however, adequately treats the role of innovation.

博尔顿，罗伯特。

Bolton, Robert.

人际交往能力：如何维护自己、倾听他人和解决冲突。第一试金石版。纽约：西蒙和舒斯特出版社，1986 年。

People Skills: How to Assert Yourself, Listen to Others, and Resolve Conflicts. 1st Touchstone ed. New York: Simon & Schuster, 1986.

如果您缺乏人际交往能力，其他领导素质将被否定。每个人，无论领导者多么熟练，都可以从这种对基本原理的脚踏实地的回顾中受益。

Other leadership qualities will be negated if you lack people skills. Every person, no matter how skilled a leader, could benefit from this down- to-earth review of the fundamentals.

布兰登，纳撒尼尔。

Branden, Nathaniel.

自尊心理学：开创现代心理学新纪元的自我理解的革命性方法。32 周年纪念版。旧金山：Jossey-Bass，2001 年。

The Psychology of Self-Esteem: A Revolutionary Approach to Self-Understanding That Launched a New Era in Modern Psychology. 32nd anniversary ed. San Francisco: Jossey-Bass, 2001.

自尊是领导力的核心。布兰登是这个主题上最受欢迎的作家之一。

Self-esteem is at the heart of leadership. Branden is one of the most popular writers on this subject.

卡内基，戴尔。

Carnegie, Dale.

如何赢得朋友和影响他人。纽约：西蒙和舒斯特出版社，1982 年。

How to Win Friends and Influence People. New York: Simon & Schuster, 1982.

领导的一般原则在 75 年甚至 5000 年内都没有改变（尽管这部自助经典有一个修订的现代化版本）。如果你发现你不能容忍卡内基相当普通的规则，你可能还没有准备好成为相当普通人的领导者。

The general principles of leadership haven’t changed in seventy-five years, or even five thousand (though there is a revised, modernized edition of this self-help classic). If you find you cannot tolerate Carnegie’s rather ordinary rules, you’re probably not ready to be a leader of rather ordinary people.

多伊尔、迈克尔和大卫·施特劳斯。

Doyle, Michael, and David Straus.

如何让会议发挥作用！：新的交互方式。伯克利贸易 pbk。编辑。纽约：伯克利出版社，1993 年。

How to Make Meetings Work! : The New Interaction Method. Berkley trade pbk. ed. New York: Berkley Books, 1993.

Doyle 和 Straus 开发了用于组织和操作各种类型会议的“交互方法”。使用本书中清楚描述的这种方法，我的许多客户已经将他们的会议从最糟糕的时刻转变为最好的时刻。（对于专门的技术会议，另请参阅 Freedman 和 Weinberg。）

Doyle and Straus have developed the “interaction method” for organizing and operating meetings of all types. Using this method, clearly described in this book, dozens of my clients have converted their meetings from the worst of times to the best of times. (For specialized technical meetings, see also Freedman and Weinberg.)

Freedman、Daniel P. 和 Gerald M. Weinberg。

Freedman, Daniel P., and Gerald M. Weinberg.

演练、检查和技术审查手册：评估计划、项目和产品。第三版。纽约州纽约市：Dorset House Pub.，1990 年。

Handbook of Walkthroughs, Inspections, and Technical Reviews : Evaluating Programs, Projects, and Products. 3rd ed. New York, NY: Dorset House Pub., 1990.

许多技术会议采用对正在进行的工作进行严格审查的形式。技术审查可能是技术增长的源泉，也可能是巨大的焦虑和冲突的源泉，这取决于它们的领导方式。我们认为我们的手册及其问答形式是所有花时间参加审查会议的人的基本指南。（对于其他类型的会议，请参阅 Doyle 和 Straus。）

Many technical meetings take the form of critical reviews of work in progress. Technical reviews can be a source of either technical growth or great anxiety and conflict, depending on how they are led. We feel that our handbook, with its question and answer format, is an essential guide for all people who spend time in review meetings. (For other types of meetings, see Doyle and Straus.)

Gause、Donald C. 和 Gerald M. Weinberg。

Gause, Donald C., and Gerald M. Weinberg.

你的灯亮着吗？: 如何找出真正的问题所在。纽约州纽约市：Dorset House Pub.，1990 年。

Are Your Lights On? : How to Figure out What the Problem Really Is. New York, NY: Dorset House Pub., 1990.

如果您通常不确定下一步要做什么，这本关于问题定义的友好小书将对您有所帮助。它还教授技术领导力必不可少的思维方式。

This friendly little book on problem definition will help you if you are generally uncertain about where you want to go next. It also teaches the kind of thinking that is essential in technical leadership.

戈登，托马斯。

Gordon, Thomas.

Leader Effectiveness Training, LET：领导今天的业务走向明天的成熟技能。第一近地点编辑。纽约州纽约市：伯克利酒吧。集团，2001。

Leader Effectiveness Training, L.E.T. : Proven Skills for Leading Today’s Business into Tomorrow. 1st Perigee ed. New York, N.Y.: Berkley Pub. Group, 2001.

戈登 (Gordon) 是广受欢迎且很有帮助的《家长效能培训》(Parent Effectiveness Training) 的作者。戈登的“不输”方法将吸引那些想要跳出大游戏的技术领导者。

Gordon is the author of the tremendously popular and helpful Parent Effectiveness Training. Gordon’s “no-lose” approach will appeal to technical leaders who want to step out of the Big Game.

恶心，罗纳德。

Gross, Ronald.

终身学习者。纽约：西蒙和舒斯特出版社，1979 年。

The Lifelong Learner. New York: Simon and Schuster, 1979.

对于那些对自己的学习负责的人来说，这是一本必不可少的手册；它充满了自我更新的想法、建议和特定资源。

This is an essential handbook for those who take responsibility for their own learning; it is full of ideas, suggestions, and specific resources for self-renewal.

哈特，洛伊丝博兰。

Hart, Lois Borland.

向上！妇女与领导力。纽约：AMACOM，1980 年。

Moving Up! Women and Leadership. New York: AMACOM, 1980.

这本书的几乎所有内容对男人和女人一样有趣，这不是批评。本书的一大特色是大量的自我评估图表。

Almost all of this book would be just as interesting to men as to women, which is not a criticism. A special feature of this book is the great number of self-assessment charts.

荷兰人，埃德温·P。

Hollander, Edwin P.

领导力动态。纽约：自由出版社，1978 年。

Leadership Dynamics. New York: Free Press, 1978.

本书为有关领导力的理论和实验结果提供了一个很好的切入点。参考资料详尽但不显眼，因此您可以从想法开始，然后根据需要转到源代码。

This book offers a good entry point to the theoretical and experimental results about leadership. The references are thorough, but inconspicuous, so that you may start with ideas and move to sources if you wish.

约瑟夫维茨，娜塔莎。

Josefowitz, Natasha.

权力之路：从第一份工作到高级管理人员的女性指南。马萨诸塞州雷丁：Addison-Wesley，1980 年。

Paths to Power: A Woman’s Guide from First Job to Top Executive. Reading, Mass.: Addison-Wesley, 1980.

这本书从权力问题的角度描绘了一个女人的整个职业生涯。虽然它涵盖的不仅仅是领导力问题，但我的线人向我保证，这本书比哈特的书包含更多对女性领导者特别有用的信息。

This book plots a woman’s entire career in terms of power issues. Although it covers more than leadership issues, my informants assure me that this book has more information specifically useful to women leaders than, for example, Hart’s book.

肯尼迪，尤金。

Kennedy, Eugene.

关于成为辅导员：非专业辅导员和其他帮助者的基本指南。新的扩展和修订版。第三。编辑。纽约：十字路口酒吧。有限公司，2001 年。

On Becoming a Counselor : A Basic Guide for Nonprofessional Counselors and Other Helpers. New expanded and rev. 3rd. ed. New York: Crossroad Pub. Co., 2001.

被视为领导者的人经常发现自己扮演着寻求帮助的人的顾问角色。肯尼迪的书是针对那些不是专业顾问，但经常发现自己扮演这个角色并且至少想知道如何避免伤害的人。

People who are seen as leaders often find themselves in the role of counselors to people asking for help. Kennedy’s book is directed to those who are not professional counselors, but who often find them- selves in this role and at least want to know how to avoid doing harm.

奥什里，巴里。

Oshry, Barry.

观察系统：解开组织生活的奥秘。第二版。旧金山：Berrett-Koehler 出版社，2007 年。

Seeing Systems : Unlocking the Mysteries of Organizational Life. 2nd ed. San Francisco: Berrett-Koehler Publishers, 2007.

在了解组织中权力的系统方面时，巴里奥什里是无与伦比的。

When it comes to understanding the systems aspects of power in organizations, Barry Oshry has no equal.

NTL 应用行为科学研究所。

NTL Institute for Applied Behavioral Science.

人际关系培训读物。第 8 版。弗吉尼亚州亚历山大市：NTL 应用行为科学研究所，1999 年。

Reading Book for Human Relations Training. 8th ed. Alexandria, Va.: NTL Institute for Applied Behavioral Science, 1999.

我的许多车间毕业生都想更多地了解他们如何与他人互动。我经常建议他们参加 NTL 的人机交互实验室，这是他们从该实验室带回家的读物

Many of my workshop graduates want to learn more about how they interact with other people. I often recommend that they take NTL’s Human Interaction Laboratory, and this is the book of readings that they take home from that lab

普罗格夫，艾拉。

Progoff, Ira.

在期刊研讨会上：写作以获取潜意识的力量并激发创造力。第 1 版，（内部工作簿系列）。洛杉矶：JP Tarcher，1992 年。

At a Journal Workshop : Writing to Access the Power of the Unconscious and Evoke Creative Ability. 1st ed, (Inner Workbook Series). Los Angeles: J.P. Tarcher, 1992.

如果你想了解更多关于写日记的知识，这里有一本关于这个主题的书。

If you want to learn more about keeping a journal, here’s a whole book on the subject.

代表，保罗。

Reps, Paul.

禅肉，禅骨：禅与前禅著作集。Rutland, Vt.: Charles E. Tuttle Co., 1998。

Zen Flesh, Zen Bones : A Collection of Zen & Pre-Zen Writings. Rutland, Vt.: Charles E. Tuttle Co., 1998.

一些读者建议我的书应该命名为《禅与技术领导艺术》，但禅只是故事的一部分。即便如此，那些想将自己转变为技术领导者的人应该了解禅宗方法，而 Paul Reps 可能是第一个在西方普及禅宗的作者。本书主要是禅宗教学故事集。

Some readers have suggested that my book should have been titled Zen and the Art of Technical Leadership, but Zen is only part of the story. Even so, those who would transform themselves into technical leaders should be aware of the Zen approach, and Paul Reps was probably the first author to popularize Zen in the West. This book is primarily a collection of Zen teaching stories.

罗杰斯，卡尔。

Rogers, Carl.

卡尔·罗杰斯谈个人力量：内在力量及其革命性影响，跨大西洋出版物，1978 年

Carl Rogers on Personal Power: Inner Strength and Its Revolutionary Impact,Trans-Atlantic Publications, 1978

如果您对权力和领导力感兴趣，请在做任何其他事情之前阅读这本书。卡尔·罗杰斯 (Carl Rogers) 的其他书籍将帮助您走上有效领导之路，包括：

If you are interested in power and leadership, read this book before you do anything else. Other books by Carl Rogers that will help you on your path to effective leadership include these:

成为一个人：治疗师对心理治疗的看法，Constable，2004 年

On Becoming a Person: A Therapist’s View of Psychotherapy, Constable, 2004

一种存在方式。波士顿：Mariner Books，1995 年。

A Way of Being. Boston: Mariner Books, 1995.

罗素，伯特兰。

Russell, Bertrand.

幸福的征服。第 1 版，劳特利奇经典。伦敦 ; 纽约：Routledge，2006 年。（也可在多个站点免费在线获取）

The Conquest of Happiness. 1st ed, Routledge Classics. London ; New York: Routledge, 2006. (also available for free on-line at several sites)

不快乐的人不是领导者。诺贝尔奖得主、哲学家伯特兰·罗素解决了如何快乐这一古老问题，并取得了成功。

Unhappy people are not leaders. Nobel Prize-winning philosopher Bertrand Russell tackles the ancient question of how to be happy, and succeeds.

萨提亚，弗吉尼亚。

Satir, Virginia.

联合家庭治疗，第 3 版。加利福尼亚州帕洛阿尔托：科学与行为书籍，1983 年。

Conjoint Family Therapy, 3rd ed. Palo Alto, Calif.: Science and Behavior Books, 1983.

新造人。加州山景城：科学与行为书籍，1988 年。

The New Peoplemaking. Mountain View, Calif.: Science and Behavior Books, 1988.

自尊。加利福尼亚州米尔布雷：天体艺术，1975 年。

Self-Esteem. Millbrae, Calif.: Celestial Arts, 1975.

建立联系。加利福尼亚州米尔布雷：天体艺术，1976 年。

Making Contact. Millbrae, Calif.: Celestial Arts, 1976.

你的许多面孔：被爱的第一步。新版。纽约：天艺出版社，2009 年。

Your Many Faces : The First Step to Being Loved. New ed. New York: Celestial Arts, 2009.

显然，弗吉尼亚·萨丁 (Virginia Satin) 的作品对我影响很大，我首先通过 Peoplemaking 了解到她激进的生活方式，这是对她学习如何与他人互动的方法的一个很好的调查。联合家庭治疗更像是一本针对治疗师的综合性教科书，但就像她所有的书一样，它的写作没有学术上的矫饰。要更轻松地介绍对领导者重要的特定主题，请尝试她的一本或所有来自 Celestial Arts 的小书。

Obviously, I have been greatly influenced by the work of Virginia Satin I first became aware of her radical approach to life through Peoplemaking, which is a good survey of her approach to how we learn to interact with others. Conjoint Family Therapy is more of a comprehensive textbook aimed at therapists, but like all her books, it is written without academic pretension. For a lighter introduction to specific topics of importance to leaders, try one or all of her little books from Celestial Arts.

沙阿，伊德里斯。

Shah, Idries.

无与伦比的穆拉纳斯鲁丁的微妙之处，伦敦：八角出版社，1973 年。

The Subtleties of the Inimitable Mulla Nasrudin, London: Octagon Press, 1973.

在许多方面，我的领导和教学方法深受苏菲思想的影响。我相信任何渴望成为领导者的人都应该熟悉苏菲派的方法。大部分在英语中广为人知的关于苏菲派的内容都是伊德里斯·沙阿 (Idries Shah) 带给我们的。这只是他的苏菲教义故事集之一，但任何其他故事都可以作为起点。

In many ways, my approach to leadership and teaching has been deeply influenced by Sufi ideas. I believe that anyone who aspires to be a leader should be familiar with the Sufi approach. Most of what is popularly known in English about the Sufi has been brought to us by Idries Shah. This is but one of his collections of Sufi teaching stories, but any other will do as a starting point.

温伯格，杰拉尔德 M.

Weinberg, Gerald M.

了解专业程序员。纽约：多塞特宫，1988 年。

Understanding the Professional Programmer. New York: Dorset House, 1988.

在你前进到更大更好的事情之前，了解你从哪里来以及你现在在哪里会有所帮助。如果您有编程背景，那么前面的书应该会有所帮助。另一本书要读的是

Before you advance to bigger and better things, it helps to understand where you came from and where you are now. If you come from a programming background, the preceding book should help. Another book to read is

咨询的秘密：成功提供和获得建议的指南。纽约：多赛特出版社，1985 年。

The Secrets of Consulting: A Guide to Giving & Getting Advice Successfully. New York: Dorset House Publishing, 1985.

当我整理这本参考书目时，我意识到我长期以来一直在撰写有关解决问题的领导力的文章。尽管《成为技术领导者》是我第一本全面涵盖该主题的书，但其他书籍也阐述了解决问题的领导者的三个主要关注点。

As I assembled this bibliography, I realized that I have been writing about problem-solving leadership for a long time. Even though Becoming a Technical Leader is my first book to cover the subject as a whole, other books develop the three major concerns of problem-solving leaders.

你的灯亮着吗？, 与 Don Gause 讨论了理解问题的主题。

Are Your Lights On?, with Don Gause, addresses the subject of understanding the problem.

与 Daniel Freedman 合着的 Handbook of Walkthroughs, Inspections, and Technical Reviews涉及控制质量。完美软件和其他关于测试的错觉也是如此。纽约州纽约市：多塞特宫，2008 年。

The Handbook of Walkthroughs, Inspections, and Technical Reviews, with Daniel Freedman, deals with controlling the quality. So does Perfect Software and Other Illusions About Testing. New York, NY: Dorset House, 2008.

咨询的秘密：成功提供和获得建议的指南。针对第三个主要领域：管理思想流。它的副标题就是它的全部内容。我最近的电子书，软件是如何构建的，为什么软件会遇到麻烦，如何观察软件系统，以及对重大软件事件的响应也讨论了思维方式，可以远远超出软件范围的应用方式，并且基于我们的关于一般系统思考的书籍。

The Secrets of Consulting : A Guide to Giving & Getting Advice Successfully. is aimed at the third major area: managing the flow of ideas. Its subtitle is what it’s all about. My recent eBooks, How Software is Built, Why Software Gets In Trouble, How to Observe Software Systems, and Responding to Significant Software Events also address ways of thinking, ways that may be applied well beyond the bounds of software, and are based on our books on General Systems Thinking.

说到电子书，最后一个推荐。在过去的几年里，我一直在通过编写包含领导力课程的激动人心的虚构故事，通过年轻人努力成为领导者的故事来接近领导力教学。通过小说，我发现我可以展示这些课程，而不仅仅是讲述它们。阅读这些小说，作为领导者的您可以亲身体验这些正在成为领导者的人正在经历的事情。

And speaking of eBooks, one final recommendation. Over the past few years, I’ve been approaching the teaching about leadership by writing exciting fictional stories containing lessons on leadership, through tales of young people struggling to become leaders. Through fiction, I find I can show these lessons, not just telling them. Reading these novels, you the leader can vicariously experience what these leaders-in-becoming are experiencing.

我的网站http://www.geraldmweinberg.com包含我所有小说的列表以及示例章节的链接以帮助您从中选择。我认为您在学习有关领导力的一些重要知识的同时会喜欢我的小说。感谢您试一试。

My website http://www.geraldmweinberg.com contains a listing of all my novels as well as links to sample chapters to help you choose among them. I think you’ll enjoy my novels while you’re learning a few important things about leadership. Thanks for giving them a try.
